Title: Health and Care Act 2022
Date: 2024-09-18
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2022/31

## Health and Care Act 2022

      B e it enacted  by the Queen’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Health service in England: integration, collaboration and other changes

#### NHS England

##### NHS Commissioning Board renamed NHS England

1

1.1

The National Health Service Commissioning Board is renamed NHS England.

1.2

Schedule 1 contains consequential amendments.

##### Power to require commissioning of specialised services

2

2.1

Section 3B of the National Health Service Act 2006 (Secretary of State’s power
to require commissioning of services) is amended as follows.

2.2

For subsection (2) substitute—

2.2.2

A service or facility may be prescribed under subsection (1)(d) only if the
Secretary of State considers that it would be appropriate for NHS England to
arrange for the provision of that service or facility (whether by NHS England
making arrangements itself or by giving directions under section  13YB  or
making arrangements under section 65Z5).

2.3

In subsection (3), omit paragraph (d).

2.4

After subsection (4) insert—

2.4.4A

If the Secretary of State refuses a request by NHS England to revoke provision
made by regulations under subsection (1)(d) prescribing a service or facility,
the Secretary of State must explain why to NHS England.

##### Spending on mental health

3

3.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

3.2

After section 12E insert—

########### Expected mental health spending

3.2.12F

3.2.12F.1

The Secretary of State must, in respect of each financial year, publish and
lay before Parliament a document—

3.2.12F.1.a

stating, by comparison with the previous financial year—

3.2.12F.1.a.i

whether the Secretary of State expects there to be an increase in the amount
of expenditure incurred by NHS England and integrated care boards (taken
together) in relation to mental health, and

3.2.12F.1.a.ii

whether the Secretary of State expects there to be an increase in the
proportion of the expenditure incurred by NHS England and integrated care
boards (taken together) that relates to mental health, and

3.2.12F.1.b

explaining why.

3.2.12F.2

The Secretary of State must publish and lay the document before the financial
year to which it relates.

3.3

In section 13U (annual report), after subsection (2A) (inserted by section 34
of this Act) insert—

3.3.2B

The annual report must include—

3.3.2B.a

a statement of the amount of expenditure incurred by NHS England and
integrated care boards during the year (taken together) in relation to mental
health,

3.3.2B.b

a calculation of the proportion of the expenditure incurred by NHS England and
integrated care boards during the year (taken together) that relates to mental
health, and

3.3.2B.c

an explanation of the statement and calculation.

##### NHS England mandate: general

4

4.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

4.2

In section 13A (mandate)—

4.2.a

in subsection (1), omit “Before the start of each financial year,”;

4.2.b

in subsection (2), in paragraph (a), omit from “during that financial year” to
the end of that paragraph (but not the final “and”);

4.2.c

omit subsections (3) and (4);

4.2.d

in subsection (5), omit “in relation to the first financial year to which the
mandate relates”;

4.2.e

after subsection (6) insert—

4.2.e.6A

The Secretary of State may revise the mandate.

4.2.e.6B

If the Secretary of State revises the mandate, the Secretary of State must
publish and lay before Parliament the mandate as revised.

4.3

In section 13B (the mandate: supplementary provision)—

4.3.a

for the heading substitute  “Review of NHS England’s performance in
implementing the mandate” ;

4.3.b

omit subsections (2) to (5).

4.4

In section 13T (business plan)—

4.4.a

in subsection (3), omit “for the first financial year to which the plan
relates”;

4.4.b

after subsection (3) insert—

4.4.b.3A

The fact that the mandate is revised during the period to which a business
plan relates does not require NHS England to revise the plan.

4.5

In section 13U (annual report), in subsection (2), for paragraph (a)
substitute—

4.5.a

the extent to which, in that year, it met any objectives or requirements
specified in the mandate,

.

##### NHS England mandate: cancer outcome targets

5

5.1

Section 13A of the National Health Service Act 2006 (mandate) is amended in
accordance with subsection (2).

5.2

After subsection (2), insert the following new subsection—

5.2.2A

The objectives specified by the Secretary of State under subsection (2)(a) for
NHS England must include objectives relating to outcomes for cancer patients,
and those objectives are to be treated by NHS England as having priority over
any other objectives relating specifically to cancer.

##### Duties as to reducing inequalities

6

In section 13G of the National Health Service Act 2006 (NHS England’s duties
in relation to the reduction of inequalities)—

6.a

in paragraph (a), for “patients” substitute  “persons” ;

6.b

in paragraph (b), after “services” insert  “(including the outcomes described
in section 13E(3))” .

      section 13L;

##### NHS England: wider effect of decisions

8

After section 13N of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

######### Duty to have regard to wider effect of decisions

8.13NA

8.13NA.1

In making a decision about the exercise of its functions, NHS England must
have regard to all likely effects of the decision in relation to—

8.13NA.1.a

the health and well-being of the people of England;

8.13NA.1.b

the quality of services provided to individuals—

8.13NA.1.b.i

by relevant bodies, or

8.13NA.1.b.ii

in pursuance of arrangements made by relevant bodies,

for or in connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness,
as part of the health service in England;

8.13NA.1.c

efficiency and sustainability in relation to the use of resources by relevant
bodies for the purposes of the health service in England.

8.13NA.2

In subsection  (1) —

8.13NA.2.a

the reference to a decision does not include a reference to a decision about
the services to be provided to a particular individual for or in connection
with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness;

8.13NA.2.b

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the health and well-
being of the people of England includes a reference to its effects in relation
to inequalities between the people of England with respect to their health and
well-being;

8.13NA.2.c

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the quality of services
provided to individuals includes a reference to its effects in relation to
inequalities between individuals with respect to the benefits that they can
obtain from those services.

8.13NA.3

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS England must have regard to
guidance published by it under section  13NB .

8.13NA.4

In this section “ relevant bodies ” means—

8.13NA.4.a

NHS England,

8.13NA.4.b

integrated care boards,

8.13NA.4.c

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

8.13NA.4.d

NHS foundation trusts.

######### Guidance about discharge of duty

8.13NB

8.13NB.1

NHS England may publish guidance about the discharge of—

8.13NB.1.a

the duty imposed on it by section  13NA ;

8.13NB.1.b

the duty imposed on integrated care boards by section  14Z43 ;

8.13NB.1.c

the duty imposed on NHS trusts by section  26A ;

8.13NB.1.d

the duty imposed on NHS foundation trusts by section  63A .

8.13NB.2

NHS England must consult any persons NHS England considers it appropriate to
consult—

8.13NB.2.a

before first publishing guidance under this section, and

8.13NB.2.b

before publishing any revised guidance containing changes that are, in the
opinion of NHS England, significant.

##### NHS England: duties in relation to climate change etc

9

After section 13NB of the National Health Service Act 2006 (inserted by
section 8 of this Act) insert—

######### Duties as to climate change etc

9.13NC

9.13NC.1

NHS England must, in the exercise of its functions, have regard to the need
to—

9.13NC.1.a

contribute towards compliance with—

9.13NC.1.a.i

section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target), and

9.13NC.1.a.ii

section 5 of the Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets), and

9.13NC.1.b

adapt to any current or predicted impacts of climate change identified in the
most recent report under section 56 of the Climate Change Act 2008.

9.13NC.2

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS England must have regard to
guidance published by it under section  13ND .

######### Guidance about discharge of duty under section 

9.13ND

NHS England may publish guidance about the discharge of—

9.13ND.a

the duty imposed on it by section  13NC ;

9.13ND.b

the duty imposed on integrated care boards by section  14Z44 ;

9.13ND.c

the duty imposed on NHS trusts by section 26B;

9.13ND.d

the duty imposed on NHS foundation trusts by section 63B.

##### Public involvement: carers and representatives

10

In section 13Q of the National Health Service Act 2006 (public involvement and
consultation), in subsection (2), after “individuals to whom the services are
being or may be provided” insert  “, and their carers and representatives (if
any),” .

##### Information about inequalities

11

11.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

11.2

After section 13S insert—

########### Information about inequalities

11.2.13SA

11.2.13SA.1

NHS England must publish a statement setting out—

11.2.13SA.1.a

a description of the powers available to relevant NHS bodies to collect,
analyse and publish information relating to—

11.2.13SA.1.a.i

inequalities between persons with respect to their ability to access health
services;

11.2.13SA.1.a.ii

inequalities between persons with respect to the outcomes achieved for them by
the provision of health services (including the outcomes described in section
13E(3)); and

11.2.13SA.1.b

the views of NHS England about how those powers should be exercised in
connection with such information.

11.2.13SA.2

NHS England may from time to time publish a revised statement under subsection
(1).

11.2.13SA.3

In this section “ relevant NHS bodies ” means—

11.2.13SA.3.a

integrated care boards,

11.2.13SA.3.b

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

11.2.13SA.3.c

NHS foundation trusts.

11.3

In Schedule 4 (NHS trusts: constitution etc), in paragraph 12, after sub-
paragraph (1A) (inserted by Schedule 4 to this Act) insert—

11.3.1B

The annual report must, in particular, review the extent to which the NHS
trust has exercised its functions consistently with NHS England’s views set
out in the latest statement published under section 13SA(1) (views about how
functions relating to inequalities information should be exercised).

11.4

In Schedule 7 (constitution of public benefit corporations), in paragraph 26,
after sub-paragraph (1A) (inserted by Schedule 4 to this Act) insert—

11.4.1B

The reports must, in particular, review the extent to which the public benefit
corporation has exercised its functions consistently with NHS England’s views
set out in the latest statement published under section 13SA(1) (views about
how functions relating to inequalities information should be exercised).

##### Support and assistance by NHS England

12

After section 13Y of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

######### Assistance and support

########## Power of NHS England to provide assistance and support

12.13YA

12.13YA.1

NHS England may provide assistance or support to—

12.13YA.1.a

any person providing or proposing to provide services as part of the health
service;

12.13YA.1.b

any person, not within paragraph  (a) , exercising functions in relation to
the health service.

12.13YA.2

The assistance that may be provided under subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b)
includes making available the services of NHS England’s employees or any other
resources of NHS England.

12.13YA.3

The assistance that may be provided under subsection  (1)(a) , or that may be
provided under subsection  (1)(b)  to integrated care boards, also includes
financial assistance.

12.13YA.4

Assistance or support provided under this section may be provided on such
terms, including terms as to payment, as NHS England considers appropriate.

##### Exercise of functions relating to provision of services

13

13.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

13.2

After section 13YA (inserted by section 12 of this Act) insert—

########### Discharge of functions

############ Directions in respect of functions relating to provision of services

13.2.13YB

13.2.13YB.1

NHS England may by direction provide for any of its relevant functions to be
exercised by one or more integrated care boards.

13.2.13YB.2

In this section “ relevant function ” means—

13.2.13YB.2.a

any function of NHS England under section 3B(1) (commissioning functions);

13.2.13YB.2.b

any function of NHS England, not within paragraph  (a) , that relates to the
provision of—

13.2.13YB.2.b.i

primary medical services,

13.2.13YB.2.b.ii

primary dental services,

13.2.13YB.2.b.iii

primary ophthalmic services, or

13.2.13YB.2.b.iv

services that may be provided as pharmaceutical services, or as local
pharmaceutical services, under Part 7;

13.2.13YB.2.c

any function of NHS England by virtue of section  7A  or  7B  (exercise of
Secretary of State’s public health functions);

13.2.13YB.2.d

any other functions of NHS England so far as exercisable in connection with
any functions within paragraphs  (a)  to  (c) .

13.2.13YB.3

Regulations may—

13.2.13YB.3.a

provide that the power in subsection  (1)  does not apply, or applies only to
a prescribed extent, in relation to a prescribed function;

13.2.13YB.3.b

impose conditions on the exercise of the power.

13.2.13YB.4

A direction under subsection  (1)  may include provision prohibiting or
restricting the integrated care board from making delegation arrangements in
relation to a function that is exercisable by it by virtue of the direction.

13.2.13YB.5

In subsection  (4)  “ delegation arrangements ” means arrangements made by a
person for the exercise of a function by someone else.

13.2.13YB.6

NHS England may make payments to an integrated care board in respect of the
exercise by it of a function by virtue of a direction under subsection  (1) .

13.2.13YB.7

NHS England may give directions to an integrated care board as to the exercise
by it of any functions in pursuance of a direction under subsection  (1) .

13.2.13YB.8

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a direction under subsection
(1) , NHS England must publish it.

13.2.13YB.9

Any rights acquired, or liabilities (including liabilities in tort) incurred,
in respect of the exercise by an integrated care board of any function by
virtue of this section are enforceable by or against it (and no other person).

13.3

In section 73 (directions and regulations under Part 2), in subsection (1),
after paragraph (b) insert—

13.3.ba

section  13YB ,

.

##### Preparation of consolidated accounts for providers

14

Before section 66 of the National Health Service Act 2006 (and the italic
heading before it) insert—

######### Consolidated accounts

########## Consolidated accounts for NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

14.65Z4

14.65Z4.1

NHS England must, in respect of each financial year, prepare a set of accounts
that consolidates the annual accounts of—

14.65Z4.1.a

all NHS trusts established under section 25, and

14.65Z4.1.b

all NHS foundation trusts.

14.65Z4.2

The Secretary of State may give NHS England directions as to—

14.65Z4.2.a

the content and form of the consolidated accounts, and

14.65Z4.2.b

the methods and principles to be applied in preparing them.

14.65Z4.3

NHS England must, within such period as the Secretary of State may direct,
send a copy of the consolidated accounts to—

14.65Z4.3.a

the Secretary of State, and

14.65Z4.3.b

the Comptroller and Auditor General.

14.65Z4.4

The accounts must be accompanied by such reports or other information as the
Secretary of State may direct.

14.65Z4.5

The Comptroller and Auditor General must—

14.65Z4.5.a

examine, certify and report on the consolidated accounts, and

14.65Z4.5.b

send a copy of the report to the Secretary of State and NHS England.

14.65Z4.6

NHS England must lay before Parliament a copy of—

14.65Z4.6.a

the consolidated accounts, and

14.65Z4.6.b

the Comptroller and Auditor General’s report on them.

##### Funding for service integration

15

15.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

15.2

In section 223B (funding of NHS England)—

15.2.a

for subsection (6) substitute—

15.2.a.6

The Secretary of State may direct NHS England—

15.2.a.6.a

that an amount of the sums paid to it under this section in respect of a
financial year is to be used for purposes relating to service integration;

15.2.a.6.b

about the use by NHS England of that amount for those purposes.

;

15.2.b

in subsection (7)—

15.2.b.i

for “subsection (6)” substitute  “subsection (6)(a)” ;

15.2.b.ii

in paragraph (b), for “mandate” substitute  “direction” ;

15.2.c

after subsection (7) insert—

15.2.c.7A

The power under subsection  (6)(b)  includes power to give NHS England
directions about the exercise of any of its functions under or by virtue of
section 223GA (including directions requiring consultation with the Secretary
of State or other specified persons).

15.2.c.7B

The Secretary of State must publish any direction under subsection  (6) .

15.3

In section 223GA (expenditure on integration)—

15.3.a

for subsections (1) and (2) substitute—

15.3.a.1

Where the Secretary of State has given NHS England a direction under section
223B (6)(a)  about sums paid to it in respect of a financial year, NHS England
may direct an integrated care board that an amount (a “designated amount”) of
the sums paid to the board under section 223G in respect of that year is to be
used for purposes relating to service integration.

15.3.a.2

The designated amount—

15.3.a.2.a

is to be determined in such manner as NHS England considers appropriate, and

15.3.a.2.b

must be specified in the direction under subsection  (1) .

;

15.3.b

in subsection (6), for paragraph (a) (but not the “and” at the end)
substitute—

15.3.b.a

it may use the amount for any purposes relating to service integration,

;

15.3.c

omit subsection (7).

##### Payments in respect of quality

16

In section 223K of the National Health Service Act 2006, omit subsections (4)
and (5) (power of Secretary of State to make regulations about payments by NHS
England in respect of quality).

##### Secondments to NHS England

17

17.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

17.2

In section 272 (orders, regulations, rules and directions), in subsection (6)—

17.2.a

omit the “or” at the end of paragraph (b);

17.2.b

after paragraph (c) insert—

17.2.b.d

regulations under paragraph  9A(5)  of Schedule A1, or

.

17.3

In Schedule A1 (constitution of NHS England), after paragraph 9 insert—

17.3.9A

17.3.9A.1

NHS England may make arrangements for a person to be seconded to NHS England
to serve as a member of NHS England’s staff.

17.3.9A.2

A period of secondment to NHS England does not affect the continuity of a
person’s employment with the employer from whose service the person is
seconded.

17.3.9A.3

In paragraphs 9, 10, and 13 a reference to an employee of NHS England includes
a person seconded to NHS England.

17.3.9A.4

In paragraph 3(3) the reference to an employee of NHS England includes any of
the following seconded to NHS England—

17.3.9A.4.a

a person employed in the civil service of the State, or

17.3.9A.4.b

a person employed by—

17.3.9A.4.b.i

an integrated care board,

17.3.9A.4.b.ii

an NHS trust established under section 25,

17.3.9A.4.b.iii

an NHS foundation trust,

17.3.9A.4.b.iv

a Special Health Authority performing functions only or mainly in respect of
England,

17.3.9A.4.b.v

the Care Quality Commission,

17.3.9A.4.b.vi

the Health and Social Care Information Centre,

17.3.9A.4.b.vii

the Health Services Safety Investigations Body,

17.3.9A.4.b.viii

the Human Tissue Authority,

17.3.9A.4.b.ix

the Human Fertilisation and Embryology Authority, or

17.3.9A.4.b.x

NICE.

17.3.9A.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this paragraph so as to
provide that other references in this Act to an employee of NHS England
include persons, or persons of a prescribed description, seconded to NHS
England.

#### Integrated care boards

##### Role of integrated care boards

18

For section 1I of the National Health Service Act 2006 and the italic heading
before it substitute—

######### Role of integrated care boards in the health service in England

########## General functions of integrated care boards

18.1I

An integrated care board established under Chapter A3 of Part 2 has the
function of arranging for the provision of services for the purposes of the
health service in England in accordance with this Act.

##### Establishment of integrated care boards

19

19.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

19.2

In Part 2, after Chapter A2 insert—

########### Integrated care boards

############ “Establishment of integrated care boards (including by re-purposing clinical commissioning groups)

############# Duty to establish integrated care boards

19.2.14Z25

19.2.14Z25.1

NHS England must establish bodies called integrated care boards in accordance
with this Chapter.

19.2.14Z25.2

Each integrated care board is to be established by order made by NHS England
for an area within England.

19.2.14Z25.3

The area for which an integrated care board is established must not coincide
or overlap with the area of any other integrated care board.

19.2.14Z25.4

NHS England must ensure that, at all times on and after the appointed day, the
areas of integrated care boards together cover the whole of England.

19.2.14Z25.5

An order establishing an integrated care board must provide for the
constitution of the board, either by setting out the constitution or by making
provision by reference to a published document where it is set out.

19.2.14Z25.6

In Schedule 1B—

19.2.14Z25.6.a

Part 1 is about the constitution of an integrated care board (including its
area);

19.2.14Z25.6.b

Part 2 is about the status and powers of an integrated care board and its
accounts.

19.2.14Z25.7

Before varying or revoking an order under this section NHS England must
consult any integrated care board that it considers likely to be affected.

19.2.14Z25.8

NHS England must publish orders under this section.

19.2.14Z25.9

In this section “ the appointed day ” means a day appointed under this
subsection by regulations made by the Secretary of State.

############# Process for establishing initial integrated care boards

19.2.14Z26

19.2.14Z26.1

NHS England must publish a list of the initial areas for which integrated care
boards are to be established (each of which is referred to in this section as
an “ initial area ”).

19.2.14Z26.2

The relevant clinical commissioning group or groups for an initial area must
propose the constitution of the first integrated care board to be established
for that area.

19.2.14Z26.3

Before making a proposal under subsection  (2) , the relevant clinical
commissioning group or groups must consult any persons they consider it
appropriate to consult (and it is immaterial for this purpose whether the
consultation is carried out before or after this section comes into force).

19.2.14Z26.4

When establishing the first integrated care board under section  14Z25  for an
initial area, NHS England must give effect to any proposal under subsection
(2)  unless it considers that—

19.2.14Z26.4.a

the proposal is inappropriate, or

19.2.14Z26.4.b

the relevant clinical commissioning group or groups have not carried out an
appropriate consultation under subsection  (3) ,

and in that case NHS England must determine the terms of the constitution
itself.

19.2.14Z26.5

Nothing in this section—

19.2.14Z26.5.a

prevents NHS England from establishing the first integrated care board for an
initial area in a case where the relevant clinical commissioning group or
groups have failed within a reasonable period to make a proposal under
subsection  (2) , or

19.2.14Z26.5.b

limits the re-exercise of the power in section  14Z25 .

19.2.14Z26.6

NHS England may publish guidance for clinical commissioning groups about the
exercise of their functions under this section.

19.2.14Z26.7

A clinical commissioning group must have regard to guidance published under
this section.

19.2.14Z26.8

In this section “ the relevant clinical commissioning group or groups ” means—

19.2.14Z26.8.a

in relation to an area that coincides with the area of a clinical
commissioning group, that group;

19.2.14Z26.8.b

in relation to an area that includes the whole or part of the area of more
than one clinical commissioning group, those groups acting jointly.

############# Abolition of clinical commissioning groups

19.2.14Z27

19.2.14Z27.1

Any clinical commissioning group in existence immediately before the appointed
day is abolished at the beginning of that day.

19.2.14Z27.2

In this section “ the appointed day ” has the same meaning as in section
14Z25 .

############# Transfer schemes in connection with integrated care boards

19.2.14Z28

19.2.14Z28.1

NHS England may, in connection with the abolition of a clinical commissioning
group under section 14Z27, make a scheme for the transfer of the group’s
property, rights or liabilities to NHS England or an integrated care board.

19.2.14Z28.2

NHS England may, in connection with the establishment of an integrated care
board, make a scheme for the transfer of property, rights or liabilities to
the board from—

19.2.14Z28.2.a

NHS England,

19.2.14Z28.2.b

an NHS trust established under section 25,

19.2.14Z28.2.c

an NHS foundation trust, or

19.2.14Z28.2.d

a Special Health Authority established under section 28.

19.2.14Z28.3

NHS England may, in connection with the variation of the constitution of an
integrated care board or the abolition of an integrated care board, make a
scheme for the transfer of the board’s property, rights or liabilities to NHS
England or an integrated care board.

19.2.14Z28.4

The reference in subsection  (3)  to the variation of the constitution of an
integrated care board is to its variation by order under section 14Z25 or
under provision included in its constitution by virtue of paragraph 14 of
Schedule 1B.

19.2.14Z28.5

NHS England must exercise its powers under subsection (1) or (3) so as to
ensure that—

19.2.14Z28.5.a

on the abolition of a clinical commissioning group whose area coincides with
that of an integrated care board, all of the group’s property, rights and
liabilities (other than criminal liabilities) are transferred to that board;

19.2.14Z28.5.b

on the abolition of a clinical commissioning group whose area does not
coincide with that of an integrated care board, all of the group’s property,
rights and liabilities (other than criminal liabilities) are transferred to
one or more integrated care boards;

19.2.14Z28.5.c

on the abolition of an integrated care board, all of the board’s liabilities
(other than criminal liabilities) are transferred.

19.2.14Z28.6

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

19.2.14Z28.6.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

19.2.14Z28.6.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

19.2.14Z28.6.c

criminal liabilities.

19.2.14Z28.7

A transfer scheme may—

19.2.14Z28.7.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

19.2.14Z28.7.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by, on behalf of or
in relation to the transferor in respect of anything transferred;

19.2.14Z28.7.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

19.2.14Z28.7.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

19.2.14Z28.7.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

19.2.14Z28.7.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

19.2.14Z28.7.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

19.2.14Z28.8

A transfer scheme may provide—

19.2.14Z28.8.a

for modifications by agreement;

19.2.14Z28.8.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

19.2.14Z28.9

In subsection  (7)(f) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

19.2.14Z28.10

In this section—

19.2.14Z28.10.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

19.2.14Z28.10.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

############ Constitution: publication

############# Duty for integrated care board to publish constitution

19.2.14Z29

Each integrated care board must publish its constitution (as varied from time
to time by order under section  14Z25  or under provision included in its
constitution by virtue of paragraph  15  of Schedule 1B).

############ Conflicts of interest

############# Register of interests and management of conflicts of interests

19.2.14Z30

19.2.14Z30.1

Each integrated care board must maintain one or more registers of the
interests of—

19.2.14Z30.1.a

members of the board,

19.2.14Z30.1.b

members of its committees or sub-committees, and

19.2.14Z30.1.c

its employees.

19.2.14Z30.2

Each integrated care board must publish the registers maintained under
subsection  (1)  or make arrangements to ensure that members of the public
have access to the registers on request.

19.2.14Z30.3

Each integrated care board must make arrangements to ensure—

19.2.14Z30.3.a

that a person mentioned in subsection  (1)  declares any conflict or potential
conflict of interest that the person has in relation to a decision to be made
in the exercise of the commissioning functions of the integrated care board,

19.2.14Z30.3.b

that any such declaration is made as soon as practicable after the person
becomes aware of the conflict or potential conflict and, in any event, within
28 days of the person becoming aware, and

19.2.14Z30.3.c

that any such declaration is included in the registers maintained under
subsection  (1) .

19.2.14Z30.4

Each integrated care board must make arrangements for managing conflicts and
potential conflicts of interest in such a way as to ensure that they do not,
and do not appear to, affect the integrity of the board’s decision-making
processes.

19.2.14Z30.5

For the purposes of this section, the commissioning functions of an integrated
care board are the functions of the board in arranging for the provision of
services as part of the health service.

19.3

In section 272 (orders, regulations, rules and directions), in subsection (1),
before paragraph (a) insert—

19.3.za

section  14Z25 (2) ,

.

19.4

Schedule 2 inserts into the National Health Service Act 2006 a new Schedule 1B
(integrated care boards: constitution etc) and contains a consequential
amendment.

##### People for whom integrated care boards have responsibility

20

20.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

20.2

After section  14Z30  (inserted by section 19 of this Act) insert—

########### People for whom integrated care board has responsibility

############ People for whom integrated care board has responsibility

20.2.14Z31

20.2.14Z31.1

NHS England must from time to time publish rules for determining the group of
people for whom each integrated care board has core responsibility.

20.2.14Z31.2

The rules must ensure that the following are allocated to at least one group—

20.2.14Z31.2.a

everyone who is provided with NHS primary medical services, and

20.2.14Z31.2.b

everyone who is usually resident in England and is not provided with NHS
primary medical services.

20.2.14Z31.3

Regulations may create exceptions to subsection  (2)  in relation to people of
a prescribed description (which may include a description framed by reference
to the primary medical services with which the people are provided).

20.2.14Z31.4

References in this Act to the group of people for whom an integrated care
board has core responsibility are to be read in accordance with this section.

20.2.14Z31.5

In this section, “ NHS primary medical services ” means services provided by a
person, other than NHS England or an integrated care board, in pursuance of—

20.2.14Z31.5.a

a general medical services contract to provide primary medical services of a
prescribed description,

20.2.14Z31.5.b

arrangements under section 83(2) for the provision of primary medical services
of a prescribed description, or

20.2.14Z31.5.c

section 92 arrangements for the provision of primary medical services of a
prescribed description.

20.3

20.3.a

in subsection (1), after paragraph  (za)  (inserted by section 19 of this Act)
insert—

20.3.a.zb

section  14Z31 (1) ,

;

20.3.b

in subsection (6), after paragraph (zb) insert—

20.3.b.zba

regulations under section  14Z31 (3) ,

.

20.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

20.4.a

substitute the following section for section  14Z31  of the National Health
Service Act 2006 (as inserted by subsection  (2)  of this section)—

############# People for whom integrated care board has responsibility

20.4.a.14Z31

20.4.a.14Z31.1

References in this Act to the group of people for whom an integrated care
board has core responsibility are to the people who usually reside in its
area.

20.4.a.14Z31.2

Regulations may create exceptions to subsection  (1)  in relation to people of
a prescribed description.

,

20.4.b

repeal section 272(1) (zb)  of that Act (as inserted by subsection  (3)  of
this section), and

20.4.c
