#### Integrated care boards: functions

##### Commissioning hospital and other health services

21

For sections 3 and 3A of the National Health Service Act 2006 substitute—

######### Duties of integrated care boards as to commissioning certain health services

21.3

21.3.1

An integrated care board must arrange for the provision of the following to
such extent as it considers necessary to meet the reasonable requirements of
the people for whom it has responsibility—

21.3.1.a

hospital accommodation,

21.3.1.b

other accommodation for the purpose of any service provided under this Act,

21.3.1.c

medical services other than primary medical services (for primary medical
services, see Part 4),

21.3.1.d

dental services other than primary dental services (for primary dental
services, see Part 5),

21.3.1.e

ophthalmic services other than primary ophthalmic services (for primary
ophthalmic services, see Part 6),

21.3.1.f

nursing and ambulance services,

21.3.1.g

such other services or facilities for the care of pregnant women, women who
are breastfeeding and young children as the board considers are appropriate as
part of the health service,

21.3.1.h

such other services or facilities for palliative care as the board considers
are appropriate as part of the health service,

21.3.1.i

such other services or facilities for the prevention of illness, the care of
persons suffering from illness and the after-care of persons who have suffered
from illness as the board considers are appropriate as part of the health
service, and

21.3.1.j

such other services or facilities as are required for the diagnosis and
treatment of illness.

21.3.2

For the purposes of this section an integrated care board has responsibility
for—

21.3.2.a

the group of people for whom it has core responsibility (see section  14Z31 ),
and

21.3.2.b

such other people as may be prescribed (whether generally or in relation to a
prescribed service or facility).

21.3.3

The duty imposed on an integrated care board by subsection  (1)  to arrange
for the provision of services or facilities does not apply to the extent that—

21.3.3.a

NHS England has a duty to arrange for their provision;

21.3.3.b

another integrated care board has a duty to arrange for their provision by
virtue of subsection  (2)(b) .

21.3.4

In exercising its functions under this section, an integrated care board must
act consistently with—

21.3.4.a

the discharge by the Secretary of State and NHS England of their duty under
section 1(1) (duty to promote a comprehensive health service), and

21.3.4.b

the objectives and requirements for the time being specified in the mandate
published under section 13A.

######### Power of integrated care boards to commission certain health services

21.3A

21.3A.1

Each integrated care board may arrange for the provision of such services or
facilities as it considers appropriate for the purposes of the health service
that relate to securing improvement—

21.3A.1.a

in the physical and mental health of the people for whom it has
responsibility, or

21.3A.1.b

in the prevention, diagnosis and treatment of illness in those people.

21.3A.2

For the purposes of this section an integrated care board has responsibility
for—

21.3A.2.a

the group of people for whom it has core responsibility (see section  14Z31 ),
and

21.3A.2.b

such other people as may be prescribed (whether generally or in relation to a
prescribed service or facility).

21.3A.3

An integrated care board may not arrange for the provision of a service or
facility under subsection (1) if NHS England has a duty to arrange for its
provision by virtue of section 3B or 4.

21.3A.4

In exercising its functions under this section, an integrated care board must
act consistently with—

21.3A.4.a

the discharge by the Secretary of State and NHS England of their duty under
section 1(1) (duty to promote a comprehensive health service), and

21.3A.4.b

the objectives and requirements for the time being specified in the mandate
published under section 13A.

##### Commissioning primary care services etc

22

Schedule 3 confers functions on integrated care boards in relation to primary
care services and contains other amendments relating to primary care services.

##### Transfer schemes in connection with transfer of primary care functions

23

23.1

NHS England may, in connection with the amendments made by Schedule 3, make
one or more schemes for the transfer of its property, rights and liabilities
to an integrated care board.

23.2

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

23.2.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

23.2.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

23.2.c

criminal liabilities.

23.3

A transfer scheme may—

23.3.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

23.3.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by, on behalf of or
in relation to the transferor in respect of anything transferred;

23.3.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

23.3.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

23.3.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

23.3.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

23.3.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

23.4

A transfer scheme may provide—

23.4.a

for modifications by agreement;

23.4.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

23.5

In subsection  (3)(f) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

23.6

For the purposes of this section—

23.6.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

23.6.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

##### Commissioning arrangements: conferral of discretions

24

In section 12ZA of the National Health Service Act 2006 (commissioning
arrangements by NHS England and integrated care boards), after subsection (2)
insert—

24.2A

The arrangements may confer discretions on a person with whom they are made in
relation to anything to be provided under the arrangements.

##### General functions

25

25.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

25.2

After section  14Z31  (inserted by section 20 of this Act) insert—

########### General duties of integrated care boards

############ Duty to promote NHS Constitution

25.2.14Z32

25.2.14Z32.1

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions—

25.2.14Z32.1.a

act with a view to securing that health services are provided in a way which
promotes the NHS Constitution, and

25.2.14Z32.1.b

promote awareness of the NHS Constitution among patients, staff and members of
the public.

25.2.14Z32.2

In this section, “ patients ” and “ staff ” have the same meaning as in
Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the Health Act 2009 (see section 3(7) of that Act).

############ Duty as to effectiveness, efficiency etc

25.2.14Z33

Each integrated care board must exercise its functions effectively,
efficiently and economically.

############ Duty as to improvement in quality of services

25.2.14Z34

25.2.14Z34.1

Each integrated care board must exercise its functions with a view to securing
continuous improvement in the quality of services provided to individuals for
or in connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness.

25.2.14Z34.2

In discharging its duty under subsection  (1) , an integrated care board must,
in particular, act with a view to securing continuous improvement in the
outcomes that are achieved from the provision of the services.

25.2.14Z34.3

The outcomes relevant for the purposes of subsection  (2)  include, in
particular, outcomes which show—

25.2.14Z34.3.a

the effectiveness of the services,

25.2.14Z34.3.b

the safety of the services, and

25.2.14Z34.3.c

the quality of the experience undergone by patients.

############ Duties as to reducing inequalities

25.2.14Z35

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, have regard
to the need to—

25.2.14Z35.a

reduce inequalities between persons with respect to their ability to access
health services, and

25.2.14Z35.b

reduce inequalities between patients with respect to the outcomes achieved for
them by the provision of health services (including the outcomes described in
section  14Z34 (3) ).

############ Duty to promote involvement of each patient

25.2.14Z36

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, promote the
involvement of patients, and their carers and representatives (if any), in
decisions which relate to—

25.2.14Z36.a

the prevention or diagnosis of illness in the patients, or

25.2.14Z36.b

their care or treatment.

############ Duty as to patient choice

25.2.14Z37

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, act with a
view to enabling patients to make choices with respect to aspects of health
services provided to them.

############ Duty to obtain appropriate advice

25.2.14Z38

Each integrated care board must obtain advice appropriate for enabling it
effectively to discharge its functions from persons who (taken together) have
a broad range of professional expertise in—

25.2.14Z38.a

the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness, and

25.2.14Z38.b

the protection or improvement of public health.

############ Duty to promote innovation

25.2.14Z39

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, promote
innovation in the provision of health services (including innovation in the
arrangements made for their provision).

############ Duty in respect of research

25.2.14Z40

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, facilitate
or otherwise promote—

25.2.14Z40.a

research on matters relevant to the health service, and

25.2.14Z40.b

the use in the health service of evidence obtained from research.

############ Duty to promote education and training

25.2.14Z41

Each integrated care board must, in exercising its functions, have regard to
the need to promote education and training for the persons mentioned in
section 1F(1) so as to assist the Secretary of State and Health Education
England in the discharge of the duty under that section.

############ Duty to promote integration

25.2.14Z42

25.2.14Z42.1

Each integrated care board must exercise its functions with a view to securing
that health services are provided in an integrated way where it considers that
this would—

25.2.14Z42.1.a

improve the quality of those services (including the outcomes that are
achieved from their provision),

25.2.14Z42.1.b

reduce inequalities between persons with respect to their ability to access
those services, or

25.2.14Z42.1.c

reduce inequalities between persons with respect to the outcomes achieved for
them by the provision of those services.

25.2.14Z42.2

Each integrated care board must exercise its functions with a view to securing
that the provision of health services is integrated with the provision of
health-related services or social care services where it considers that this
would—

25.2.14Z42.2.a

improve the quality of the health services (including the outcomes that are
achieved from the provision of those services),

25.2.14Z42.2.b

reduce inequalities between persons with respect to their ability to access
those services, or

25.2.14Z42.2.c

reduce inequalities between persons with respect to the outcomes achieved for
them by the provision of those services.

25.2.14Z42.3

In this section—

      “ health-related services ” means services that may have an effect on
the health of individuals but are not health services or social care services;
“ social care services ” means services that are provided in pursuance of the
social services functions of local authorities (within the meaning of the
Local Authority Social Services Act 1970 or for the purposes of the Social
Services and Well-being (Wales) Act 2014).

25.2.14Z42.4

For the purposes of this section, the provision of housing accommodation is a
health-related service.

############ Duty to have regard to wider effect of decisions

25.2.14Z43

25.2.14Z43.1

In making a decision about the exercise of its functions, an integrated care
board must have regard to all likely effects of the decision in relation to—

25.2.14Z43.1.a

the health and well-being of the people of England;

25.2.14Z43.1.b

the quality of services provided to individuals—

25.2.14Z43.1.b.i

by relevant bodies, or

25.2.14Z43.1.b.ii

in pursuance of arrangements made by relevant bodies,

for or in connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness,
as part of the health service in England;

25.2.14Z43.1.c

efficiency and sustainability in relation to the use of resources by relevant
bodies for the purposes of the health service in England.

25.2.14Z43.2

In subsection  (1) —

25.2.14Z43.2.a

the reference to a decision does not include a reference to a decision about
the services to be provided to a particular individual for or in connection
with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness;

25.2.14Z43.2.b

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the health and well-
being of the people of England includes a reference to its effects in relation
to inequalities between the people of England with respect to their health and
well-being;

25.2.14Z43.2.c

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the quality of services
provided to individuals includes a reference to its effects in relation to
inequalities between individuals with respect to the benefits that they can
obtain from those services.

25.2.14Z43.3

In discharging the duty under this section, integrated care boards must have
regard to guidance published by NHS England under section 13NB.

25.2.14Z43.4

In this section “ relevant bodies ” means—

25.2.14Z43.4.a

NHS England,

25.2.14Z43.4.b

integrated care boards,

25.2.14Z43.4.c

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

25.2.14Z43.4.d

NHS foundation trusts.

############ Duties as to climate change etc

25.2.14Z44

25.2.14Z44.1

Each integrated care board must, in the exercise of its functions, have regard
to the need to—

25.2.14Z44.1.a

contribute towards compliance with—

25.2.14Z44.1.a.i

section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target), and

25.2.14Z44.1.a.ii

section 5 of the Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets), and

25.2.14Z44.1.b

adapt to any current or predicted impacts of climate change identified in the
most recent report under section 56 of the Climate Change Act 2008.

25.2.14Z44.2

In discharging the duty under this section, integrated care boards must have
regard to guidance published by NHS England under section 13ND.

########### Involvement of the public

############ Public involvement and consultation by integrated care boards

25.2.14Z45

25.2.14Z45.1

This section applies in relation to any health services which are, or are to
be, provided pursuant to arrangements made by an integrated care board in the
exercise of its functions (“commissioning arrangements”).

25.2.14Z45.2

The integrated care board must make arrangements to secure that individuals to
whom the services are being or may be provided, and their carers and
representatives (if any), are involved (whether by being consulted or provided
with information or in other ways)—

25.2.14Z45.2.a

in the planning of the commissioning arrangements by the integrated care
board,

25.2.14Z45.2.b

in the development and consideration of proposals by the integrated care board
for changes in the commissioning arrangements where the implementation of the
proposals would have an impact on—

25.2.14Z45.2.b.i

the manner in which the services are delivered to the individuals (at the
point when the service is received by them), or

25.2.14Z45.2.b.ii

the range of health services available to them, and

25.2.14Z45.2.c

in decisions of the integrated care board affecting the operation of the
commissioning arrangements where the implementation of the decisions would (if
made) have such an impact.

25.2.14Z45.3

This section does not require an integrated care board to make arrangements in
relation to matters to which a trust special administrator’s draft or final
report under section 65F or 65I relates before—

25.2.14Z45.3.a

in a case where the administrator’s report relates to an NHS trust, NHS
England and the Secretary of State have made their decisions under section
65K(1) and (2), or

25.2.14Z45.3.b

in a case where the administrator’s report relates to an NHS foundation trust,
the Secretary of State is satisfied as mentioned in section 65KB(1) or 65KD(1)
or makes a decision under section 65KD(9).

########### Joint exercise of functions with Local Health Boards

############ Joint exercise of functions with Local Health Boards

25.2.14Z46

25.2.14Z46.1

Regulations may provide for any prescribed functions of an integrated care
board to be exercised jointly with a Local Health Board.

25.2.14Z46.2

The regulations may permit or require any functions that are exercisable
jointly by an integrated care board and a Local Health Board by virtue of the
regulations to be exercised by a joint committee of those bodies.

25.2.14Z46.3

Arrangements made by virtue of this section do not affect the liability of an
integrated care board for the exercise of any of its functions.

########### Additional powers of integrated care boards

############ Raising additional income

25.2.14Z47

25.2.14Z47.1

An integrated care board has power to do anything specified in section
7(2)(a), (b) and (e) to (h) of the Health and Medicines Act 1988 (provision of
goods etc) for the purpose of making additional income available for improving
the health service.

25.2.14Z47.2

An integrated care board may exercise a power conferred by subsection  (1)
only to the extent that its exercise does not to any significant extent
interfere with the exercise by the board of its other functions.

############ Power to make grants

25.2.14Z48

25.2.14Z48.1

An integrated care board may make payments—

25.2.14Z48.1.a

by way of grant to any of its partner NHS trusts or NHS foundation trusts;

25.2.14Z48.1.b

by way of grant or loan to a voluntary organisation which provides or arranges
for the provision of services which are similar to the services in respect of
which the integrated care board has functions.

25.2.14Z48.2

The payments may be made subject to such terms as the integrated care board
considers appropriate.

25.2.14Z48.3

For the purposes of this Act an NHS trust or NHS foundation trust is a
“partner” of an integrated care board if the trust—

25.2.14Z48.3.a

provides services for the purposes of the health service within the integrated
care board’s area, and

25.2.14Z48.3.b

has the function, under the integrated care board’s constitution, of
participating in the nomination of members as a result of falling within a
description prescribed for the purposes paragraph  8(2)(a)  of Schedule 1B.

########### Experience of members

############ Duty to keep experience of members under review etc

25.2.14Z49

An integrated care board must—

25.2.14Z49.a

keep under review the skills, knowledge and experience that it considers
necessary for members of the board to possess (when taken together) in order
for the board effectively to carry out its functions, and

25.2.14Z49.b

if it considers that the board as constituted lacks the necessary skills,
knowledge and experience, take such steps as it considers necessary to address
or mitigate that shortcoming.

########### NHS England’s functions in relation to integrated care boards

############ Responsibility for payments to providers

25.2.14Z50

25.2.14Z50.1

NHS England may publish a document specifying—

25.2.14Z50.1.a

circumstances in which an integrated care board is liable to make a payment to
a person in respect of services provided by that person in pursuance of
arrangements made by another integrated care board in the discharge of
commissioning functions, and

25.2.14Z50.1.b

how the amount of any such payment is to be determined.

25.2.14Z50.2

An integrated care board is required to make payments in accordance with any
document published under subsection (1).

25.2.14Z50.3

Where an integrated care board is required to make a payment by virtue of
subsection (2), no other integrated care board is liable to make it.

25.2.14Z50.4

Accordingly, any obligation of another integrated care board to make the
payment ceases to have effect.

25.2.14Z50.5

Any sums payable by virtue of subsection (2) may be recovered summarily as a
civil debt (but this does not affect any other method of recovery).

25.2.14Z50.6

NHS England may publish guidance for integrated care boards for the purpose of
assisting them in understanding and applying any document published under
subsection (1).

25.2.14Z50.7

In this section “ commissioning functions ” means the functions of integrated
care boards in arranging for the provision of services as part of the health
service.

############ Guidance by NHS England

25.2.14Z51

25.2.14Z51.1

NHS England must publish guidance for integrated care boards on the discharge
of their functions.

25.2.14Z51.2

Each integrated care board must have regard to guidance under this section.

########### Forward planning and reports

############ Joint forward plans for integrated care board and its partners

25.2.14Z52

25.2.14Z52.1

Before the start of each financial year, an integrated care board and its
partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts must prepare a plan setting out
how they propose to exercise their functions in the next five years.

25.2.14Z52.2

The plan must, in particular—

25.2.14Z52.2.a

describe the health services for which the integrated care board proposes to
make arrangements in the exercise of its functions by virtue of this Act;

25.2.14Z52.2.b

explain how the integrated care board proposes to discharge its duties under—

25.2.14Z52.2.b.i

sections  14Z34  to  14Z45  (general duties of integrated care boards), and

25.2.14Z52.2.b.ii

sections 223GB to 223N (financial duties);

25.2.14Z52.2.c

set out any steps that the integrated care board proposes to take to implement
any joint local health and wellbeing strategy to which it is required to have
regard under section 116B(1) of the Local Government and Public Involvement in
Health Act 2007;

25.2.14Z52.2.d

set out any steps that the integrated care board proposes to take to address
the particular needs of children and young persons under the age of 25;

25.2.14Z52.2.e

set out any steps that the integrated care board proposes to take to address
the particular needs of victims of abuse (including domestic abuse and sexual
abuse, whether of children or adults).

25.2.14Z52.3

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must publish the plan.

25.2.14Z52.4

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must give a copy of the plan to—

25.2.14Z52.4.a

the integrated care partnership for the board’s area,

25.2.14Z52.4.b

each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board, and

25.2.14Z52.4.c

NHS England.

25.2.14Z52.5

NHS England may give a direction as to the date by which subsection  (4)  must
be complied with.

25.2.14Z52.6

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must have regard to the plan under subsection  (1) .

25.2.14Z52.7

In this Chapter “ relevant Health and Wellbeing Board ”, in relation to an
integrated care board (or an integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts
and NHS foundation trusts), means a Health and Wellbeing Board established by
a local authority whose area coincides with, or includes the whole or any part
of, the area of the integrated care board.

25.2.14Z52.8

In this Act “ financial year ”, in relation to an integrated care board,
means—

25.2.14Z52.8.a

the period beginning with the date on which the integrated care board is
established and ending with the 31 March following that date, and

25.2.14Z52.8.b

each successive period of twelve months.

############ Revision of forward plans

25.2.14Z53

25.2.14Z53.1

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
may revise a plan published under section  14Z52 .

25.2.14Z53.2

If the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts revise the plan in a way that they consider to be significant, section
14Z52 (3)  and  (4)  apply in relation to the revised plan as they applied in
relation to the original plan.

25.2.14Z53.3

If the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts revise the plan in any other way they must—

25.2.14Z53.3.a

publish a document setting out the changes, and

25.2.14Z53.3.b

give a copy of the document to—

25.2.14Z53.3.b.i

the integrated care partnership for the board’s area,

25.2.14Z53.3.b.ii

each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board, and

25.2.14Z53.3.b.iii

NHS England.

############ Consultation about forward plans

25.2.14Z54

25.2.14Z54.1

This section applies where an integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts
and NHS foundation trusts are—

25.2.14Z54.1.a

preparing a plan under section  14Z52 , or

25.2.14Z54.1.b

revising a plan under section  14Z53  in a way that they consider to be
significant.

25.2.14Z54.2

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must consult—

25.2.14Z54.2.a

the group of people for whom the integrated care board has core
responsibility, and

25.2.14Z54.2.b

any other persons they consider it appropriate to consult.

25.2.14Z54.3

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must involve each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board in preparing or revising
the plan.

25.2.14Z54.4

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must, in particular—

25.2.14Z54.4.a

give each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board a draft of the plan or (as the
case may be) the plan as revised, and

25.2.14Z54.4.b

consult each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board on whether the draft takes
proper account of each joint local health and wellbeing strategy published by
it which relates to the period (or any part of the period) to which the plan
relates.

25.2.14Z54.5

Where a Health and Wellbeing Board is consulted under subsection  (4)(b) —

25.2.14Z54.5.a

it must respond with its opinion on the matter mentioned there;

25.2.14Z54.5.b

it may also give that opinion to NHS England.

25.2.14Z54.6

Where a Health and Wellbeing Board gives its opinion to NHS England under
subsection  (5)(b)  it must inform the integrated care board and its partner
NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts that it has done so (unless it informed
them, in advance, that it was planning to do so).

25.2.14Z54.7

If an integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts revise or further revise a draft after it has been given to each
relevant Health and Wellbeing Board under subsection  (4) , subsections  (4)
and  (5)  apply in relation to the revised draft as they applied in relation
to the original draft.

25.2.14Z54.8

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must include in a plan published under section  14Z52 (3) —

25.2.14Z54.8.a

a summary of the views expressed by anyone consulted under subsection  (2) ,

25.2.14Z54.8.b

an explanation of how they took account of those views, and

25.2.14Z54.8.c

a statement of the final opinion of each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board
consulted in relation to the plan under subsection  (4) .

25.2.14Z54.9

In this section, “ joint local health and wellbeing strategy ” means a
strategy under section 116A of the Local Government and Public Involvement in
Health Act 2007.

############ Opinion of Health and Wellbeing Boards on forward plan

25.2.14Z55

25.2.14Z55.1

A relevant Health and Wellbeing Board—

25.2.14Z55.1.a

may give NHS England its opinion on whether a plan published by an integrated
care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts under section
14Z52 (3)  takes proper account of each joint local health and wellbeing
strategy published by the Health and Wellbeing Board which relates to the
period (or any part of the period) to which the plan relates, and

25.2.14Z55.1.b

if it does so, must give the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts
and NHS foundation trusts a copy of its opinion.

25.2.14Z55.2

In this section, “ joint local health and wellbeing strategy ” has the same
meaning as in section  14Z54 (9) .

############ Joint capital resource use plan for integrated care board and its partners

25.2.14Z56

25.2.14Z56.1

Before the start of each financial year, an integrated care board and its
partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts must prepare a plan setting out
their planned capital resource use.

25.2.14Z56.2

The plan must relate to such period as may be specified in a direction by the
Secretary of State.

25.2.14Z56.3

The Secretary of State must publish any direction under subsection  (2) .

25.2.14Z56.4

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must publish the plan.

25.2.14Z56.5

The integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must give a copy of the plan to—

25.2.14Z56.5.a

the integrated care partnership for the board’s area,

25.2.14Z56.5.b

each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board, and

25.2.14Z56.5.c

NHS England.

25.2.14Z56.6

NHS England may give a direction as to the date by which subsection  (5)  must
be complied with.

25.2.14Z56.7

NHS England may publish guidance about the discharge by an integrated care
board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts of their functions
under this section.

25.2.14Z56.8

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must have regard to any guidance published under subsection  (7) .

25.2.14Z56.9

NHS England may give directions, in relation to a financial year—

25.2.14Z56.9.a

specifying descriptions of resources which must, or must not, be treated as
capital resources for the purposes of this section;

25.2.14Z56.9.b

specifying uses of capital resources which must, or must not, be taken into
account for the purposes of this section.

25.2.14Z56.10

The reference in subsection  (1)  to the use of capital resources is a
reference to its expenditure, consumption or reduction in value.

############ Revision of joint capital resource use plans

25.2.14Z57

25.2.14Z57.1

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
may revise a plan published under section  14Z56 .

25.2.14Z57.2

If the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts revise the plan in a way that they consider to be significant, section
14Z56 (4)  and  (5)  apply in relation to the revised plan as they applied in
relation to the original plan.

25.2.14Z57.3

If the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts revise the plan in any other way, they must—

25.2.14Z57.3.a

publish a document setting out the changes, and

25.2.14Z57.3.b

give a copy of the document to—

25.2.14Z57.3.b.i

the integrated care partnership for the board’s area,

25.2.14Z57.3.b.ii

each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board, and

25.2.14Z57.3.b.iii

NHS England.

############ Annual report

25.2.14Z58

25.2.14Z58.1

An integrated care board must, in each financial year, prepare a report (an
“annual report”) on how it has discharged its functions in the previous
financial year.

25.2.14Z58.2

An annual report must, in particular—

25.2.14Z58.2.a

explain how the integrated care board has discharged its duties under sections
14Z34  to  14Z45  and  14Z49  (general duties of integrated care boards),

25.2.14Z58.2.b

review the extent to which the board has exercised its functions in accordance
with the plans published under—

      section  14Z52  (forward plan), and           section  14Z56  (capital
resource use plan),

25.2.14Z58.2.c

review the extent to which the board has exercised its functions consistently
with NHS England’s views set out in the latest statement published under
section 13SA(1) (views about how functions relating to inequalities
information should be exercised), and

25.2.14Z58.2.d

review any steps that the board has taken to implement any joint local health
and wellbeing strategy to which it was required to have regard under section
116B(1) of the Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007.

25.2.14Z58.3

In undertaking the review required by subsection  (2)(d) , an integrated care
board must consult each relevant Health and Wellbeing Board.

25.2.14Z58.4

An annual report must include—

25.2.14Z58.4.a

a statement of the amount of expenditure incurred by the integrated care board
during the financial year in relation to mental health,

25.2.14Z58.4.b

a calculation of the proportion of the expenditure incurred by the integrated
care board during the financial year that relates to mental health, and

25.2.14Z58.4.c

an explanation of the statement and calculation.

25.2.14Z58.5

NHS England may give directions to integrated care boards as to the form and
content of an annual report.

25.2.14Z58.6

An integrated care board must—

25.2.14Z58.6.a

give a copy of its annual report to NHS England before the date specified by
NHS England in a direction, and

25.2.14Z58.6.b

publish a copy of the annual report.

########### Performance assessment of integrated care boards

############ Performance assessment of integrated care boards

25.2.14Z59

25.2.14Z59.1

NHS England must conduct a performance assessment of each integrated care
board in respect of each financial year.

25.2.14Z59.2

A performance assessment is an assessment of how well the integrated care
board has discharged its functions during that year.

25.2.14Z59.3

The assessment must, in particular, include an assessment of how well the
integrated care board has discharged its duties under—

25.2.14Z59.3.a

section  14Z34  (improvement in quality of services),

25.2.14Z59.3.b

section  14Z35  (reducing inequalities),

25.2.14Z59.3.c

section  14Z38  (obtaining appropriate advice),

25.2.14Z59.3.d

section  14Z40  (duty in respect of research),

25.2.14Z59.3.e

section  14Z43  (duty to have regard to effect of decisions),

25.2.14Z59.3.f

section  14Z45  (public involvement and consultation),

25.2.14Z59.3.g

sections  223GB  to  223N  (financial duties), and

25.2.14Z59.3.h

section 116B(1) of the Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act
2007 (duty to have regard to assessments and strategies).

25.2.14Z59.4

In conducting a performance assessment, NHS England must consult each relevant
Health and Wellbeing Board as to its views on any steps that the board has
taken to implement any joint local health and wellbeing strategy to which the
board was required to have regard under section 116B(1) of that Act of 2007.

25.2.14Z59.5

In conducting a performance assessment, NHS England must, in particular, have
regard to—

25.2.14Z59.5.a

any guidance published by the Secretary of State for the purposes of this
section, and

25.2.14Z59.5.b

any guidance published under section  14Z51 .

25.2.14Z59.6

NHS England must publish a report in respect of each financial year containing
a summary of the results of each performance assessment conducted by NHS
England in respect of that year.

########### Power of NHS England to obtain information

############ Power of NHS England to obtain information

25.2.14Z60

25.2.14Z60.1

NHS England may require an integrated care board to provide NHS England with
information.

25.2.14Z60.2

The information must be provided in such form, and at such time or within such
period, as NHS England may require.

########### Intervention powers

############ Power to give directions to integrated care boards

25.2.14Z61

25.2.14Z61.1

This section applies if NHS England is satisfied that—

25.2.14Z61.1.a

an integrated care board is failing or has failed to discharge any of its
functions, or

25.2.14Z61.1.b

there is a significant risk that an integrated care board will fail to do so.

25.2.14Z61.2

NHS England may direct the integrated care board to discharge such of those
functions in such manner and within such period or periods as may be specified
in the direction.

25.2.14Z61.3

NHS England may direct—

25.2.14Z61.3.a

the integrated care board, or

25.2.14Z61.3.b

the chief executive of the integrated care board,

to cease to perform any functions for such period or periods as may be
specified in the direction.

25.2.14Z61.4

NHS England may—

25.2.14Z61.4.a

terminate the appointment of the integrated care board’s chief executive, and

25.2.14Z61.4.b

direct the chair of the board as to which individual to appoint as a
replacement and on what terms.

25.2.14Z61.5

Where a direction is given under subsection  (3)(a)  NHS England may—

25.2.14Z61.5.a

exercise, on behalf of the integrated care board, any of the functions that
are the subject of the direction;

25.2.14Z61.5.b

direct another integrated care board to perform any of those functions on
behalf of the integrated care board, in such manner and within such period or
periods as may be specified in the direction.

25.2.14Z61.6

A direction under subsection  (5)(b)  may include provision prohibiting or
restricting the integrated care board from making delegation arrangements in
relation to a function that is exercisable by it by virtue of the direction.

25.2.14Z61.7

In subsection  (6)  “ delegation arrangements ” means arrangements made by a
person for the exercise of a function by someone else.

25.2.14Z61.8

Where a direction is given under subsection  (3)(b)  NHS England may—

25.2.14Z61.8.a

exercise, on behalf of the chief executive, any of the functions that are the
subject of the direction;

25.2.14Z61.8.b

direct the chief executive of another integrated care board to perform any of
those functions on behalf of the chief executive, in such manner and within
such period or periods as may be specified in the direction.

25.2.14Z61.9

For the purposes of this section—

25.2.14Z61.9.a

a failure to discharge a function includes a failure to discharge it properly,
and

25.2.14Z61.9.b

a failure to discharge a function properly includes a failure to discharge it
consistently with what NHS England considers to be the interests of the health
service.

############ Section 

25.2.14Z62

25.2.14Z62.1

Before exercising the power conferred by section  14Z61 (5)(b)  or  (8)(b)
NHS England must consult the integrated care board to which it is proposing to
give the direction or to whose chief executive it is proposing to give the
direction.

25.2.14Z62.2

Where a direction is given under section  14Z61 (3)(b)  to the chief executive
of an integrated care board, that board must co-operate with any chief
executive to whom a direction is given under subsection  (8)(b) .

########### Disclosure of information

############ Permitted disclosures of information

25.2.14Z63

25.2.14Z63.1

An integrated care board may disclose information obtained by it in the
exercise of its functions if—

25.2.14Z63.1.a

the information has previously been lawfully disclosed to the public,

25.2.14Z63.1.b

the disclosure is made under or pursuant to regulations under section 113 or
114 of the Health and Social Care (Community Health and Standards) Act 2003
(complaints about health care or social services),

25.2.14Z63.1.c

the disclosure is made in accordance with any enactment or court order,

25.2.14Z63.1.d

the disclosure is necessary or expedient for the purposes of protecting the
welfare of any individual,

25.2.14Z63.1.e

the disclosure is made to any person in circumstances where it is necessary or
expedient for the person to have the information for the purpose of exercising
functions of that person under any enactment,

25.2.14Z63.1.f

the disclosure is made for the purpose of facilitating the exercise of any of
the integrated care board’s functions,

25.2.14Z63.1.g

the disclosure is made in connection with the investigation of a criminal
offence (whether or not in the United Kingdom), or

25.2.14Z63.1.h

the disclosure is made for the purpose of criminal proceedings (whether or not
in the United Kingdom).

25.2.14Z63.2

Subsection  (1)(a)  to  (c)  and  (h)  have effect notwithstanding any rule of
common law which would otherwise prohibit or restrict the disclosure.

########### Interpretation

############ Interpretation

25.2.14Z64

In this Chapter—

      “ the health service ” means the health service in England;           “
health services ” means services provided as part of the health service;
“ integrated care partnership ” has the meaning given by section  116ZA (1)
of the Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007;           “
relevant Health and Wellbeing Board ”, in relation to an integrated care
board, has the meaning given by section  14Z52 (7) .

25.3

In section 48 (power to obtain information from NHS foundation trust)—

25.3.a

after subsection (1) insert—

25.3.a.1A

An integrated care board may require any of its partner NHS foundation trusts
to provide it with any information that it requires.

;

25.3.b

for subsection (2) substitute—

25.3.b.2

Information required under this section must be provided in such form, and at
such time or within such period, as may be specified by the person imposing
the requirement.

25.4

In Schedule 4 (NHS trusts: constitution etc), in paragraph 13—

25.4.a

the existing provision becomes sub-paragraph (1);

25.4.b

after that sub-paragraph insert—

25.4.b.2

An integrated care board may require any of its partner NHS trusts to provide
it with any information that it requires.

25.4.b.3

Information required under sub-paragraph (2) must be provided in such form,
and at such time or within such period, as may be specified by the integrated
care board.

#### Integrated care partnerships

##### Integrated care partnerships and strategies

26

26.1

The Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007 is amended in
accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (6) .

26.2

In section 104 (interpretation: partner authorities), in subsection (2), for
paragraph (ja) substitute—

26.2.ja

an integrated care board;

.

26.3

In section 116 (health and social care: joint strategic needs assessments)—

26.3.a

in subsection (4), for paragraph (b) substitute—

26.3.a.b

each of its partner integrated care boards,

;

26.3.b

after subsection (5) insert—

26.3.b.5A

The responsible local authority must give a copy of each assessment of
relevant needs prepared under this section to any integrated care partnership
established under section 116ZA whose area coincides with or includes the
whole or part of the area of the responsible local authority.

;

26.3.c

in subsections (6) and (7), for “clinical commissioning group”, in each place
it occurs, substitute  “integrated care board” ;

26.3.d

in subsection (8), for “clinical commissioning groups” substitute  “integrated
care boards” ;

26.3.e

in subsections (8A) and (9), for “clinical commissioning group”, in each place
it occurs, substitute  “integrated care board” .

26.4

After section 116 insert—

########### Integrated care partnerships

26.4.116ZA

26.4.116ZA.1

An integrated care board and each responsible local authority whose area
coincides with or falls wholly or partly within the board’s area must
establish a joint committee for the board’s area (an “integrated care
partnership”).

26.4.116ZA.2

The integrated care partnership for an area is to consist of—

26.4.116ZA.2.a

one member appointed by the integrated care board,

26.4.116ZA.2.b

one member appointed by each of the responsible local authorities, and

26.4.116ZA.2.c

any members appointed by the integrated care partnership.

26.4.116ZA.3

An integrated care partnership may determine its own procedure (including
quorum).

########### Integrated care strategies

26.4.116ZB

26.4.116ZB.1

An integrated care partnership must prepare a strategy (an “integrated care
strategy”) setting out how the assessed needs in relation to its area are to
be met by the exercise of functions of—

26.4.116ZB.1.a

the integrated care board for its area,

26.4.116ZB.1.b

NHS England, or

26.4.116ZB.1.c

the responsible local authorities whose areas coincide with or fall wholly or
partly within its area.

26.4.116ZB.2

In preparing a strategy under this section, an integrated care partnership
must, in particular, consider the extent to which the needs could be met more
effectively by the making of arrangements under section 75 of the National
Health Service Act 2006 (rather than in any other way).

26.4.116ZB.3

In preparing a strategy under this section, an integrated care partnership
must have regard to—

26.4.116ZB.3.a

the mandate published by the Secretary of State under section 13A of the
National Health Service Act 2006, and

26.4.116ZB.3.b

any guidance issued by the Secretary of State.

26.4.116ZB.4

In preparing a strategy under this section, an integrated care partnership
must—

26.4.116ZB.4.a

involve the Local Healthwatch organisations whose areas coincide with or fall
wholly or partly within its area, and

26.4.116ZB.4.b

involve the people who live or work in that area.

26.4.116ZB.5

An integrated care partnership may include in a strategy under this section a
statement of its views on how arrangements for the provision of health-related
services in its area could be more closely integrated with arrangements for
the provision of health services and social care services in that area.

26.4.116ZB.6

Each time that an integrated care partnership receives an assessment of
relevant needs under section 116(5A) it must—

26.4.116ZB.6.a

consider whether the current integrated care strategy should be revised, and

26.4.116ZB.6.b

if so, prepare a revised integrated care strategy under subsection (1).

26.4.116ZB.7

An integrated care partnership must—

26.4.116ZB.7.a

publish each integrated care strategy, and

26.4.116ZB.7.b

give a copy of each integrated care strategy to—

26.4.116ZB.7.b.i

each responsible local authority whose area coincides with or falls wholly or
partly within its area, and

26.4.116ZB.7.b.ii

each partner integrated care board of those responsible local authorities.

26.4.116ZB.8

In this section—

26.4.116ZB.8.a

“ assessed needs ”, in relation to the area of an integrated care partnership,
means the needs assessed under section 116 in relation to the areas of the
responsible local authorities so far as those needs relate to the integrated
care partnership’s area;

26.4.116ZB.8.b

“ partner integrated care board ”, in relation to a responsible local
authority, has the same meaning as in section 116;

26.4.116ZB.8.c

“ health services ”, “ health-related services ” and “ social care services ”
have the same meaning as in section 195 of the Health and Social Care Act
2012.

26.5

In section 116A (health and social care: joint health and wellbeing
strategies)—

26.5.a

in the heading, after “joint” insert  “local” ;

26.5.b

for subsections (1) and (2) substitute—

26.5.b.1

This section applies where a responsible local authority and each of its
partner integrated care boards receive an integrated care strategy under
section  116ZB (7)(b) .

26.5.b.2

The responsible local authority and each of its partner integrated care boards
must prepare a strategy (“a joint local health and wellbeing strategy”)
setting out how the assessed needs in relation to the responsible local
authority’s area are to be met by the exercise of functions of—

26.5.b.2.a

the responsible local authority,

26.5.b.2.b

its partner integrated care boards, or

26.5.b.2.c

NHS England.

26.5.b.2A

But the responsible local authority and its partner integrated care boards
need not prepare a new joint local health and wellbeing strategy if, having
considered the integrated care strategy, they consider that the existing joint
local health and wellbeing strategy is sufficient.

;

26.5.c

in subsection (3)—

26.5.c.i

#### Integrated care system: financial controls

##### NHS England’s financial responsibilities

27

For sections 223C to 223E of the National Health Service Act 2006 substitute—

######### Financial duties of NHS England: expenditure

27.223C

27.223C.1

NHS England must exercise its functions with a view to ensuring that
expenditure incurred by the following bodies in a financial year (taken
together) does not exceed the aggregate of any sums received by them in the
year—

27.223C.1.a

NHS England;

27.223C.1.b

integrated care boards.

27.223C.2

The Secretary of State may by direction—

27.223C.2.a

specify descriptions of expenditure that are, or are not, to be treated for
the purposes of this section as expenditure incurred by a body, or expenditure
incurred by it in a particular financial year;

27.223C.2.b

specify descriptions of sums that are, or are not, to be treated for the
purposes of this section as having been received by a body, or as having been
received by it in a particular financial year;

27.223C.2.c

provide for sums received by NHS England under section 223B in a year but not
spent to be treated for the purposes of this section as expenditure incurred
by it in a particular financial year;

27.223C.2.d

provide for sums received by an integrated care board under section 223G in a
year but not spent to be treated for the purposes of this section as
expenditure incurred by it in a particular financial year.

27.223C.3

For the purposes of this section any sum allotted to NHS England for a year
under section 223B is to be treated as received by it in that year (subject to
any direction under subsection  (2)(b) ).

######### NHS England: banking facilities

27.223CA

The Secretary of State may by direction require NHS England to use banking
facilities specified in the direction for any purposes so specified.

######### Financial duties of NHS England: controls on total resource use

27.223D

27.223D.1

NHS England must exercise its functions with a view to ensuring that, in
respect of each financial year—

27.223D.1.a

total capital resource use does not exceed the limit specified in a direction
by the Secretary of State;

27.223D.1.b

total revenue resource use does not exceed the limit specified in a direction
by the Secretary of State.

27.223D.2

In subsection  (1)  “total capital resource use” and “ total revenue resource
use ” means the use of capital resources or (as the case may be) revenue
resources by relevant NHS bodies, other than use that consists of the transfer
of resources between relevant NHS bodies.

27.223D.3

In subsection  (2)  “ relevant NHS bodies ” means—

27.223D.3.a

NHS England,

27.223D.3.b

integrated care boards,

27.223D.3.c

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

27.223D.3.d

NHS foundation trusts.

27.223D.4

A direction under subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b)  specifying a limit in relation
to a financial year may be varied by a subsequent direction only if—

27.223D.4.a

NHS England agrees to the change,

27.223D.4.b

a parliamentary general election takes place, or

27.223D.4.c

the Secretary of State considers that there are exceptional circumstances
which make the variation necessary.

27.223D.5

The Secretary of State must publish and lay before Parliament any directions
under this section.

27.223D.6

Any reference in this Chapter to the use of capital resources or revenue
resources is a reference to their expenditure, consumption or reduction in
value.

######### Financial duties of NHS England: additional controls on resource use

27.223E

27.223E.1

The Secretary of State may direct NHS England to ensure—

27.223E.1.a

that relevant capital resource in a financial year which is attributable to
matters specified in the direction does not exceed an amount so specified;

27.223E.1.b

that relevant revenue resource use in a financial year which is attributable
to matters specified in the direction does not exceed an amount so specified.

27.223E.2

In subsection  (1)  “relevant capital resource use” and “ relevant revenue
resource use ” means the use of capital resources or (as the case may be)
revenue resources by NHS England and integrated care boards.

27.223E.3

The Secretary of State may direct NHS England to ensure that NHS England’s use
of revenue resources in a financial year which is attributable to such matters
relating to administration as are specified in the direction does not exceed
an amount so specified.

In section  223C  of the National Health Service Act 2006 (as substituted by
section 27 of this Act), in subsection (1), after paragraph (b) insert—

28.c

NHS trusts established under section 25;

28.d

NHS foundation trusts.

##### Financial responsibilities of integrated care boards and their partners

29

29.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

29.2

For the italic heading before section 223G substitute—

  Integrated care boards

.

29.3

After section 223GA insert—

########### Power to impose financial requirements on integrated care boards

29.3.223GB

29.3.223GB.1

NHS England may give integrated care boards directions about their management
or use of financial or other resources.

29.3.223GB.2

The directions that may be given include a direction imposing limits on
expenditure or resource use by integrated care boards.

29.3.223GB.3

NHS England must publish any directions under this section.

########### Financial duties of integrated care boards: expenditure limits

29.3.223GC

29.3.223GC.1

An integrated care board must exercise its functions with a view to ensuring
that expenditure incurred by the board in a financial year does not exceed the
sums received by it in that year.

29.3.223GC.2

NHS England may by direction—

29.3.223GC.2.a

specify descriptions of expenditure that are, or are not, to be treated for
the purposes of this section as expenditure incurred by an integrated care
board, or expenditure incurred by it in a particular financial year;

29.3.223GC.2.b

specify descriptions of sums that are, or are not, to be treated for the
purposes of this section as having been received by an integrated care board,
or as having been received by it in a particular financial year;

29.3.223GC.2.c

provide for sums received by an integrated care board under section 223G in a
year but not spent to be treated for the purposes of this section as
expenditure incurred by it in a particular financial year.

29.3.223GC.3

For the purposes of this section any sum allotted to an integrated care board
for a year under section 223G is to be treated as received by it in that year
(subject to any direction under subsection  (2)(b) ).

########### Integrated care boards: banking facilities

29.3.223GD

The Secretary of State may give integrated care boards directions requiring
them to use specified banking facilities for any specified purposes.

29.4

Omit sections 223H to 223J (financial duties of clinical commissioning
groups).

29.5

After section 223K insert—

########### Joint duties of an integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

############ Joint financial objectives for integrated care boards etc

29.5.223L

29.5.223L.1

NHS England may set joint financial objectives for integrated care boards and
their partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts.

29.5.223L.2

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
must seek to achieve any financial objectives set under this section.

29.5.223L.3

Financial objectives under this section may apply to—

29.5.223L.3.a

integrated care boards and their partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts
generally,

29.5.223L.3.b

a particular integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS
foundation trusts, or

29.5.223L.3.c

an integrated care board of a particular description and its partner NHS
trusts and NHS foundation trusts.

############ Financial duties of integrated care boards etc: use of resources

29.5.223M

29.5.223M.1

Each integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts must exercise their functions with a view to ensuring that, in respect
of each financial year—

29.5.223M.1.a

local capital resource use does not exceed the limit specified in a direction
by NHS England;

29.5.223M.1.b

local revenue resource use does not exceed the limit specified in a direction
by NHS England.

29.5.223M.2

In this section “local capital resource use” and “ local revenue resource use
” means the use of capital resources or (as the case may be) revenue resources
by the integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts, other than use that consists of the transfer of resources between
those bodies.

29.5.223M.3

Where an NHS trust or NHS foundation trust is the partner of more than one
integrated care board, its use of capital resources or revenue resources is to
be apportioned for the purposes of this section to one or more of the
integrated care boards in such manner as may be provided for in a direction by
NHS England.

29.5.223M.4

NHS England may by direction make provision for determining to which
integrated care board, NHS trust or NHS foundation trust a use of capital
resources or revenue resources is to be attributed for the purposes of this
section.

############ Financial duties of integrated care boards etc: additional controls on resource use

29.5.223N

29.5.223N.1

NHS England may direct an integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and
NHS foundation trusts to exercise their functions with a view to—

29.5.223N.1.a

ensuring that local capital resource use in a financial year which is
attributable to matters specified in the direction does not exceed an amount
so specified;

29.5.223N.1.b

ensuring that local revenue resource use in a financial year which is
attributable to matters specified in the direction does not exceed an amount
so specified.

29.5.223N.2

A direction under subsection  (1)  may—

29.5.223N.2.a

specify descriptions of resources which must, or must not, be treated as local
capital resources or local revenue resources for the purposes of the
direction;

29.5.223N.2.b

specify uses of local capital resources or local revenue resources which must,
or must not, be taken into account for the purposes of the direction.

29.5.223N.3

Any directions given under section  223M (3)  or  (4)  apply for the purposes
of this section as they apply for the purposes of section  223M .

29.5.223N.4

In this section “local capital resource use” and “local revenue resource use”
have the meaning given by section  223M (2) .

########### Directions about resources etc to be taken into account

############ Resources etc relevant to section 223D, 223E or 

29.5.223O

The Secretary of State may give directions, in relation to a financial year—

29.5.223O.a

specifying descriptions of resources which must, or must not, be treated as
capital resources or revenue resources for the purposes of section 223D, 223E
or  223M ;

29.5.223O.b

specifying uses of capital resources or revenue resources which must, or must
not, be taken into account for the purposes of section 223D, 223E or  223M .

########### Financial duties of integrated care boards etc: expenditure limits

30.3.223LA

30.3.223LA.1

An integrated care board and its partner NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

in a financial year (taken together) does not exceed the aggregate of any sums
received by them in the year.

##### Care Quality Commission reviews etc of integrated care system

31

31.1

Chapter 3 of Part 1 of the Health and Social Care Act 2008 (quality of health

31.2

After section 46A (inserted by section 163 of this Act) insert—

########### Reviews and performance assessments: integrated care system

31.2.46B

31.2.46B.1

The Commission must, in accordance with this section—

31.2.46B.1.a

conduct reviews of—

31.2.46B.1.a.i

the provision of relevant health care, and adult social care, within the area
of each integrated care board, and

31.2.46B.1.a.ii

the exercise of the functions of the following in relation to the provision of
that care within the area of each integrated care board: the board; its
partner local authorities; and registered service providers,

31.2.46B.1.b

assess the functioning of the system for the provision of relevant health
care, and adult social care, within the area of each integrated care board
(taking into account, in particular, how those mentioned in paragraph  (a)(ii)
work together), and

31.2.46B.1.c

publish a report of its assessment.

31.2.46B.2

The Secretary of State—

31.2.46B.2.a

must set, and may from time to time revise, objectives and priorities for the
Commission in relation to assessments under this section, and

31.2.46B.2.b

must inform the Commission of the objectives and priorities.

31.2.46B.3

The priorities set by the Secretary of State under subsection (2)(a) must
include priorities relating to leadership, the integration of services and the
quality and safety of services.

31.2.46B.4

The Commission—

31.2.46B.4.a

must determine, and may from time to time revise, indicators of quality for
the purposes of assessments under this section, and

31.2.46B.4.b

must obtain the approval of the Secretary of State in relation to the
indicators.

31.2.46B.5

The Secretary of State may direct the Commission to revise the indicators
under subsection  (4) .

31.2.46B.6

Different objectives and priorities may be set, and different indicators of
quality may be determined, for different cases.

31.2.46B.7

The Commission—

31.2.46B.7.a

must prepare, and may from time to time revise, a statement—

31.2.46B.7.a.i

setting out the frequency with which reviews under this section are to be
conducted and the period to which they are to relate, and

31.2.46B.7.a.ii

describing the method that it proposes to use in assessing and evaluating the
functioning of the system for the provision of relevant health care, and adult
social care, within the area of an integrated care board, and

31.2.46B.7.b

must obtain the approval of the Secretary of State in relation to the
statement.

31.2.46B.8

The statement may—

31.2.46B.8.a

make different provision about frequency and period of reviews for different
cases, and

31.2.46B.8.b

describe different methods for different cases.

31.2.46B.9

Before preparing or revising a statement under subsection  (7)  the Commission
must consult—

31.2.46B.9.a

NHS England, and

31.2.46B.9.b

any other persons it considers appropriate.

31.2.46B.10

The Secretary of State may direct the Commission to revise the statement under
subsection  (7) .

31.2.46B.11

The Commission must publish—

31.2.46B.11.a

the objectives and priorities under subsection  (2) ,

31.2.46B.11.b

the indicators of quality under subsection  (4) , and

31.2.46B.11.c

the statement under subsection  (7) .

31.2.46B.12

For the purposes of this section—

      “ adult social care ” means social care for individuals aged 18 or over;
“ partner local authority ”, in relation to an integrated care board, means
any English local authority whose area coincides with, or includes the whole
or any part of, the area of the integrated care board;           “ registered
service provider ” means a person registered under Chapter 2 as a service
provider;           “ relevant health care ” means—         NHS care, or
the promotion and protection of public health.

31.2.46B.13

Regulations may amend the definition of “relevant health care” to include
health care which is provided or commissioned by a public authority (but which
does not amount to NHS care).

31.3

46A ” (inserted by section 163 of this Act) insert  “or  46B ” .

31.4

In section 50 (failings by English local authorities), in subsection (1),
after “ 46A ” (inserted by section 163 of this Act) insert  “or  46B ” .

In section 162 (orders and regulations: parliamentary control), in subsection
(3), after paragraph (c) insert—

31.5.c

regulations under section  46B (13)  (amendment of definition of relevant
health care),

##### Transfer schemes in connection with abolished bodies

38

38.1

The Secretary of State may make one or more schemes for the transfer of
property, rights and liabilities from Monitor or the National Health Service
Trust Development Authority to NHS England.

38.2

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

38.2.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

38.2.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

38.2.c

criminal liabilities.

38.3

A transfer scheme may—

38.3.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

38.3.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by the transferor in
respect of anything transferred;

38.3.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

38.3.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

38.3.e

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

38.3.f

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

38.4

In subsection  (3)(e) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

38.5

In this section references to rights and liabilities include rights and
liabilities relating to a contract of employment.

##### Transfer schemes under section 38: taxation

39

39.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision varying the way in which a
relevant tax has effect in relation to—

39.1.a

anything transferred under a scheme under section 38, or

39.1.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, a transfer under such a
scheme.

39.2

The provision which may be made under subsection  (1)(a)  includes in
particular provision for—

39.2.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything transferred;

39.2.b

anything transferred to be treated in a specified way for the purposes of a
tax provision;

39.2.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything transferred.

39.3

The provision which may be made under subsection (1)(b) includes in particular
provision for—

39.3.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything done for the purposes of or in relation to the transfer;

39.3.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer to have or
not have a specified consequence or be treated in a specified way;

39.3.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything done for the
purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer.

39.4

Regulations under this section are subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of the House of Commons.

39.5

In this section—

      “ relevant tax ” means income tax, corporation tax, capital gains tax,
value added tax, stamp duty or stamp duty reserve tax;           “ tax
provision ” means a provision of an enactment about a relevant tax.

##### Arrangements for exercise of public health functions

42

For section 7A of the National Health Service Act 2006 substitute—

######### Exercise of Secretary of State’s public health functions

42.7A

42.7A.1

The Secretary of State may arrange for any of the public health functions of
the Secretary of State to be exercised by one or more relevant bodies.

42.7A.2

In this section “ relevant body ” means—

42.7A.2.a

NHS England,

42.7A.2.b

an integrated care board,

42.7A.2.c

a local authority (within the meaning of section 2B),

42.7A.2.d

a combined authority, or

42.7A.2.e

such other body as may be prescribed.

42.7A.3

Arrangements under this section may be made on such terms as may be agreed
between the parties including—

42.7A.3.a

terms as to payment;

42.7A.3.b

terms prohibiting or restricting a relevant body from making delegation
arrangements in relation to a function that is exercisable by it by virtue of
arrangements under this section.

42.7A.4

In subsection  (3)(b)  “ delegation arrangements ” means arrangements made by
a person for the exercise of a function by someone else.

42.7A.5

Any rights acquired, or liabilities (including liabilities in tort) incurred,
in respect of the exercise by a relevant body of any function by virtue of
this section are enforceable by or against that body (and no other person).

42.7A.6

The reference in subsection (1) to the public health functions of the
Secretary of State includes any functions of the Secretary of State
exercisable in connection with those functions (including the powers conferred
by section 12).

44.2.7C.1.a

NHS England, or

44.2.7C.1.b

any other public body,

to exercise any of the investigation functions which are specified in the

subsection  (1) .

########### Transfer schemes in connection with a direction under section 7C

44.2.7D

44.2.7D.1

The Secretary of State may, in connection with a direction under section  7C ,
make one or more transfer schemes.

44.2.7D.2

A “transfer scheme” is a scheme for the transfer to NHS England or any other
public body of any property, rights or liabilities relating to the discharge
of functions pursuant to any directions made by the Secretary of State under
the power conferred by section 7C.

44.2.7D.3

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

44.2.7D.3.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

44.2.7D.3.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

44.2.7D.3.c

criminal liabilities.

44.2.7D.4

A transfer scheme may—

44.2.7D.4.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

44.2.7D.4.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by, or on behalf of
or in relation to the transferor in respect of anything transferred;

44.2.7D.4.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

44.2.7D.4.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

44.2.7D.4.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

44.2.7D.4.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

44.2.7D.4.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

44.2.7D.5

A transfer scheme may provide—

44.2.7D.5.a

for modifications by agreement;

44.2.7D.5.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

44.2.7D.6

In subsection  (4) (f) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

44.2.7D.7

For the purposes of this section—

44.2.7D.7.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

44.2.7D.7.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

44.2.7D.8

For the purposes of subsection  (7) (a) —

44.2.7D.8.a

an individual who holds employment in the civil service of the State is to be
treated as employed by virtue of a contract of employment, and

44.2.7D.8.b

the terms of the individual’s employment in the civil service are to be
regarded as constituting the terms of the contract of employment.

########### Transfer schemes under section 

44.2.7E

44.2.7E.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision varying the way in which a
relevant tax has effect in relation to—

44.2.7E.1.a

anything transferred under a scheme under section  7D , or

44.2.7E.1.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, a transfer under such a
scheme.

44.2.7E.2

The provision which may be made under subsection  (1)(a)  includes in
particular provision for—

44.2.7E.2.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything transferred;

44.2.7E.2.b

anything transferred to be treated in a specified way for the purposes of a
tax provision;

44.2.7E.2.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything transferred.

44.2.7E.3

The provision which may be made under subsection (1)(b) includes in particular
provision for—

44.2.7E.3.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything done for the purposes of or in relation to the transfer;

44.2.7E.3.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer to have or
not have a specified consequence or be treated in a specified way;

44.2.7E.3.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything done for the
purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer.

44.2.7E.4

In this section references to the transfer of property include the grant of a
lease.

44.2.7E.5

In this section—

      “ relevant tax ” means income tax, corporation tax, capital gains tax,
value added tax, stamp duty or stamp duty reserve tax;           “ tax
provision ” means a provision of an enactment about a relevant tax.

section 7C,

##### General power to direct NHS England

45

45.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

45.2

Before section 13Z1 (and the italic heading before it) insert—

########### Powers of direction

############ Secretary of State directions as to exercise of NHS England functions

45.2.13ZC

45.2.13ZC.1

The Secretary of State may give NHS England directions as to the exercise of
any of its functions.

45.2.13ZC.2

The directions that may be given include a direction as to whether a power is
to be exercised or not.

45.2.13ZC.3

The directions that may be given include a direction as to—

45.2.13ZC.3.a

when or how a function is, or is not, to be exercised;

45.2.13ZC.3.b

conditions that must be met before a function is exercised (for example,
conditions relating to the provision of information, consultation or
approval);

45.2.13ZC.3.c

matters to be taken into account in exercising a function.

45.2.13ZC.4

For exceptions to the power to give directions under subsection  (1) , see
section  13ZD .

45.2.13ZC.5

A direction under subsection  (1)  must include a statement that the Secretary
of State considers the direction to be in the public interest.

45.2.13ZC.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a direction under subsection
(1) , the Secretary of State must publish it.

45.2.13ZC.7

The fact that the Secretary of State has a function under any other enactment
in relation to NHS England’s exercise of functions is not to be read as
limiting the power conferred by subsection (1).

45.2.13ZC.8

The reference in subsection (7) to a function of the Secretary of State does
not include a function of making subordinate legislation.

############ Power to give directions: exceptions

45.2.13ZD

45.2.13ZD.1

A direction under section  13ZC  may not be given in relation to a function
relating to the appointment or employment of a person.

45.2.13ZD.2

A direction under section  13ZC  may not be given in relation to a decision
about the services to be provided to a particular individual for or in
connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness.

45.2.13ZD.3

A direction under section  13ZC  may not be given in relation to the provision
of any drug, medicine or other treatment, or the use of any diagnostic
technique, unless NICE has made a recommendation or issued guidance as to its
clinical and cost effectiveness and the direction is not inconsistent with
that recommendation or guidance.

############ Compliance with directions: significant failure

45.2.13ZE

45.2.13ZE.1

This section applies where—

45.2.13ZE.1.a

NHS England is given a direction under section  13ZC ,

45.2.13ZE.1.b

the direction —

45.2.13ZE.1.b.i

states that the Secretary of State considers that NHS England is failing or
has failed to discharge any of its functions, and

45.2.13ZE.1.b.ii

states that the Secretary of State considers that the failure is significant
and explains why,

45.2.13ZE.1.c

the direction states that it is given for the purposes of addressing that
failure, and

45.2.13ZE.1.d

NHS England fails to comply with the direction.

45.2.13ZE.2

The Secretary of State may—

45.2.13ZE.2.a

discharge the functions to which the direction relates, or

45.2.13ZE.2.b

make arrangements for any other person to discharge them on the Secretary of
State’s behalf.

45.2.13ZE.3

Where the Secretary of State exercises the power under subsection (2), the
Secretary of State must publish the reasons for doing so.

45.2.13ZE.4

For the purpose of this section—

45.2.13ZE.4.a

a failure to discharge a function includes a failure to discharge it properly,
and

45.2.13ZE.4.b

a failure to discharge a function properly includes a failure to discharge it
consistently with what the Secretary of State considers to be the interests of
the health service.

############ Secretary of State directions to provide information

45.2.13ZF

45.2.13ZF.1

The Secretary of State may direct NHS England to provide the Secretary of
State with any documents or other information that may be specified in the
direction.

45.2.13ZF.2

The directions that may be given include a direction to provide documents or
other information that NHS England would need to obtain from others in the
exercise of some other power.

45.2.13ZF.3

The directions may include provision as to—

45.2.13ZF.3.a

the form or manner in which the documents or information must be provided;

45.2.13ZF.3.b

the time at which or period within which the documents or information must be
provided.

45.3

Omit section 13Z2 (failure to discharge functions) and the italic heading
before it.

45.4

In Schedule A1 (constitution of NHS England), omit paragraph 14 and the italic
heading before it.
