##### Review into NHS supply chains

47

47.1

The Secretary of State must carry out a review into the risk of slavery and
human trafficking taking place in relation to people involved in NHS supply
chains.

47.2

The Secretary of State may determine which NHS supply chains to consider as
part of the review or otherwise limit the scope of the review.

47.3

But the review must at least consider a significant proportion of NHS supply
chains for cotton-based products in relation to which companies formed under
section 223 of the National Health Service Act 2006 (taken as a whole)
exercise functions.

47.4

The Secretary of State must publish and lay before Parliament a report on the
outcome of the review before the end of the period of 18 months beginning with
the day on which this section comes into force.

47.5

The report must describe—

47.5.a

the scope of the review, and

47.5.b

the methodology used in carrying out the review.

47.6

The report must include any views of the Secretary of State as to steps that
should be taken to mitigate the risk mentioned in subsection  (1) .

47.7

NHS England must assist in the carrying out of the review or the preparation
of the report under this section, if requested to do so by the Secretary of
State.

47.8

In this section—

      “ health service in England ” means the health service continued under
section 1(1) of the National Health Service Act 2006;           “ NHS supply
chain ” means the supply chain for providing goods or services for the
purposes of the health service in England;           “ slavery and human
trafficking ” has the meaning given by section 54(12) of the Modern Slavery
Act 2015.

##### NHS trusts: wider effect of decisions

52

After section 26 of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

######### Duty to have regard to wider effect of decisions

52.26A

52.26A.1

In making a decision about the exercise of its functions, an NHS trust
established under section 25 must have regard to all likely effects of the
decision in relation to—

52.26A.1.a

the health and well-being of the people of England;

52.26A.1.b

the quality of services provided to individuals—

52.26A.1.b.i

by relevant bodies, or

52.26A.1.b.ii

in pursuance of arrangements made by relevant bodies,

for or in connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness,
as part of the health service in England;

52.26A.1.c

efficiency and sustainability in relation to the use of resources by relevant
bodies for the purposes of the health service in England.

52.26A.2

In subsection  (1) —

52.26A.2.a

the reference to a decision does not include a reference to a decision about
the services to be provided to a particular individual for or in connection
with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness;

52.26A.2.b

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the health and well-
being of the people of England includes a reference to its effects in relation
to inequalities between the people of England with respect to their health and
well-being;

52.26A.2.c

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the quality of services
provided to individuals includes a reference to its effects in relation to
inequalities between individuals with respect to the benefits that they can
obtain from those services.

52.26A.3

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS trusts must have regard to
guidance published by NHS England under section 13NB.

52.26A.4

In this section “ relevant bodies ” means—

52.26A.4.a

NHS England,

52.26A.4.b

integrated care boards,

52.26A.4.c

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

52.26A.4.d

NHS foundation trusts.

##### NHS trusts: duties in relation to climate change

53

After section 26A of the National Health Service Act 2006 (inserted by section
52 of this Act) insert—

######### Duties in relation to climate change etc

53.26B

53.26B.1

An NHS trust established under section 25 must, in the exercise of its
functions, have regard to the need to—

53.26B.1.a

contribute towards compliance with—

53.26B.1.a.i

section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target), and

53.26B.1.a.ii

section 5 of the Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets), and

53.26B.1.b

adapt to any current or predicted impacts of climate change identified in the
most recent report under section 56 of the Climate Change Act 2008.

53.26B.2

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS trusts must have regard to
guidance published by NHS England under section 13ND.

(2) .

##### Capital spending limits for NHS foundation trusts

62

62.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

62.2

After section 42A insert—

########### Limits on capital expenditure

62.2.42B

62.2.42B.1

NHS England may make an order imposing a limit on the capital expenditure of
an NHS foundation trust in respect of a single financial year.

62.2.42B.2

The order must specify—

62.2.42B.2.a

the trust,

62.2.42B.2.b

the capital expenditure limit, and

62.2.42B.2.c

the financial year to which the limit relates.

62.2.42B.3

NHS England must consult the trust before making the order.

62.2.42B.4

NHS England must publish each order under this section.

62.2.42B.5

An order under this section may be made at any time during or before the
financial year to which it relates.

62.2.42B.6

A trust that is the subject of an order under this section must not exceed the
capital expenditure limit imposed by the order during the financial year to
which it relates.

62.2.42B.7

In this section “ capital expenditure ”, in relation to an NHS foundation
trust, means expenditure of the trust which falls to be capitalised in its
annual accounts.

########### Guidance in relation to orders under section 42B

62.2.42C

62.2.42C.1

NHS England must publish guidance about the exercise of its power to make
orders under section  42B , including guidance about—

62.2.42C.1.a

the circumstances in which it is likely to make an order, and

62.2.42C.1.b

the method it will use to determine the capital expenditure limit.

62.2.42C.2

NHS England must consult the Secretary of State before it publishes guidance,
or revised guidance, under this section.

62.2.42C.3

NHS England must have regard to the guidance in exercising its power to make
orders under section 42B.

62.3

In section 64 (orders and regulations under Chapter 5), in subsection (1),
after “regulations” insert  “, other than the power to make an order under
section 42B,” .

##### NHS foundation trusts: wider effect of decisions

67

In the National Health Service Act 2006, after section 63 insert—

######### Duty to have regard to wider effect of decisions

67.63A

67.63A.1

In making a decision about the exercise of its functions, an NHS foundation
trust must have regard to all likely effects of the decision in relation to—

67.63A.1.a

the health and well-being of the people of England;

67.63A.1.b

the quality of services provided to individuals—

67.63A.1.b.i

by relevant bodies, or

67.63A.1.b.ii

in pursuance of arrangements made by relevant bodies,

for or in connection with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness,
as part of the health service in England;

67.63A.1.c

efficiency and sustainability in relation to the use of resources by relevant
bodies for the purposes of the health service in England.

67.63A.2

In subsection  (1) —

67.63A.2.a

the reference to a decision does not include a reference to a decision about
the services to be provided to a particular individual for or in connection
with the prevention, diagnosis or treatment of illness;

67.63A.2.b

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the health and well-
being of the people of England includes a reference to its effects in relation
to inequalities between the people of England with respect to their health and
well-being;

67.63A.2.c

the reference to effects of a decision in relation to the quality of services
provided to individuals includes a reference to its effects in relation to
inequalities between individuals with respect to the benefits that they can
obtain from those services.

67.63A.3

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS foundation trusts must have
regard to guidance published by NHS England under section 13NB.

67.63A.4

In this section “ relevant bodies ” means—

67.63A.4.a

NHS England,

67.63A.4.b

integrated care boards,

67.63A.4.c

NHS trusts established under section 25, and

67.63A.4.d

NHS foundation trusts.

##### NHS foundation trusts: duties in relation to climate change

68

After section 63A of the National Health Service Act 2006 (inserted by section
67 of this Act) insert—

######### Duties in relation to climate change etc

68.63B

68.63B.1

An NHS foundation trust must, in the exercise of its functions, have regard to
the need to—

68.63B.1.a

contribute towards compliance with—

68.63B.1.a.i

section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target), and

68.63B.1.a.ii

section 5 of the Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets), and

68.63B.1.b

adapt to any current or predicted impacts of climate change identified in the
most recent report under section 56 of the Climate Change Act 2008.

68.63B.2

In discharging the duty under this section, NHS foundation trusts must have
regard to guidance published by NHS England under section 13ND.

#### NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

##### Transfer schemes between trusts

69

After section 69 of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

######### Transfer schemes

########## Transfer schemes: NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

69.69A

69.69A.1

NHS England may make one or more schemes for the transfer of property, rights
and liabilities from a relevant NHS body to another relevant NHS body on an
application made to it under this section.

69.69A.2

The application must—

69.69A.2.a

be made jointly by the relevant NHS bodies, and

69.69A.2.b

state the property, rights or liabilities to be transferred.

69.69A.3

NHS England may grant an application under this section only if it is
satisfied that such steps as are necessary to prepare for the transfer have
been taken.

69.69A.4

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

69.69A.4.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

69.69A.4.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

69.69A.4.c

criminal liabilities.

69.69A.5

A transfer scheme may—

69.69A.5.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

69.69A.5.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by the transferor in
respect of anything transferred;

69.69A.5.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

69.69A.5.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

69.69A.5.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

69.69A.5.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

69.69A.5.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

69.69A.6

A transfer scheme may provide—

69.69A.6.a

for modifications by agreement;

69.69A.6.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

69.69A.7

In this section—

69.69A.7.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

69.69A.7.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

69.69A.8

In this section—

      “ relevant NHS body ” means—         an NHS trust established under
section 25;           an NHS foundation trust;                 “ the TUPE
regulations ” means the Transfer of Undertakings (Protection of Employment)
Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

#### Joint working and delegation of functions

##### Joint working and delegation arrangements

71

71.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

71.2

After section  65Z4  (inserted by section 14 of this Act) insert—

########### Joint working arrangements and delegation

############ Joint working and delegation arrangements

71.2.65Z5

71.2.65Z5.1

A relevant body may arrange for any functions exercisable by it to be
exercised by or jointly with any one or more of the following—

71.2.65Z5.1.a

a relevant body;

71.2.65Z5.1.b

a local authority (within the meaning of section 2B);

71.2.65Z5.1.c

a combined authority.

71.2.65Z5.2

In this section “ relevant body ” means—

71.2.65Z5.2.a

NHS England,

71.2.65Z5.2.b

an integrated care board,

71.2.65Z5.2.c

an NHS trust established under section 25,

71.2.65Z5.2.d

an NHS foundation trust, or

71.2.65Z5.2.e

such other body as may be prescribed.

71.2.65Z5.3

Regulations may—

71.2.65Z5.3.a

provide that the power in subsection (1) does not apply, or applies only to a
prescribed extent, in relation to prescribed functions;

71.2.65Z5.3.b

impose conditions on the exercise of the power.

71.2.65Z5.4

Arrangements under this section may be made on such terms as may be agreed
between the parties, including—

71.2.65Z5.4.a

terms as to payment;

71.2.65Z5.4.b

terms prohibiting or restricting a body from making delegation arrangements in
relation to a function that is exercisable by it by virtue of arrangements
under this section.

71.2.65Z5.5

In subsection  (4)(b)  “ delegation arrangements ” means arrangements made by
a body for the exercise of a function by someone else.

71.2.65Z5.6

Any rights acquired, or liabilities (including liabilities in tort) incurred,
in respect of the exercise by a body of any function by virtue of this section
are enforceable by or against that body (and no other person).

############ Joint committees and pooled funds

71.2.65Z6

71.2.65Z6.1

This section applies where a function is exercisable jointly (by virtue of
section  65Z5  or otherwise) by a relevant body and any one or more of the
following—

71.2.65Z6.1.a

a relevant body;

71.2.65Z6.1.b

a local authority (within the meaning of section 2B);

71.2.65Z6.1.c

a combined authority.

71.2.65Z6.2

The bodies by whom the function is exercisable jointly may—

71.2.65Z6.2.a

arrange for the function to be exercised by a joint committee of theirs;

71.2.65Z6.2.b

arrange for one or more of the bodies, or a joint committee of the bodies, to
establish and maintain a pooled fund.

71.2.65Z6.3

A pooled fund is a fund—

71.2.65Z6.3.a

which is made up of payments received in accordance with the arrangements from
relevant bodies that are party to the arrangements, and

71.2.65Z6.3.b

out of which payments may be made in accordance with the arrangements towards
expenditure incurred in the exercise of functions in relation to which the
arrangements are made.

71.2.65Z6.4

Arrangements under this section may be made on such terms as may be agreed
between the parties, including terms as to payment.

71.2.65Z6.5

In this section “ relevant body ” has the meaning given by section  65Z5 (2) .

############ Joint working and delegation: guidance by NHS England

71.2.65Z7

71.2.65Z7.1

NHS England may publish guidance for relevant bodies about the exercise of
their powers under sections  65Z5  and  65Z6 .

71.2.65Z7.2

A relevant body must have regard to any guidance published under this section.

71.2.65Z7.3

In this section “ relevant body ” has the meaning given by section  65Z5 (2) .

71.3

In section 75(7B)—

71.3.a

at the end of paragraph (a) insert  “or” ;

71.3.b

for paragraphs (b) and (c) substitute—

71.3.b.b

section  65Z5  (joint working and delegation arrangements).

71.4

In consequence of subsection  (2) , omit sections 13Z to 13ZB and the italic
heading before those sections.

#### Patient choice and procurement

##### Regulations as to patient choice

78

78.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

78.2

In section 6E (standing rules)—

78.2.a

in subsection (1)—

78.2.a.i

for “may” substitute  “must” ;

78.2.a.ii

for “or” substitute  “and” ;

78.2.b

after subsection (1) insert—

78.2.b.1A

The regulations must make provision as to the arrangements that NHS England
and integrated care boards must make, in exercising their commissioning
functions, for enabling persons to whom specified treatments or other
specified services are to be provided to make choices with respect to
specified aspects of them.

78.2.b.1B

The regulations may make other provision for the purpose of securing that, in
exercising their commissioning functions, NHS England and integrated care
boards protect and promote the rights of persons to make choices in relation
to treatments or other services, where those rights—

78.2.b.1B.a

arise by virtue of regulations under subsection  (1A) , or

78.2.b.1B.b

are described in the NHS Constitution.

;

78.2.c

omit subsection (2)(c).

78.3

After section 6E insert—

########### Enforcement of section 6E regulations relating to patient choice

78.3.6F

78.3.6F.1

NHS England may investigate whether an integrated care board has failed or is
likely to fail to comply with a requirement imposed by regulations under
section 6E (1A)  or  (1B)  (a “patient choice requirement”).

78.3.6F.2

NHS England may direct an integrated care board—

78.3.6F.2.a

to put in place measures for the purpose of preventing failures to comply with
patient choice requirements or mitigating the effect of such failures, or

78.3.6F.2.b

where an investigation under subsection  (1)  has been carried out, to remedy
a failure to comply with patient choice requirements.

78.3.6F.3

Where an investigation under subsection  (1)  is being or has been carried
out, NHS England may accept from the integrated care board an undertaking that
it will take any action falling within subsection  (2)(a)  or  (b)  that is
specified in the undertaking, within a period that is so specified.

78.3.6F.4

Where NHS England accepts an undertaking under subsection  (3) , NHS England
may not—

78.3.6F.4.a

continue to carry out any ongoing investigation under subsection  (1)  so far
as relating to matters to which the undertaking relates, or

78.3.6F.4.b

give a direction under subsection  (2)  in relation to those matters,

unless the integrated care board fails to comply with the undertaking.

78.3.6F.5

If an integrated care board from which NHS England has accepted an undertaking
under subsection  (3)  complies partially with the undertaking, NHS England
must take the partial compliance into account in deciding whether to do
something mentioned in subsection  (4) (a)  or  (b) .

78.3.6F.6

Schedule 1ZA makes further provision about undertakings.

########### Guidance relating to patient choice

78.3.6G

78.3.6G.1

NHS England must publish guidance about how it intends to exercise powers
conferred on it by section  6F  and Schedule 1ZA.

78.3.6G.2

Before publishing guidance under this section, NHS England must obtain the
approval of the Secretary of State.

78.4

In section 13U (annual report), in subsection (2)(c), for the words from
“sections” to the end substitute

or by virtue of—

      section 6E (1A)  and  (1B) ;           section 13E;           section
13G;           section 13I;           section 13Q.

##### Procurement regulations

79

After section 12ZA of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

######### Procurement

########## Procurement regulations

79.12ZB

79.12ZB.1

Regulations may make provision in relation to the processes to be followed and
objectives to be pursued by relevant authorities in the procurement of—

79.12ZB.1.a

health care services for the purposes of the health service in England, and

79.12ZB.1.b

other goods or services that are procured together with those health care
services.

79.12ZB.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)  must include provision specifying steps to
be taken when following a competitive tendering process.

79.12ZB.3

Regulations under subsection  (1)  must, in relation to the procurement of all
health care services to which they apply, make provision for the purposes of—

79.12ZB.3.a

ensuring transparency;

79.12ZB.3.b

ensuring fairness;

79.12ZB.3.c

ensuring that compliance can be verified;

79.12ZB.3.d

managing conflicts of interest.

79.12ZB.4

NHS England must publish such guidance as it considers appropriate about
compliance with the regulations.

79.12ZB.5

A relevant authority must have regard to guidance published under this
section.

79.12ZB.6

Before publishing guidance under this section, NHS England must obtain the
approval of the Secretary of State.

79.12ZB.7

In this section—

      “ health care service ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 of the Health
and Social Care Act 2012 (see section 150 of that Act);           “ relevant
authority ” means—         a combined authority;           an integrated care
board;           a local authority in England;           NHS England;
an NHS foundation trust;           an NHS trust established under section 25.

##### Eradicating slavery and human trafficking in supply chains

81

81.1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

81.2

After section 12ZB (inserted by section 79) insert—

########### Eradicating slavery and human trafficking in supply chains

81.2.12ZC

81.2.12ZC.1

The Secretary of State must by regulations make such provision as the
Secretary of State thinks appropriate with a view to eradicating the use in
the health service in England of goods or services that are tainted by slavery
and human trafficking.

81.2.12ZC.2

The regulations may, in particular, include—

81.2.12ZC.2.a

provision in connection with the processes to be followed by public bodies in
the procurement of goods or services for the purposes of the health service in
England (including provision as to circumstances in which a supplier is
excluded from consideration for the award of a contract);

81.2.12ZC.2.b

provision as to steps that must be taken by public bodies for assessing and
addressing the risk of slavery and human trafficking taking place in relation
to people involved in health service supply chains;

81.2.12ZC.2.c

provision as to matters for which provision must be made in contracts for
goods or services entered into by public bodies for the purposes of the health
service in England.

81.2.12ZC.3

In this section—

      “ health service supply chains ” means supply chains for providing goods
or services for the purposes of the health service in England;           “
public body ” means a body exercising functions of a public nature;
“ slavery and human trafficking ” has the meaning given by section 54(12) of
the Modern Slavery Act 2015;           “tainted”: goods or services are
“tainted” by slavery and human trafficking if slavery and human trafficking
takes place in relation to anyone involved in the supply chain for providing
those goods or services.

81.3

In section 272 (orders, regulations, rules and directions), in subsection (6),
after paragraph (zze) (inserted by section 80), insert—

81.3.zzf

regulations under section 12ZC,

.

##### Tidying up etc provisions about accounts of certain NHS bodies

87

87.1

After section 29 of the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

########### Special Health Authorities: accounts and audit

87.1.29A

87.1.29A.1

In this section a reference to a Special Health Authority is to a Special
Health Authority which—

87.1.29A.1.a

performs functions only or mainly in respect of England, or

87.1.29A.1.b

neither performs functions only or mainly in respect of England, nor performs
functions only or mainly in respect of Wales.

87.1.29A.2

A Special Health Authority must keep proper accounts and proper records in
relation to the accounts.

87.1.29A.3

The Secretary of State may give a Special Health Authority directions as to
the form in which its accounts must be kept.

87.1.29A.4

A Special Health Authority must prepare, in respect of each financial year,
annual accounts in such form as the Secretary of State may direct.

87.1.29A.5

A Special Health Authority must send copies of any annual accounts prepared by
it under subsection  (4) —

87.1.29A.5.a

to the Secretary of State, by such date as the Secretary of State may direct,
and

87.1.29A.5.b

to the Comptroller and Auditor General, as soon as is reasonably practicable
following the end of the financial year in question.

87.1.29A.6

The Comptroller and Auditor General must examine, certify and report on the
annual accounts.

87.1.29A.7

The Special Health Authority must lay before Parliament—

87.1.29A.7.a

a copy of the annual accounts, and

87.1.29A.7.b

the Comptroller and Auditor General’s report on them.

87.1.29A.8

Nothing in subsection  (2)  requires any annual accounts prepared by a Special
Health Authority to include matters relating to a charitable trust of which it
is a trustee.

87.1.29A.9

Nothing in subsection  (4)  has effect in relation to accounts relating to a
charitable trust of which the Special Health Authority is a trustee.

87.2

In Schedule 4 to that Act (NHS trusts), after paragraph 11 insert—

########### Accounts and audit

87.2.11A

87.2.11A.1

An NHS trust must keep proper accounts and proper records in relation to the
accounts.

87.2.11A.2

The Secretary of State may give an NHS trust directions as to the form in
which its accounts must be kept.

87.2.11A.3

An NHS trust must prepare, in respect of each financial year, annual accounts
in such form as the Secretary of State may direct.

87.2.11A.4

For the audit of the annual accounts, see the Local Audit and Accountability
Act 2014 (and, in particular, section 4 of that Act).

87.2.11A.5

The Comptroller and Auditor General may examine—

87.2.11A.5.a

the annual accounts and any records relating to them, and

87.2.11A.5.b

any report on them by the auditor or auditors.

87.2.11A.6

An NHS trust must send a copy of its audited annual accounts to NHS England by
such date as NHS England may direct.

87.2.11A.7

Nothing in sub-paragraph  (1)  has effect in relation to accounts relating to
a charitable trust of which an NHS trust is a trustee.

87.2.11A.8

Nothing in sub-paragraph  (3)  requires any accounts prepared by an NHS trust
to include matters relating to a charitable trust of which it is a trustee.

87.3

In consequence of subsections  (1)  and  (2) —

########### Transfer schemes in respect of previously transferred property

89.2.302

89.2.302.1

This section applies in relation to any property, rights or liabilities
transferred under a property transfer scheme made under section 300(1) (before
its repeal) from a Primary Care Trust, a Strategic Health Authority or the
Secretary of State to a Special Health Authority or a qualifying company.

89.2.302.2

The Secretary of State may make a scheme for the transfer of any such

89.2.302.3.c

89.2.302.8.a

89.2.302.8.b

a subsidiary of a company which is formed under that section and wholly owned
by the Secretary of State.

### Health and adult social care: information

#### Information about payments etc to persons in the health care sector

92

92.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations require manufacturers or commercial
suppliers of health care products, or connected persons, to—

92.1.a

publish information about payments or other benefits provided by them to
relevant persons, or

92.1.b

provide such information to the Secretary of State.

92.2

The regulations may make further provision about when and how the information
is to be published or provided.

92.3

The information may, in particular, include information about—

92.3.a

a payment or other benefit,

92.3.b

the person who provided it, or

92.3.c

the person who received it.

92.4

The regulations may make provision permitting or requiring the further
sharing, publication or use of the information.

92.5

The regulations may impose requirements on manufacturers or commercial
suppliers of health care products, or connected persons, about the retention
of information relating to payments or other benefits provided by them to
relevant persons.

92.6

The regulations may—

92.6.a

authorise the Secretary of State to designate as a “relevant scheme” any
scheme under which information about payments or other benefits to relevant
persons is collected or published by a person other than the Secretary of
State, if the Secretary of State considers that the provision of information
under the scheme would render compliance with some or all of the requirements
imposed by the regulations unnecessary;

92.6.b

create exceptions from requirements to publish or provide information imposed
by virtue of subsection  (1)  where information is provided under a relevant
scheme;

92.6.c

if such exceptions are created—

92.6.c.i

require a person who holds information mentioned in subsection  (1)  in
connection with the operation of a relevant scheme to provide the information
to the Secretary of State;

92.6.c.ii

permit or require the Secretary of State to publish the information.

92.7

The regulations may impose requirements on a person mentioned in subsection
(6)(c)(i)  about the retention of information mentioned there.

92.8

The provision for exceptions that may be made by the regulations includes
provision authorising the Secretary of State to grant an exception from a
requirement imposed by the regulations in a particular case, on grounds
specified in the regulations.

92.9

The regulations may provide that the disclosure of information under the
regulations does not breach—

92.9.a

an obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

92.9.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of the information (however imposed),
other than a restriction imposed by the data protection legislation.

92.10

Provision made by the regulations may, in particular, be framed by reference
to manufacturers or commercial suppliers with a specified connection to the
United Kingdom or a part of it.

92.11

In this section—

92.11.a

“ connected person ”, in relation to a manufacturer or commercial supplier,
means a person who has a connection, of a description specified in regulations
made by the Secretary of State, with the manufacturer or commercial supplier;

92.11.b

“ relevant person ” means—

92.11.b.i

a person who provides health care in the United Kingdom or a part of it,
whether or not under arrangements made by another person, or

92.11.b.ii

another person who carries on activities connected with health care provided
in the United Kingdom or a part of it and is of a description specified in
regulations made by the Secretary of State.

92.12

In this section—

      “ commercial supplier ”, in relation to a health care product, means a
person who supplies the product otherwise than in the course of providing
health care;           “ data protection legislation ” has the meaning given
by section 3(9) of the Data Protection Act 2018;           “ health care ”
means all forms of health care provided for individuals, whether relating to
physical or mental health;           “ health care product ” means a medicine,
medical device or other product which is supplied or prescribed in the course
of the provision of health care;           “ manufacturer ”, in relation to a
health care product, means a person who manufactures or assembles the product;
“ payments or other benefits ” includes any payment or other benefit—
wherever it is provided,           whether or not it is of a financial nature,
whether it is provided under a contract or otherwise, and           whether it
is provided directly or through a third party.

#### Regulations under section 92: enforcement

93

93.1

Regulations under section 92 (1)  may make provision for the enforcement of
requirements imposed by the regulations, including provision conferring on the
Secretary of State the power to impose a financial penalty on a person who,
without reasonable excuse—

93.1.a

fails to comply with such a requirement, or

93.1.b

provides information in response to such a requirement that is false or
misleading to a material extent.

93.2

The amount of the financial penalty is to be specified in, or determined in
accordance with, the regulations.

93.3

Regulations by virtue of subsection  (1)  must include provision—

93.3.a

requiring the Secretary of State, before imposing a financial penalty on a
person, to give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the
proposed financial penalty;

93.3.b

ensuring that the person is given an opportunity to make representations about
the proposed financial penalty;

93.3.c

requiring the Secretary of State, after the period for making representations,
to decide whether to impose the financial penalty;

93.3.d

requiring the Secretary of State, if the Secretary of State decides to impose
the financial penalty, to give the person notice in writing (a “final notice”)
imposing the penalty;

93.3.e

enabling a person on whom a financial penalty is imposed to appeal to a court
or tribunal in accordance with the regulations;

93.3.f

as to the powers of the court or tribunal on such an appeal.

93.4

The provision that may be made by the regulations by virtue of subsection  (1)
includes provision—

93.4.a

enabling a notice of intent or final notice to be withdrawn or amended;

93.4.b

requiring the Secretary of State to withdraw a final notice in circumstances
specified in the regulations;

93.4.c

for a financial penalty to be increased by an amount specified in or
determined in accordance with the regulations in the event of late payment;

93.4.d

as to how financial penalties are recoverable.

#### Regulations under section 92: consent

94

94.1

Before making regulations under section 92, the Secretary of State must—

94.1.a

obtain the consent of the Scottish Ministers in relation to any provision
which—

94.1.a.i

would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament, if
contained in an Act of that Parliament, and

94.1.a.ii

is not merely incidental to, or consequential on, provision which would be
outside that legislative competence;

94.1.b

obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers in relation to any provision which—

94.1.b.i

would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru, if contained in an
Act of the Senedd, and

94.1.b.ii

is not merely incidental to, or consequential on, provision which would be
outside that legislative competence;

94.1.c

obtain the consent of the Department of Health in Northern Ireland in relation
to any provision which—

94.1.c.i

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
if contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

94.1.c.ii

is not merely incidental to, or consequential on, provision which would be
outside that legislative competence.

94.2

Consent is not required under subsection  (1)(c)  in relation to any provision
if—

94.2.a

a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly containing the provision
would require the consent of the Secretary of State under section 8 of the
Northern Ireland Act 1998, and

94.2.b

the provision does not affect, other than incidentally, a transferred matter
(within the meaning of that Act).

#### Information standards

95

95.1

The Health and Social Care Act 2012 is amended as follows.

In section 250 (information standards)—

health care or of adult social care in England;

95.2.a.2B.d

any person, other than a public body, who is required to be registered under
Chapter 2 of Part 1 of the Health and Social Care Act 2008 in respect of the
carrying on of a regulated activity (within the meaning of Part 1 of that
Act).

;

95.2.b

applies to the Secretary of State.

95.2.d.6A

Any other person to whom an information standard published under this section
applies must comply with the information standard, except in so far as the
requirement to comply is waived (see subsection (6B)).

95.2.d.6B

Regulations may confer on a person who publishes an information standard the
power to waive a person’s requirement to comply with the information standard
(in whole or in part and generally or for a specific period).

95.2.d.6C

#### Sharing anonymous health and social care information

96

After section 251C of the Health and Social Care Act 2012 insert—

######## Sharing of anonymous information

######### Sharing anonymous information

96.251D

96.251D.1

A health or social care body may—

96.251D.1.a

require another health or social care body to provide information, other than
personal information, that relates only to its activities in connection with
the provision of health services or adult social care in England;

96.251D.1.b

require a private health or social care provider to provide information, other
than personal information, that relates only to its activities in connection
with the provision of health services, or adult social care in England, in
pursuance of arrangements made with a public body.

96.251D.2

A health or social care body may impose a requirement under subsection  (1)
only for purposes related to its functions in connection with the provision of
health services or adult social care in England.

96.251D.3

Regulations may create exceptions to subsection  (1) , which may be framed by
reference to specified bodies or descriptions of bodies, descriptions of
information or otherwise.

96.251D.4

Subsection  (1)  does not require a person to process information so as to
render it into a form in which it must be provided.

96.251D.5

For enforcement of requirements under subsection  (1)(b) , see section  277E .

96.251D.6

For the purposes of this section—

      “ adult social care ” has the meaning given by section 250(7);
“ health services ” has the meaning given by section 251C(6A);           “
health or social care body ” means a public body which exercises functions in
connection with the provision of health services or of adult social care in
England;           “ personal information ” means information which is in a
form that—         identifies any individual, or           enables the
identity of any individual to be ascertained;                 “ private health
or social care provider ” means a person (other than a public body) who
provides health services, or adult social care in England, pursuant to
arrangements made with a health or social care body;           “ public body ”
has the meaning given by section 250(7).

#### Collection of information about adult social care

99

In Part 9 of the Health and Social Care Act 2012, after section 277 insert—

######## Information about adult social care

######### Provision of adult social care information to Secretary of State

99.277A

99.277A.1

The Secretary of State may require a relevant provider of adult social care
services to provide the Secretary of State with information that relates to—

99.277A.1.a

the person on whom the requirement is imposed,

99.277A.1.b

their activities in connection with the provision of adult social care in
England, or

99.277A.1.c

any person to whom they have provided —

99.277A.1.c.i

adult social care in England, or

99.277A.1.c.ii

adult social care, outside England, in pursuance of arrangements made by an
English local authority.

99.277A.2

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement under subsection  (1)  only if
the information is sought for purposes connected with the health care system,
or adult social care system, in England.

99.277A.3

A requirement under subsection  (1)  may specify—

99.277A.3.a

the form and manner in which information is to be provided, and

99.277A.3.b

when information is to be provided.

99.277A.4

A requirement under subsection  (1)  must be in writing.

99.277A.5

The provision of information under this section—

99.277A.5.a

does not breach any obligation of confidence owed by the person providing it,
but

99.277A.5.b

is subject to any express restriction on disclosure imposed by any enactment
(other than a restriction which allows disclosure if authorised by an
enactment).

99.277A.6

For enforcement of requirements under subsection  (1) , see section  277E .

99.277A.7

In this section—

      “adult social care”—         includes all forms of personal care and
other practical assistance provided for individuals who, by reason of age,
illness, disability, pregnancy, childbirth, dependence on alcohol or drugs, or
any other similar circumstances, are in need of such care or other assistance,
but           does not include anything provided by an establishment or agency
for which Her Majesty’s Chief Inspector of Education, Children’s Services and
Skills is the registration authority under section 5 of the Care Standards Act
2000;                 “ English local authority ” means—         a county
council in England;           a district council for an area in England for
which there is no county council;           a London borough council;
the Common Council of the City of London (in its capacity as a local
authority);                 “ relevant provider of adult social care services
” means a person who is required to be registered under Chapter 2 of Part 1 of
the Health and Social Care Act 2008 in respect of the carrying on of a
regulated activity (within the meaning of Part 1 of that Act) involving or
connected with the provision of adult social care.

######### Restrictions on onward disclosure of information

99.277B

99.277B.1

Information provided under section  277A  may not be disclosed by the
Secretary of State except for purposes connected with the health care system,
or adult social care system, in England.

99.277B.2

Commercially sensitive information provided under section  277A  may not be
disclosed by the Secretary of State (even for the purposes mentioned in
subsection  (1) ) unless the Secretary of State considers that the disclosure
is appropriate, having taken into account the public interest as well as the
interests of the person to whom the commercially sensitive information
relates.

99.277B.3

Subsections  (1)  and  (2)  do not restrict the disclosure of information
where—

99.277B.3.a

the person to whom the information relates has consented to the disclosure,

99.277B.3.b

the information has previously been lawfully disclosed to the public,

99.277B.3.c

the disclosure is in accordance with any court order,

99.277B.3.d

the disclosure is necessary or expedient for the purposes of protecting the
welfare of any individual,

99.277B.3.e

the disclosure is made to any person in circumstances where it is necessary or
expedient for the person to have the information for the purpose of exercising
functions of that person conferred under or by virtue of any provision of this
or any other Act,

99.277B.3.f

the disclosure is in connection with the investigation of a criminal offence
(whether or not in the United Kingdom), or

99.277B.3.g

the disclosure is for the purpose of criminal proceedings (whether or not in
the United Kingdom).

99.277B.4

In this section “ commercially sensitive information ” means commercial
information whose disclosure the Secretary of State thinks might significantly
harm the legitimate business interests of the person to whom it relates.

######### Directions to certain bodies to exercise functions under this Chapter

99.277C

99.277C.1

The Secretary of State may direct the Health and Social Care Information
Centre to exercise the functions of the Secretary of State under section  277A
(and where a direction is given, section  277B  applies accordingly).

99.277C.2

The Secretary of State may direct a Special Health Authority performing
functions only or mainly in respect of England to exercise the functions of
the Secretary of State under section  277A  (and where a direction is given,
section  277B  applies accordingly).

99.277C.3

The Secretary of State may give directions to a body about the exercise of any
functions that it is directed to exercise under subsection  (1)  or  (2)
(including directions as to the processing of information that the body
obtains in exercising those functions).

######### Arrangements with third parties

99.277D

99.277D.1

The Secretary of State may make arrangements for any person prescribed by
regulations under this subsection to exercise the functions of the Secretary
of State under section  277A  (and where arrangements are made, section  277B
applies accordingly).

99.277D.2

Arrangements under subsection  (1)  may—

99.277D.2.a

provide for the Secretary of State to make payments to the person;

99.277D.2.b

make provision as to the circumstances in which any such payments are to be
repaid to the Secretary of State.

99.277D.3

Section 304(9) (differential provision) applies in relation to the power to
make arrangements under subsection  (1)  as it applies to a power of the
Secretary of State to give directions under this Act.

#### Enforcement of duties against private providers

100

100.1

100.2

After section  277D  (inserted by section 99 of this Act) insert—

########## Enforcement

########### Enforcement of provisions under this Part

100.2.277E

100.2.277E.1

Regulations may make provision conferring on the Secretary of State the power
to impose a financial penalty on a person, other than a public body, who
without reasonable excuse—

100.2.277E.1.a

fails to comply with an information standard (unless the requirement for the
person to comply has been waived by virtue of regulations under section
250(6B));

100.2.277E.1.b

fails to comply with a requirement to provide information imposed under
section 251ZA(1),  251D (1)(b) , 259(1)(a) or (aa) or  277A (1);

100.2.277E.1.c

provides information in response to such a requirement that is false or
misleading to a material extent.

100.2.277E.2

The amount of the financial penalty is to be specified in, or determined in
accordance with, the regulations.

100.2.277E.3

The regulations must include provision—

100.2.277E.3.a

requiring the Secretary of State, before imposing a financial penalty on a
person, to give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the
proposed financial penalty;

100.2.277E.3.b

ensuring that the person is given an opportunity to make representations about
the proposed financial penalty;

100.2.277E.3.c

requiring the Secretary of State, after the period for making representations,
to decide whether to impose the financial penalty;

100.2.277E.3.d

requiring the Secretary of State, if the Secretary of State decides to impose
the financial penalty, to give the person notice in writing (a “final notice”)
imposing the penalty;

100.2.277E.3.e

enabling a person on whom a financial penalty is imposed to appeal to the
First-tier Tribunal in accordance with the regulations;

100.2.277E.3.f

as to the powers of the Tribunal on such an appeal.

100.2.277E.4

The provision that may be made by the regulations includes provision—

100.2.277E.4.a

enabling a notice of intent or final notice to be withdrawn or amended;

100.2.277E.4.b

requiring the Secretary of State to withdraw a final notice in circumstances
specified in the regulations;

100.2.277E.4.c

for a financial penalty to be increased by an amount specified in or
determined in accordance with the regulations in the event of late payment;

100.2.277E.4.d

for the recovery of financial penalties in the county court.

100.2.277E.5

In this section “ public body ” has the meaning given by section 250(7).

#### Medicine information systems

101

After that Chapter insert—

########## Regulations: information systems

########### Information systems

101.3.7A

101.3.7A.1

The appropriate authority may by regulations make provision about the
establishment and operation by the Health and Social Care Information Centre
(“the Information Centre”) of one or more information systems for purposes
relating to—

101.3.7A.1.a

the safety of human medicines, including the safety of clinical decisions
relating to human medicines;

101.3.7A.1.b

the quality and efficacy of human medicines.

101.3.7A.2

The regulations may (among other things) make provision—

101.3.7A.2.a

about the information in relation to human medicines which may or must be
entered or retained in an information system established under subsection  (1)
;

101.3.7A.2.b

requiring information to be provided to the Information Centre for the
purposes of its functions under the regulations;

101.3.7A.2.c

about the use or disclosure of information contained in an information system
established under subsection  (1) ;

101.3.7A.2.d

requiring the Information Centre to have regard to specified matters in
exercising its functions under the regulations.

101.3.7A.3

The provision mentioned in subsection  (2)(a)  and  (b)  may relate to—

101.3.7A.3.a

information for specified purposes,

101.3.7A.3.b

information that the Information Centre considers it necessary or expedient to
have for the purposes of its functions under the regulations,

101.3.7A.3.c

information (including information relating to individuals) which is of a
specified description, or

101.3.7A.3.d

information (including information relating to individuals) which is of a
description set out in a direction in writing given by the appropriate
authority.

101.3.7A.4

The provision mentioned in subsection  (2)(b)  may include provision—

101.3.7A.4.a

requiring, or enabling the Information Centre to require, specified persons or
descriptions of persons to whom subsection  (5)  applies to provide
information to the Information Centre;

101.3.7A.4.b

about the manner in which, and the time at which, those persons must provide
information, or for those matters to be determined by the Information Centre;

101.3.7A.4.c

about any procedural steps the Information Centre must follow in requiring a
person to provide information to it;

101.3.7A.4.d

requiring specified persons or descriptions of persons to whom subsection  (5)
applies to record or retain information which they are, or may be, required to
provide to the Information Centre under the regulations;

101.3.7A.4.e

in relation to the enforcement of any requirement imposed by or under the
regulations.

101.3.7A.5

This subsection applies to any person who provides services, or exercises any
powers or duties, relating to—

101.3.7A.5.a

human medicines,

101.3.7A.5.b

health, or

101.3.7A.5.c

education.

101.3.7A.6

The provision mentioned in subsection  (2)(c)  may include provision about—

101.3.7A.6.a

the analysis by the Information Centre of information that is contained in an
information system (whether alone or in combination with other information)
for the purposes mentioned in subsection  (1)  or for other purposes;

101.3.7A.6.b

the publication by the Information Centre of information that is contained in
an information system or has been analysed in combination with such
information;

101.3.7A.6.c

the disclosure (other than by way of publication) of information mentioned in
paragraph  (b)  to specified persons or descriptions of persons, or for
specified purposes;

101.3.7A.6.d

the use or further disclosure by any person of information disclosed to them
under the regulations.

101.3.7A.7

Regulations conferring on the appropriate authority a power to give a
direction by virtue of subsection  (3)(d)  must —

101.3.7A.7.a

provide that the power includes power to vary or revoke the directions by a
subsequent direction, and

101.3.7A.7.b

in the case of a power exercisable in relation to Wales or Scotland, require
the Secretary of State—

101.3.7A.7.b.i

where a proposed direction relates to Wales, to consult the Welsh Ministers
before giving it, and

101.3.7A.7.b.ii

where a proposed direction relates to Scotland, to consult the Scottish
Ministers before giving it.

101.3.7A.8

Where regulations under subsection (1) include provision by virtue of
subsection (4)(a) which requires, or enables the Information Centre to
require, the provision of individual health information held for the purposes
of the health service established under section 1 of the National Health
Service (Scotland) Act 1978, the regulations must provide for the information
to be collected by the Scottish Ministers, or a person designated by them, on
behalf of the Information Centre, subject to specified exceptions.

101.3.7A.9

Regulations by virtue of subsection (8) may—

101.3.7A.9.a

confer powers or duties (including discretions) on the Scottish Ministers, a
designated person or the Information Centre;

101.3.7A.9.b

provide for powers or duties conferred on the Scottish Ministers to be treated
for the purposes of section 2 of the National Health Service (Scotland) Act
1978 as functions relating to the health service (within the meaning of that
Act).

101.3.7A.10

Where regulations under subsection (1) include provision by virtue of
subsection (4)(a) which requires, or enables the Information Centre to
require, the provision of individual health information held for the purposes
of the health service in Wales, the regulations must provide for the
information to be collected by the Welsh Ministers, or a person designated by
them, on behalf of the Information Centre, subject to specified exceptions.

101.3.7A.11

Regulations by virtue of subsection (10) may confer powers or duties
(including discretions) on the Welsh Ministers, a designated person or the
Information Centre.

101.3.7A.12

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may provide that the disclosure of
information by virtue of this section does not breach—

101.3.7A.12.a

an obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

101.3.7A.12.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of the information (however imposed),
other than a restriction imposed by the data protection legislation.

101.3.7A.13

In this section—

      “ data protection legislation ” has the meaning given by section 3(9) of
the Data Protection Act 2018;           “ health service ”, in relation to
Wales, has the meaning given by section 206(1) of the National Health Service
(Wales) Act 2006;           “ human medicine ” has the same meaning as in Part
2 (see section 9);           “ individual health information ” means
information (however recorded) which relates to—         the physical or
mental health or condition of an individual,           the diagnosis of an
individual’s condition, or           an individual’s care or treatment,
or is (to any extent) derived directly or indirectly from information relating
to any of those matters;           “ specified ” means specified in
regulations under subsection  (1) .

########### Offence of disclosing information

101.3.7B

101.3.7B.1

A person to whom information is disclosed under regulations under section  7A
(1)  commits an offence if the person uses or discloses that information in
contravention of the regulations.

101.3.7B.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

101.3.7B.2.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 51 weeks, to a fine or to both;

101.3.7B.2.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a
term not exceeding 6 months, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard
scale or to both.

101.3.7B.3

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003, the reference in subsection  (2)(a)
to 51 weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.
