authority”, after “2(1)” insert  “, 7A(1)” .

101.9

In section 47 (procedure for regulations), in subsection (2), after “2(1)”
insert  “, 7A(1)” .

101.10

In section 253 of the Health and Social Care Act 2012 (general duties of
Information Centre), after subsection (2) insert—

101.10.2A

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply in relation to the functions of the
Information Centre by virtue of the Medicines and Medical Devices Act 2021.

### Secretary of State's powers to transfer or delegate functions

#### Relevant bodies and Special Health Authorities

102

In this Part—

      “ relevant body ” means—         Health Education England,           the
Health and Social Care Information Centre,           the Health Research
Authority,           the Human Fertilisation and Embryology Authority,
the Human Tissue Authority, or           NHS England;                 “
Special Health Authority ” means a Special Health Authority established under
section 28 of the National Health Service Act 2006.

#### Power to transfer functions between bodies

103

103.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations transfer a function of a relevant
body to another relevant body.

103.2

Regulations under this section may be made only if the Secretary of State
considers that they serve the purpose of improving the exercise of public
functions, having regard to—

103.2.a

efficiency,

103.2.b

effectiveness,

103.2.c

economy, and

103.2.d

securing appropriate accountability to Ministers.

103.3

Regulations under this section may not transfer a function of NHS England if
the Secretary of State considers that to do so would make NHS England
redundant.

103.4

The provision which may be made by regulations under this section by virtue of
section 183(1)(a) includes provision—

103.4.a

modifying functions of either relevant body (see further section 105 (1) );

103.4.b

modifying the constitutional or funding arrangements of either relevant body
(see further section 105 (2)  and  (3) );

103.4.c

abolishing the relevant body from which functions are transferred, where the
Secretary of State considers that it is redundant as a result of the transfer
of functions.

103.5

Where—

103.5.a

regulations under this section contain provision for a body to exercise a
function that is exercisable in relation to Scotland, Wales or Northern
Ireland,

103.5.b

immediately before that provision takes effect, the function is exercisable by
another body whose constitutional arrangements contain provision (however
expressed) for the body to include a member whose experience, functions or
appointment are connected with that part of the United Kingdom, and

103.5.c

the Secretary of State considers that the constitutional arrangements of the
body referred to in paragraph  (a)  do not contain corresponding provision as
to membership,

the Secretary of State must make provision by virtue of section 183(1)(a)
modifying the constitutional arrangements of the body referred to in paragraph
(a)  so that they contain corresponding provision as to membership.

103.6

In this section, “ Minister ” means a Minister of the Crown (as defined by
section 8 of the Ministers of the Crown Act 1975).

#### Power to provide for exercise of functions of Secretary of State

104

104.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for a relevant body to
exercise specified functions of the Secretary of State on behalf of the
Secretary of State.

104.2

The functions that may be specified are —

104.2.a

any functions of the Secretary of State which relate to the health service in
England;

104.2.b

any other functions that the Secretary of State may provide for a Special
Health Authority to exercise.

104.3

The provision which may be made by regulations under this section by virtue of
section 183(1)(a) includes provision—

104.3.a

modifying functions of the relevant body (see further section 105 (1) );

104.3.b

modifying the constitutional or funding arrangements of the relevant body (see
further section 105 (2)  and  (3) ).

104.4

Where—

104.4.a

regulations under this section contain provision for a relevant body to
exercise a function of the Secretary of State that is exercisable in relation
to Scotland, Wales or Northern Ireland,

104.4.b

immediately before that provision takes effect, the Secretary of State’s
function is exercisable by a body whose constitutional arrangements contain
provision (however expressed) for the body to include a member whose
experience, functions or appointment are connected with that part of the
United Kingdom, and

104.4.c

the Secretary of State considers that the relevant body’s constitutional
arrangements do not contain corresponding provision as to membership,

the Secretary of State must make provision by virtue of section 183(1)(a)
modifying the relevant body’s constitutional arrangements so that they contain
corresponding provision as to membership.

104.5

Regulations under this section may make provision for determining whether and
in what circumstances the Secretary of State or a relevant body is liable for
the exercise of the specified functions by the relevant body.

104.6

The specification of a function in regulations under this section does not
preclude the Secretary of State from exercising the function.

104.7

In this section “ the health service ” has the same meaning as in the National
Health Service Act 2006 (see section 275(1) of that Act).

#### Scope of powers

105

105.1

In sections 103 and 104, references to modifying the functions of a body
include—

105.1.a

conferring a function on the body;

105.1.b

abolishing a function of the body;

105.1.c

changing the purpose or objective for which the body exercises a function;

105.1.d

changing the conditions under which the body exercises a function.

105.2

In sections 103 and 104, references to the constitutional arrangements of a
body include matters relating to—

105.2.a

the name of the body;

105.2.b

the chair of the body (including qualifications and procedures for appointment
and functions);

105.2.c

members of the body (including the number of members, qualifications and
procedures for appointment and functions);

105.2.d

staff of the body exercising functions on its behalf (including qualifications
and procedures for appointment and functions);

105.2.e

the body’s powers to employ staff;

105.2.f

governing procedures and arrangements (including the role and membership of
committees and sub-committees);

105.2.g

reports and accounts.

105.3

In sections 103 and 104, references to modifying the funding arrangements of a
body include—

105.3.a

modifying the extent to which it is funded by a Minister;

105.3.b

conferring power on the body to charge fees for the exercise of a function
(and to determine their amount).

105.4

Regulations under section 103 or 104 may repeal and re-enact (but may not
create)—

105.4.a

a power to make subordinate legislation,

105.4.b

a power of forcible entry, search or seizure,

105.4.c

a power to compel the giving of evidence, or

105.4.d

a criminal offence.

105.5

The provision which may be made by regulations under section 103 or 104 may be
made by repealing, revoking or amending provision made by or under an Act,
whenever passed or made.

105.6

The provision which may be made by regulations under section 103 or 104 by
virtue of section 183(1)(a) includes provision repealing, revoking or amending
provision made by or under any of the following, whenever passed or made—

105.6.a

an Act;

105.6.b

an Act of the Scottish Parliament;

105.6.c

a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru;

105.6.d

Northern Ireland legislation.

105.7

In this section, “ Minister ” means a Minister of the Crown (as defined by
section 8 of the Ministers of the Crown Act 1975).

#### Transfer schemes in connection with regulations

106

106.1

The Secretary of State may, in connection with regulations under section 103
or 104, make one or more schemes for the transfer of property, rights and
liabilities (“transfer schemes”).

106.2

A transfer scheme in connection with regulations under section 103 may provide
for the transfer of property, rights or liabilities to any appropriate person
from the relevant body from which functions are transferred by the
regulations.

106.3

A transfer scheme in connection with regulations under section 104 may provide
for the transfer of property, rights or liabilities to any appropriate person
from—

106.3.a

the Secretary of State,

106.3.b

a Special Health Authority, or

106.3.c

any relevant body ceasing to exercise functions of the Secretary of State as a
result of the regulations.

106.4

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

106.4.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

106.4.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

106.4.c

criminal liabilities.

106.5

A transfer scheme may—

106.5.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

106.5.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by, on behalf of or
in relation to the transferor in respect of anything transferred;

106.5.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to the transferor
in respect of anything transferred;

106.5.d

make provision for references to the transferor in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
transferee;

106.5.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

106.5.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

106.5.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

106.6

A transfer scheme may provide—

106.6.a

for modifications by agreement;

106.6.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

106.7

In subsection  (5)(f) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

106.8

For the purposes of this section—

106.8.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

106.8.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

106.9

For the purposes of subsection (8)(a)—

106.9.a

an individual who holds employment in the civil service of the State is to be
treated as employed by virtue of a contract of employment, and

106.9.b

the terms of the individual’s employment in the civil service of the State are
to be treated as constituting the terms of the contract of employment.

106.10

In this section “ appropriate person ” means—

106.10.a

any relevant body,

106.10.b

the Secretary of State,

106.10.c

an integrated care board,

106.10.d

a Special Health Authority, or

106.10.e

an NHS trust established under section 25 of the National Health Service Act
2006.

#### Transfer schemes: taxation

107

107.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision varying the way in which a
relevant tax has effect in relation to—

107.1.a

anything transferred under a scheme under section 106, or

107.1.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, a transfer under such a
scheme.

107.2

The provision which may be made under subsection  (1)(a)  includes in
particular provision for—

107.2.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything transferred;

107.2.b

anything transferred to be treated in a specified way for the purposes of a
tax provision;

107.2.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything transferred.

107.3

The provision which may be made under subsection (1)(b) includes in particular
provision for—

107.3.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything done for the purposes of or in relation to the transfer;

107.3.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer to have or
not have a specified consequence or be treated in a specified way;

107.3.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything done for the
purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer.

107.4

Regulations under this section are subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of the House of Commons.

107.5

In this section references to the transfer of property include the grant of a
lease.

107.6

In this section—

      “ relevant tax ” means income tax, corporation tax, capital gains tax,
value added tax, stamp duty or stamp duty reserve tax;           “ tax
provision ” means a provision of an enactment about a relevant tax.

#### Consent and consultation

108

108.1

Before making regulations under section 103 or 104, the Secretary of State
must—

108.1.a

obtain the consent of the Scottish Ministers in relation to any provision—

108.1.a.i

which would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament,
if contained in an Act of that Parliament, and is not merely incidental to, or
consequential on, provision which would be outside that legislative
competence, or

108.1.a.ii

which modifies the functions of the Scottish Ministers;

108.1.b

obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers in relation to any provision—

108.1.b.i

which would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru, if contained
in an Act of the Senedd, and is not merely incidental to, or consequential on,
provision which would be outside that legislative competence, or

108.1.b.ii

which modifies the functions of the Welsh Ministers;

108.1.c

obtain the consent of a Northern Ireland department in relation to any
provision—

108.1.c.i

which would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland
Assembly, if contained in an Act of that Assembly, and is not merely
incidental to, or consequential on, provision which would be outside that
legislative competence, or

108.1.c.ii

which modifies the functions of a Northern Ireland department.

108.2

Consent is not required under subsection  (1)(c)(i)  in relation to any
provision if—

108.2.a

a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly containing the provision
would require the consent of the Secretary of State under section 8 of the
Northern Ireland Act 1998, and

108.2.b

the provision does not affect, other than incidentally, a transferred matter
(within the meaning of that Act).

108.3

Before making regulations under section 103 or 104, the Secretary of State
must consult the following about a draft of the regulations—

108.3.a

any body to which the regulations relate, and

108.3.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

108.4

If, as a result of consultation under this section, it appears to the
Secretary of State appropriate to change the draft regulations, the Secretary
of State must carry out such further consultation with respect to the changes
as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

108.5

It is immaterial for the purposes of this section whether consent is obtained
or consultation is carried out before or after the commencement of this
section.

### The Health Services Safety Investigations Body

#### Introductory

##### Establishment of the HSSIB

109

109.1

A body corporate called the Health Services Safety Investigations Body is
established.

109.2

In this Part that body is referred to as “ the HSSIB ”.

109.3

Schedule 13 contains further provision about the HSSIB.

#### Investigations

##### Investigation of incidents with safety implications

110

110.1

The HSSIB has the function of investigating incidents that—

110.1.a

occur in England during the provision of health care services, and

110.1.b

have or may have implications for the safety of patients.

110.2

The purpose of the investigations is to—

110.2.a

identify risks to the safety of patients, and

110.2.b

address those risks by facilitating the improvement of systems and practices
in the provision of NHS services or other health care services in England.

110.3

In particular, where an investigation relates to an incident that did not
occur during the provision of NHS services, the HSSIB must consider whether,
in relation to any risks identified, the systems and practices in the
provision of NHS services could be improved.

110.4

The purpose of the investigations does not include assessing or determining—

110.4.a

blame,

110.4.b

civil or criminal liability, or

110.4.c

whether action needs to be taken in respect of an individual by a regulatory
body.

110.5

In this Part, an incident within subsection (1) is called a “qualifying
incident”.

##### Deciding which incidents to investigate

111

111.1

The HSSIB’s function under section 110 includes determining which qualifying
incidents it will investigate, subject to subsection  (2) .

111.2

The Secretary of State may direct the HSSIB to carry out an investigation of—

111.2.a

a particular qualifying incident that has occurred, or

111.2.b

qualifying incidents that have occurred and are of a particular description.

111.3

A direction under subsection  (2)  may specify the date by which the HSSIB
must publish its final report (see section 113).

111.4

A direction under subsection  (2) —

111.4.a

must be in writing;

111.4.b

may be varied or revoked by subsequent directions;

111.4.c

may provide for a person to exercise a discretion in dealing with any matter.

111.5

Once the HSSIB has begun an investigation into a qualifying incident, it must,
in such manner as it thinks appropriate, publish a statement which—

111.5.a

reports that it has begun the investigation,

111.5.b

contains a brief description of the incident, and

111.5.c

sets out, in general terms, the issues that the HSSIB expects to consider in
the investigation.

111.6

The HSSIB may give advance notice of a statement under subsection  (5)  to any
person the HSSIB considers may be affected by the investigation.

111.7

Where the HSSIB discontinues an investigation, it must, in such manner as it
thinks appropriate, publish a statement which—

111.7.a

reports that it has discontinued the investigation, and

111.7.b

gives its reasons for doing so.

111.8

Where the HSSIB determines not to investigate a qualifying incident, it may
give notice of its determination to any person the HSSIB considers to have an
interest in the determination.

111.9

Notice under subsection  (8)  may include—

111.9.a

a brief description of the incident, and

111.9.b

the HSSIB’s reasons for not investigating it.

##### Criteria, principles and processes

112

112.1

The HSSIB must determine and publish—

112.1.a

the criteria it will use in determining which incidents it investigates,

112.1.b

the principles which are to govern investigations,

112.1.c

the processes to be followed in carrying out investigations, and

112.1.d

the processes for ensuring that, so far as reasonable and practicable,
patients and their families are involved in investigations.

112.2

The processes determined under subsection  (1) (c)  must include—

112.2.a

the procedures and methods to be used in investigations (including in the
interviewing of persons), and

112.2.b

the time periods within which the HSSIB aims to complete investigations.

112.3

Different processes under subsection  (1) (c)  or  (d)  may be determined for
different descriptions of investigation.

112.4

Anything published under subsection (1)(d) must be—

112.4.a

easily accessible to patients and their families, and

112.4.b

capable of being easily understood by them.

112.5

The HSSIB must review the criteria, principles and processes—

112.5.a

within the period of three years beginning with their publication under
subsection  (1) , and

112.5.b

subsequently within each period of five years beginning with the completion of
the previous review.

112.6

If the HSSIB revises the criteria, principles and processes it must publish
them as revised.

112.7

In determining or revising the criteria, principles and processes the HSSIB
must consult—

112.7.a

the Secretary of State, and

112.7.b

any other persons the HSSIB considers appropriate.

#### Reports

##### Final reports

113

113.1

When the HSSIB completes an investigation, it must publish a report on the
outcome of the investigation (the “final report”).

113.2

The final report must—

113.2.a

contain a statement of findings of fact made as a result of the investigation
and an analysis of those findings,

113.2.b

make such recommendations as to the action to be taken by any person as the
HSSIB considers appropriate, and

113.2.c

set out the HSSIB’s conclusions on the matters it considered in accordance
with section 110(3) (but only if that provision is applicable to the
investigation).

113.3

The final report must focus on ascertaining risks to the safety of patients
and any recommendations as to the action to be taken by any person must focus
on addressing those risks (rather than on the activities of individuals
involved in the incident).

113.4

In particular, the final report may not include an assessment or determination
of—

113.4.a

blame,

113.4.b

civil or criminal liability, or

113.4.c

whether action needs to be taken in respect of an individual by a regulatory
body.

113.5

Information which is protected material (see section 122 (2) ) may be
disclosed in a final report if the HSSIB determines that the benefits to the
safety of patients served by the disclosure outweigh—

113.5.a

any adverse impact on current or future investigations by deterring persons
from providing information to the HSSIB, and

113.5.b

any adverse impact on securing the improvement of the safety of health care
services provided to patients in England.

113.6

The final report may not, without their consent, include the name of any
individual—

113.6.a

who has provided information to the HSSIB for the purposes of the
investigation, or

113.6.b

who was involved in the incident being investigated.

113.7

Where an investigation is carried out pursuant to a direction under section
111, the HSSIB must send a copy of the final report to the Secretary of State.

##### Interim reports

114

114.1

While the HSSIB is carrying out an investigation, it may publish a report on
any matter relating to the investigation (an “interim report”).

114.2

An interim report may—

114.2.a

contain a statement of findings of fact made as a result of the investigation
to date and an analysis of those findings,

114.2.b

make such recommendations as to the action to be taken by any person as the
HSSIB considers appropriate, and

114.2.c

set out the HSSIB’s conclusions to date on the matters it has considered in
accordance with section 110 (3) .

114.3

Subsections (3) to (7) of section 113 apply in relation to an interim report
as they apply in relation to a final report.

##### Draft reports

115

115.1

Before it publishes a final or interim report, the HSSIB—

115.1.a

must send a draft of the report to any person who the HSSIB reasonably
believes could be adversely affected by the report, and

115.1.b

may send a draft of the report to any other person who the HSSIB believes
should be sent a draft.

115.2

If a person who the HSSIB reasonably believes could have been adversely
affected by the report has died, the draft report must be sent to the person
(if any) who appears to the HSSIB to best represent the interests of the
person who has died.

115.3

The HSSIB must notify every person to whom a draft report is sent that the
person has an opportunity to comment on the draft report before the deadline
specified by the HSSIB.

115.4

If a person’s comments on a draft report are not taken into account in the
final or interim report as published, the HSSIB must explain to the person why
that is.

##### Response to reports

116

116.1

This section applies where a final or interim report includes recommendations
as to the action to be taken by any person.

116.2

The HSSIB must, in such manner as it thinks appropriate, send the report to
that person or make it available to them.

116.3

The report must specify the deadline for that person to provide a written
response.

116.4

Before that deadline, the person must respond to the HSSIB in writing setting
out the actions they propose to take in pursuance of the recommendations.

116.5

The HSSIB may publish the response.

116.6

Subsection (4) does not require a person to do anything that they could be
required to do by an Act of Senedd Cymru made without the consent of a
Minister of the Crown.

##### Admissibility of reports

117

117.1

A final report, an interim report and the draft of a final or interim report
sent to a person under section 115 are not admissible in any proceedings
within subsection (2).

117.2

Those proceedings are—

117.2.a

proceedings to determine civil or criminal liability in respect of any matter;

117.2.b

proceedings before any employment tribunal;

117.2.c

proceedings before a regulatory body (including proceedings for the purposes
of investigating an allegation);

117.2.d

proceedings to determine an appeal against a decision made in proceedings
falling within paragraphs  (a)  to  (c) .

117.3

But the High Court may order that a final or interim report is admissible in
proceedings within subsection (2) on an application by a person who is a party
to the proceedings or otherwise entitled to appear in them.

117.4

The HSSIB may make representations to the High Court about any application
under subsection  (3) .

117.5

The High Court may make an order under subsection  (3)  only if it determines
that the interests of justice served by admitting the report outweigh—

117.5.a

any adverse impact on current or future investigations by deterring persons
from providing information for the purposes of investigations, and

117.5.b

any adverse impact on securing the improvement of the safety of health care
services provided to patients in England.

#### Investigatory powers etc

##### Powers of entry, inspection and seizure

118

118.1

If an investigator considers it necessary for the purposes of an
investigation, the investigator may—

118.1.a

enter and inspect premises in England, other than premises used wholly or
mainly as a private dwelling;

118.1.b

inspect and take copies of any document at, or capable of being viewed using
equipment at, the premises;

118.1.c

inspect any equipment or other item at the premises;

118.1.d

seize and remove from the premises any document, equipment or other item
(unless that would risk the safety of any patient).

118.2

In subsection  (1) (b)  the reference to inspecting and taking copies of any
document includes requiring any document which is kept in electronic form to
be produced in a form in which it is legible and can be taken away.

118.3

Where any document, equipment or other item is seized by an investigator, or
any copy of a document is taken, it may be retained by the HSSIB for so long
as is necessary for the purposes of the investigation.

118.4

An investigator exercising any power conferred by this section must, if asked,
produce evidence of the investigator’s authority from the HSSIB to act on its
behalf.

118.5

The powers conferred by subsection (1) may be exercised in relation to
premises in which there is a Crown interest, but only if the HSSIB gives
reasonable notice to the occupier of the premises of its intention to enter
and inspect the premises.

118.6

But if the Secretary of State certifies that it appears to the Secretary of
State appropriate in the interests of national security that the powers
conferred by subsection (1)—

118.6.a

should not be exercisable in relation to any premises in which there is a
Crown interest and which are specified in the certificate, or

118.6.b

should not be exercisable in relation to any such premises which are so
specified except in circumstances specified in the certificate,

those powers are not exercisable in relation to those premises or (as the case
may be) are not exercisable except in the circumstances specified.

118.7

In this section “ Crown interest ” means—

118.7.a

an interest belonging to a government department or held in trust for Her
Majesty for the purposes of a government department;

118.7.b

an interest belonging to Her Majesty in right of the Crown;

118.7.c

an interest belonging to Her Majesty in right of the Duchy of Lancaster;

118.7.d

an interest belonging to the Duchy of Cornwall.

##### Powers to require information etc

119

119.1

An investigator may by notice require any person—

119.1.a

to attend at a specified time and place and to provide information by
answering questions;

119.1.b

to provide specified information, or information of a specified description,
by a specified date;

119.1.c

to provide specified documents, equipment or items, or documents, equipment or
items of a specified description, by a specified date.

119.2

An investigator may give a person a notice only if the investigator reasonably
believes that—

119.2.a

in the case of a requirement under subsection (1)(a), the person is able to
provide information which is necessary for the purposes of an investigation;

119.2.b

in the case of a requirement under subsection  (1) (b)—

119.2.b.i

it is necessary to obtain the information for the purposes of an
investigation, and

119.2.b.ii

the person is able to provide it;

119.2.c

in the case of a requirement under subsection (1)(c)—

119.2.c.i

it is necessary to obtain the document, equipment or other item for the
purposes of the HSSIB’s investigation function, and

119.2.c.ii

the person is able to provide it.

119.3

But a person is not required by virtue of subsection (1) to provide any
information, document, equipment or other item where—

119.3.a

its provision would risk the safety of any patient,

119.3.b

its provision might incriminate the person, or

119.3.c

in the case of information or a document, the person would be entitled to
refuse to provide it in any proceedings in any court on the grounds that it is
the subject of legal professional privilege.

119.4

A notice must—

119.4.a

specify the grounds for the investigator believing the matters in subsection
(2),

119.4.b

give an explanation of the consequences of failing to comply with the notice
(see section 121), and

119.4.c

attach evidence of the investigator’s authority from the HSSIB to exercise the
powers conferred by this section.

119.5

If a notice requires a person to provide anything which is kept in electronic
form, the notice may require it to be provided in a form in which it is
legible.

119.6

An investigator may withdraw a notice under subsection (1) by giving notice of
withdrawal to the person to whom the notice was given.

119.7

Where any document, equipment or other item is provided to an investigator
pursuant to a notice, it may be retained by the HSSIB for so long as is
necessary for the purposes of the HSSIB’s investigation function, unless its
retention would risk the safety of any patient.

119.8

Where a person attends to answer questions pursuant to a notice under
subsection (1)(a), the HSSIB—

119.8.a

must reimburse the person the reasonable costs incurred in attending;

119.8.b

may record, by any means, the answers given.

119.9

In this section “ specified ” means specified in the notice.

##### Voluntary provision of information etc

120

A person may disclose any information, document, equipment or other item to
the HSSIB if the person reasonably believes that the disclosure is necessary
for the purpose of enabling the HSSIB to carry out its investigation function.

##### Offences relating to investigations

121

121.1

A person commits an offence if the person—

121.1.a

intentionally obstructs an investigator in the performance of functions
conferred by section 118, or

121.1.b

fails without reasonable excuse to comply with a notice given under section
119.

121.2

A person commits an offence if the person provides information to the HSSIB
for the purposes of the HSSIB’s investigation function which the person knows
or suspects is false or misleading in a material respect.

121.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (2)  to
show that—

121.3.a

the person reasonably believed that the information would assist the HSSIB in
carrying out its investigation function, and

121.3.b

at the time of providing the information the person informed the HSSIB that
the person knew or suspected that it was false or misleading.

121.4

If a person charged with an offence under subsection  (2)  relies on the
defence under subsection  (3) , and evidence is adduced which is sufficient to
raise an issue with respect to that defence, the court must assume that the
defence is satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt
that it is not.

121.5

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine.

121.6

Subsections  (1) (a)  and  (5)  apply to persons in the public service of the
Crown as they apply to other persons.

#### Protection of material held by the HSSIB

##### Prohibition on disclosure of HSSIB material

122

122.1

The HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSIB, must not disclose
protected material to any person.

122.2

In this Part “ protected material ” means any information, document, equipment
or other item which—

122.2.a

is held by the HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSIB, for the
purposes of the HSSIB’s investigation function,

122.2.b

relates to a qualifying incident (whether or not investigated by the HSSIB),
and

122.2.c

has not already been lawfully made available to the public.

122.3

In this Part “ individual connected with the HSSIB ” means—

122.3.a

a member of the HSSIB,

122.3.b

a member of a committee or sub-committee of the HSSIB,

122.3.c

an investigator, or

122.3.d

an individual (other than an investigator) who works for the HSSIB.

122.4

For the purposes of subsection (3)(d) an individual “works for” the HSSIB if
the individual works—

122.4.a

under a contract of employment with the HSSIB,

122.4.b

under a contract of apprenticeship with the HSSIB,

122.4.c

under a contract under which the individual undertakes to do or perform
personally any work or services for the HSSIB, or

122.4.d

as an agency worker within the meaning of the Agency Workers Regulations 2010
( S.I. 2010/93 ) in circumstances where the HSSIB is the hirer within the
meaning of those Regulations.

122.5

An individual who was, but has ceased to be, connected with the HSSIB must not
disclose to any person, other than the HSSIB or an individual connected with
the HSSIB, any information, document, equipment or other item held by that
individual—

122.5.a

which the individual obtained because they were connected with the HSSIB,

122.5.b

which, at the time they ceased to be connected with the HSSIB, was protected
material, and

122.5.c

which has not already been lawfully made available to the public.

##### Exceptions to prohibition on disclosure

123

123.1

Section 122(1) does not apply to a disclosure which is required or authorised
by—

123.1.a

Schedule 14,

123.1.b

any other provision of this Part, or

123.1.c

regulations made by the Secretary of State.

123.2

Regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may, for example, require or authorise
disclosures of protected material by reference to—

123.2.a

the kind of material that it is (for example, a particular kind of equipment),

123.2.b

the matters to which it relates,

123.2.c

the person from whom it was obtained,

123.2.d

the purpose for which it was produced or is held, or

123.2.e

the purpose for which it is disclosed.

123.3

But regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may not require or authorise
disclosures of protected material by reference to the qualifying incident to
which the material relates.

123.4

Regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may provide for a person to exercise a
discretion in dealing with any matter.

123.5

Subject to subsection  (6) , regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may
provide that disclosures which are required or authorised by the regulations
do not breach—

123.5.a

obligations of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

123.5.b

any other restrictions on disclosure.

123.6

Nothing in regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  operates to require or
authorise disclosures which would contravene the data protection legislation
(but, for the purposes of this subsection, in determining whether any
disclosure required or authorised by the regulations would do so, take the
requirement or authorisation into account).

##### Offences of unlawful disclosure

124

124.1

A person commits an offence if the person—

124.1.a

breaches the prohibition in section 122 (1)  by knowingly or recklessly
disclosing protected material to another person, and

124.1.b

knows or suspects that the disclosure is prohibited.

124.2

An individual who was, but has ceased to be, connected with the HSSIB commits
an offence if the individual—

124.2.a

breaches the prohibition in section 122(5) by knowingly or recklessly
disclosing any information, document, equipment or other thing to another
person, and

124.2.b

knows or suspects that the disclosure is prohibited.

124.3

Subsection (4) applies where protected material is disclosed to a person not
connected with the HSSIB—

124.3.a

in a draft report sent to the person under section 115(1),

124.3.b

under paragraph 2, 3 or 4 of Schedule 14 (disclosures for purposes of an
investigation, offence or safety risk), or

124.3.c

under regulations under section 123(1)(c).

124.4

The person not connected with the HSSIB to whom protected material is
disclosed as specified in subsection (3) commits an offence if the person—

124.4.a

knowingly or recklessly discloses the protected material to another person
without reasonable excuse, and

124.4.b

knows or suspects that it is protected material.

124.5

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine.

##### Restriction of statutory powers requiring disclosure

125

125.1

A power under any enactment (whenever passed or made) other than this Part to
require the disclosure of, or to seize, any information, document, equipment
or other item may not be used—

125.1.a

to require the disclosure of protected material by the HSSIB, or

125.1.b

to seize protected material from the HSSIB.

125.2

Subsection  (1)  applies to a power to require disclosure, or to seize,
however it is expressed (and, for example, it applies if the power is to
require a person to give, supply, furnish or produce any information,
document, equipment or other item).

125.3

Subsection (1) does not apply to a power to the extent that the provision
conferring it is within the legislative competence of a devolved legislature.

125.4

A provision is within the legislative competence of a devolved legislature if—

125.4.a

it would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if it
were contained in an Act of that Parliament;

125.4.b

it would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if it were
contained in an Act of the Senedd (including any provision that could only be
made with the consent of a Minister of the Crown);

125.4.c

the provision—

125.4.c.i

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

125.4.c.ii

would not, if contained in a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
result in the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State under
section 8 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998.

125.5

In this section “ enactment ” includes an enactment comprised in subordinate
legislation within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978.

125.6

References to the HSSIB in subsection  (1)  include—

125.6.a

an individual connected with the HSSIB, and

125.6.b

an individual who was, but has ceased to be, connected with the HSSIB.

#### Relationship with other bodies

##### Co-operation

126

126.1

This section applies where—

126.1.a

the HSSIB is carrying out an investigation into a qualifying incident, and

126.1.b

a listed person is also carrying out an investigation into the same or a
related incident.

126.2

The HSSIB and the listed person must co-operate with each other regarding
practical arrangements for co-ordinating those investigations.

126.3

The following are listed persons—

126.3.a

an NHS foundation trust, an NHS trust or any other person providing NHS
services;

126.3.b

NHS England;

126.3.c

an integrated care board;

126.3.d

a Special Health Authority;

126.3.e

the Care Quality Commission;

126.3.f

the Health Research Authority;

126.3.g

the Human Tissue Authority;

126.3.h

the Human Fertilisation and Embryology Authority;

126.3.i

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

126.3.j

the Health Service Commissioner for England;

126.3.k

the Parliamentary Commissioner for Administration;

126.3.l

any regulatory body;

126.3.m

the Health and Safety Executive;

126.3.n

the Commissioner for Patient Safety.

126.4

The HSSIB must publish guidance about when a qualifying incident is to be
regarded as related to another incident for the purposes of this section.

126.5

If the HSSIB revises the guidance the HSSIB must publish it as revised.

##### Assistance of NHS bodies

127

127.1

The HSSIB must comply with—

127.1.a

any request by a relevant NHS body to provide it with assistance in connection
with the carrying out of investigations into incidents occurring during the
provision of NHS services or occurring at premises at which NHS services are
provided;

127.1.b

any request by NHS England to provide any other relevant NHS body with such
assistance;

127.1.c

any request by the Secretary of State to provide a relevant NHS body with such
assistance.

127.2

In subsection  (1)  “ relevant NHS body ” means—

127.2.a

an NHS foundation trust;

127.2.b

an NHS trust;

127.2.c

NHS England;

127.2.d

an integrated care board.

127.3

For the purposes of this section giving assistance includes—

127.3.a

disseminating information about best practice,

127.3.b

developing standards to be adopted, and

127.3.c

giving advice, guidance or training.

127.4

Subsection  (1)  does not apply if—

127.4.a

the assistance requested is giving advice, guidance or training, and

127.4.b

the HSSIB determines that it is impracticable for it to give the assistance.

127.5

The HSSIB may give assistance to a person other than a relevant NHS body in
relation to any matter connected with the carrying out of investigations if
the HSSIB has been requested to provide the assistance by the person to whom
it is to be given.

127.6

But the HSSIB may give assistance under subsection  (5)  only to the extent
that the assistance does not to any significant extent interfere with the
exercise by the HSSIB of its investigation function.

127.7

The activities which the HSSIB may carry out in, or in connection with, giving
assistance under subsection  (5)  are not restricted to activities carried out
in the United Kingdom.

127.8

The HSSIB may impose charges for or in connection with giving assistance under
subsection  (5) .

127.9

Charges under subsection  (8)  may be calculated on the basis that the HSSIB
considers to be the appropriate commercial basis.

##### Investigations relating to Wales and Northern Ireland

128

128.1

The HSSIB may enter into an agreement with any person for the HSSIB to carry
out an investigation falling within subsection (2).

128.2

An investigation falls within this subsection if—

128.2.a

it is an investigation into one or more incidents that have occurred, or are
occurring, in the United Kingdom—

128.2.a.i

during the provision of any of the services mentioned in subsection  (3) , or

128.2.a.ii

at premises at which any of those services are, or were, provided,

128.2.b

the incident or incidents have or may have implications for the safety of
persons for whom those services are provided,

128.2.c

the investigation is carried out for the purpose of identifying risks to the
safety of such persons and addressing those risks by facilitating the
improvement of systems and practices in the provision of any of the services
mentioned in subsection  (3) , and

128.2.d

the investigation does not involve the assessment or determination of blame or
civil or criminal liability.

128.3

The services referred to in subsection (2) are—

128.3.a

services provided for the purposes of the health service continued under
section 1(1) of the National Health Service (Wales) Act 2006, and

128.3.b

health care, within the meaning of the Health and Social Care (Reform) Act
(Northern Ireland) 2009, provided for the purposes of the system promoted
under section 2(1) of that Act.

128.4

The HSSIB may impose charges for providing services under an agreement under
subsection  (1) .

128.5

Those charges must not exceed the costs incurred by the HSSIB in providing the
services.

128.6

The HSSIB may enter into an agreement under subsection  (1)  only if it
considers that the provision of the services under the agreement will not to
any significant extent interfere with the exercise by the HSSIB of its
investigation function.

#### Oversight of functions

##### Failure to exercise functions

129

129.1

This section applies if the Secretary of State considers that—

129.1.a

the HSSIB is failing or has failed to exercise any of its functions, and

129.1.b

the failure is significant.

129.2

The Secretary of State may direct the HSSIB to exercise such of its functions,
in such manner and within such period, as the direction specifies.

129.3

But the Secretary of State may not give a direction under subsection  (2)
which directs the outcome of a particular investigation.

129.4

If the HSSIB fails to comply with a direction under subsection  (2) , the
Secretary of State may—

129.4.a

exercise the functions specified in the direction, or

129.4.b

make arrangements for some other person to exercise them on the Secretary of
State’s behalf.

129.5

The reference in subsection  (1) (a)  to exercising a function includes a
reference to exercising it properly.

129.6

A direction under subsection  (2) —

129.6.a

must be in writing;

129.6.b

may be varied or revoked by subsequent directions.

##### Review

130

130.1

Before the end of the period mentioned in subsection  (2) , the Secretary of
State must—

130.1.a

review the effectiveness of the exercise by the HSSIB of its investigation
function,

130.1.b

prepare and publish a report of the review, and

130.1.c

lay the report before Parliament.

130.2

The period is four years beginning with the day on which section 110 comes
into force.

#### Offences: supplementary

##### Offences by bodies corporate

131

131.1

Where an offence under this Part is committed by a body corporate and is
proved—

131.1.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
body corporate, or

131.1.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer of the body
corporate,

the officer (as well as the body corporate) commits the offence and is liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

131.2

In subsection  (1)  “ officer ”, in relation to a body corporate, means—

131.2.a

a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer, or

131.2.b

any person purporting to act in any such capacity.

In paragraph  (a)  “ director ”, in relation to a body corporate whose affairs
are managed by its members, means a member of the body corporate.

##### Offences by partnerships

132

132.1

Proceedings for an offence alleged to have been committed by a partnership may
be brought in the name of the partnership.

132.2

Rules of court relating to the service of documents have effect in relation to
proceedings for an offence as if the partnership were a body corporate.

132.3

For the purposes of such proceedings Schedule 3 to the Magistrates’ Courts Act
1980 applies as it applies in relation to a body corporate.

132.4

A fine imposed on a partnership on its conviction for an offence must be paid
out of the partnership assets.

132.5

Where an offence is committed by a partnership and is proved—

132.5.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

132.5.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of a partner,

the partner (as well as the partnership) commits the offence and is liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

132.6

In this section—

      “ offence ” means an offence under this Part;           “ partner ”
includes a person purporting to act as a partner.

#### Supplementary

##### Obligations of confidence etc

133

133.1

Subject to subsection (2), a disclosure of any information, document,
equipment or other item which is required or authorised by or under section
119 or 120 or Schedule 14 does not breach—

133.1.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

133.1.b

any other restriction on disclosure.

133.2

Nothing in this Part operates to require or authorise a disclosure of
information which would contravene the data protection legislation (but, for
the purposes of this subsection, in determining whether a disclosure required
or authorised by or under this Part would do so, take the requirement or
authorisation into account).

##### Consequential amendments relating to Part 4

134

Schedule 15 contains amendments consequential on this Part.

##### Interpretation of Part 4

135

In this Part—

      “ the 2006 Act ” means the National Health Service Act 2006;           “
Chief Investigator ” means the person appointed in accordance with paragraph
3  of Schedule 13;           “ data protection legislation ” has the same
meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);
to “ disclose ”, in relation to information, documents, equipment and other
items includes to permit access to such things;           “ documents ”
includes personal and medical records;           “ final report ” means a
report under section 113;           “ health care services ” means—
all forms of health care services provided for individuals, whether relating
to physical or mental health, and           procedures that are similar to
forms of medical or surgical care but are not provided in connection with a
medical condition;                 “ the HSSIB ” has the meaning given by
section 109 (2) ;           “ interim report ” means a report under section
114;           “investigation”, except in the case of an investigation
mentioned in section 126(1)(b), 127 or 128, means an investigation carried out
by the HSSIB under section 110(1) and any related term is to be read
accordingly;           the “investigation function” of the HSSIB is its
function under section 110(1) (and see also section 111(1));           “
investigator ” means a person authorised by the HSSIB to carry out functions
in relation to investigations on its behalf;           “ Minister of the Crown
” has the same meaning as in the Ministers of the Crown Act 1975;           “
NHS foundation trust ” has the meaning given by section 30 of the 2006 Act;
“ NHS services ” means health care services provided in England for the
purposes of the health service continued under section 1(1) of the 2006 Act;
“ NHS trust ” means a National Health Service trust established under section
25 of the 2006 Act;           “ notice ” means notice in writing;           “
patients ” means individuals for whom health care services are provided;
“ premises ” includes a vehicle;           “ protected material ” has the
meaning given by section 122(2);           “ qualifying incident ” has the
meaning given by section 110(5);           “ regulatory body ” means—
the General Medical Council,           the General Dental Council,
the General Optical Council,           the General Osteopathic Council,
the General Chiropractic Council,           the General Pharmaceutical
Council,           the Nursing and Midwifery Council,           the Health and
Care Professions Council, or           any other regulatory body, within the
meaning of Schedule 3 to the Health Act 1999, established at any time by an
Order in Council under section 60 of that Act;                 “ Special
Health Authority ” means a Special Health Authority established under section
28 of the 2006 Act.

### Virginity testing and hymenoplasty offences

#### Virginity testing offences

##### Virginity testing offences: England and Wales

###### Offence of virginity testing: England and Wales

136

136.1

It is an offence under the law of England and Wales for a person to carry out
virginity testing.

136.2

“ Virginity testing ” means the examination of female genitalia, with or
without consent, for the purpose (or purported purpose) of determining
virginity.

136.3

An offence is committed under subsection  (1)  only if the person—

136.3.a

is in England and Wales, or

136.3.b

is outside the United Kingdom, and is a United Kingdom national or habitually
resident in England and Wales.

136.4

“ United Kingdom national ” means an individual who is—

136.4.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

136.4.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

136.4.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

136.5

In subsection  (2) , “ female genitalia ” means a vagina or vulva.

###### Offence of offering to carry out virginity testing: England and Wales

137

137.1

It is an offence under the law of England and Wales—

137.1.a

for a person in England and Wales to offer to carry out virginity testing in
the United Kingdom or virginity testing that has a sufficient jurisdictional
connection, or

137.1.b

for a person anywhere to offer to carry out virginity testing if the person is
a United Kingdom national or habitually resident in England and Wales.

137.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection for the purposes
of subsection (1)(a) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

137.2.a

a United Kingdom national, or

137.2.b

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

137.3

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 136(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 136(2).

###### Offence of aiding or abetting etc a person to carry out virginity testing: England and Wales

138

138.1

It is an offence under the law of England and Wales for a person who is in
England and Wales, or for a person who is outside England and Wales but who is
a United Kingdom national or habitually resident in England and Wales, to aid,
abet, counsel or procure the carrying out of virginity testing that has a
sufficient jurisdictional connection.

138.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection for the purposes
of subsection (1) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

138.2.a

in the United Kingdom,

138.2.b

a United Kingdom national, or

138.2.c

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

138.3

This section does not affect the application to an offence under section 136
of any rule of law relating to aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring.

138.4

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 136(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 136(2).

###### Virginity testing offences in England and Wales: penalties

139

139.1

A person who commits an offence under section 136, 137 or 138 is liable—

139.1.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

139.1.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

139.2

In subsection  (1)(a)  “ the maximum summary term for either-way offences ”
means—

139.2.a

in relation to an offence committed before the time when paragraph 24(2) of
Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act 2020 comes into force, 6 months;

139.2.b

in relation to an offence committed after that time, 12 months.

##### Virginity testing offences: Scotland

###### Offence of virginity testing: Scotland

140

140.1

It is an offence under the law of Scotland for a person to carry out virginity
testing.

140.2

“ Virginity testing ” means the examination of female genitalia, with or
without consent, for the purpose (or purported purpose) of determining
virginity.

140.3

An offence is committed under subsection  (1)  only if the person—

140.3.a

is in Scotland, or

140.3.b

is outside the United Kingdom, and is a United Kingdom national or habitually
resident in Scotland.

140.4

“ United Kingdom national ” means an individual who is—

140.4.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

140.4.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

140.4.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

140.5

In subsection  (2) , “ female genitalia ” means a vagina or vulva.

###### Offence of offering to carry out virginity testing: Scotland

141

141.1

It is an offence under the law of Scotland—

141.1.a

for a person in Scotland to offer to carry out virginity testing in the United
Kingdom or virginity testing that has a sufficient jurisdictional connection,
or

141.1.b

for a person anywhere to offer to carry out virginity testing if the person is
a United Kingdom national or habitually resident in Scotland.

141.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection for the purposes
of subsection (1)(a) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

141.2.a

a United Kingdom national, or

141.2.b

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

141.3

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 140(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 140(2).

###### Offence of aiding or abetting etc a person to carry out virginity testing: Scotland

142

142.1

It is an offence under the law of Scotland for a person who is in Scotland, or
for a person who is outside Scotland but who is a United Kingdom national or
habitually resident in Scotland, to aid, abet, counsel, procure or incite the
carrying out of virginity testing that has a sufficient jurisdictional
connection.

142.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection for the purposes
of subsection (1) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

142.2.a

in the United Kingdom,

142.2.b

a United Kingdom national, or

142.2.c

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

142.3

This section does not affect the application to an offence under section 140
of any rule of law relating to aiding, abetting, counselling, procuring or
inciting.

142.4

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 140(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 140 (2) .

###### Virginity testing offences in Scotland: penalties and supplementary

143

143.1

A person who commits an offence under section 140, 141 or 142 is liable—

143.1.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

143.1.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

143.2

Where a person outside Scotland commits an offence under section 140, 142 or
143 the person may be prosecuted, tried and punished for the offence—

143.2.a

in a sheriff court district in which the person is apprehended or in custody,
or

143.2.b

in a sheriff court district determined by the Lord Advocate,

as if the offence had been committed in that district.

143.3

Where subsection  (2)  applies, the offence is, for all purposes incidental to
or consequential on the trial and punishment, deemed to have been committed in
that district.

143.4

In this section “ sheriff court district ” is to be construed in accordance
with section 307(1) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995
(interpretation).

##### Virginity testing offences: Northern Ireland

###### Offence of virginity testing: Northern Ireland

144

144.1

It is an offence under the law of Northern Ireland for a person to carry out
virginity testing.

144.2

“ Virginity testing ” means the examination of female genitalia, with or
without consent, for the purpose (or purported purpose) of determining
virginity.

144.3

An offence is committed under subsection  (1)  only if the person—

144.3.a

is in Northern Ireland, or

144.3.b

is outside the United Kingdom, and is a United Kingdom national or habitually
resident in Northern Ireland.

144.4

“ United Kingdom national ” means an individual who is—

144.4.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

144.4.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

144.4.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

144.5

In subsection  (2) , “ female genitalia ” means a vagina or vulva.

###### Offence of offering to carry out virginity testing: Northern Ireland

145

145.1

It is an offence under the law of Northern Ireland—

145.1.a

for a person in Northern Ireland to offer to carry out virginity testing in
the United Kingdom or virginity testing that has a sufficient jurisdictional
connection, or

145.1.b

for a person anywhere to offer to carry out virginity testing if the person is
a United Kingdom national or habitually resident in Northern Ireland.

145.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection for the purposes
of subsection (1)(a) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

145.2.a

a United Kingdom national, or

145.2.b

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

145.3

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 144(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 144 (2) .

###### Offence of aiding or abetting etc a person to carry out virginity testing: Northern Ireland

146

146.1

It is an offence under the law of Northern Ireland for a person who is in
Northern Ireland, or for a person who is outside Northern Ireland but who is a
United Kingdom national or habitually resident in Northern Ireland, to aid,
abet, counsel or procure the carrying out of virginity testing that has a
sufficient jurisdictional connection.

146.2

Virginity testing has a sufficient jurisdictional connection fr the purposes
of subsection (1) if it is carried out in relation to a person who is—

146.2.a

in the United Kingdom,

146.2.b

a United Kingdom national, or

146.2.c

habitually resident in the United Kingdom.

146.3

This section does not affect the application to an offence under section 144
of any rule of law relating to aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring.

146.4

In this section—

      “ United Kingdom national ” has the meaning given by section 144(4);
“ virginity testing ” has the meaning given by section 144 (2) .

###### Virginity testing offences in Northern Ireland: penalties

147

A person who commits an offence under section 144, 145 or 146 is liable—

147.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

147.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

###### Hymenoplasty offences in England and Wales: penalties

151

151.1

A person who commits an offence under section 148, 149 or 150 is liable—

151.1.a

summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

151.1.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

151.2

In subsection  (1)(a)  “ the maximum summary term for either-way offences ”
means—

151.2.a

in relation to an offence committed before the time when paragraph 24(2) of
Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act 2020 comes into force, 6 months;

151.2.b

in relation to an offence committed after that time, 12 months.

### Miscellaneous

#### Pharmaceutical services

##### Pharmaceutical services: remuneration in respect of vaccines etc

161

161.1

In section 164 of the National Health Service Act 2006 (remuneration for
persons providing pharmaceutical services)—

161.1.a

in subsection (8A) for “special medicinal products” substitute

any of the following—

161.1.a.a

drugs or medicines used for vaccinating or immunising people against disease,

161.1.a.b

anything used in connection with the supply or administration of drugs or
medicines within paragraph  (a) ,

161.1.a.c

drugs or medicines, not within paragraph  (a) , that are used for preventing
or treating a disease that, at the time the regulations are made, the
Secretary of State considers to be a pandemic disease or at risk of becoming a
pandemic disease,

161.1.a.d

anything used in connection with the supply or administration of drugs or
medicines within paragraph  (c) , or

161.1.a.e

a product which is a special medicinal product for the purposes of regulation
167 of the Human Medicines Regulations 2012 ( S.I. 2012/1916 ).

;

161.1.b

in subsection (8D)—

161.1.b.i

for “special medicinal products are” substitute  “anything within subsection
(8A) (a)  to  (e)  is” ;

161.1.b.ii

in paragraph (b), for “special medicinal products” substitute  “that thing,” ;

161.1.c

in subsection (8E), omit the definition of “special medicinal product”;

161.1.d

after subsection (8E) insert—

161.1.d.8F

Where regulations include provision made in reliance on subsection (8A)(c) or
(d) and the Secretary of State considers that the disease to which it relates
is no longer a pandemic disease or at risk of becoming a pandemic disease, the
Secretary of State must revoke that provision within such period as the
Secretary of State considers reasonable (taking into account, in particular,
the need for any transitional arrangements).

161.2

In section 88 of the National Health Service (Wales) Act 2006 (remuneration
for persons providing pharmaceutical services)—

161.2.a

in subsection (8A) for “special medicinal products” substitute

any of the following—

161.2.a.a

drugs or medicines used for vaccinating or immunising people against disease,

161.2.a.b

anything used in connection with the supply or administration of drugs or
medicines within paragraph  (a) ,

161.2.a.c

drugs or medicines, not within paragraph  (a) , that are used for preventing
or treating a disease that, at the time the regulations are made, the Welsh
Ministers consider to be a pandemic disease or at risk of becoming a pandemic
disease,

161.2.a.d

anything used in connection with the supply or administration of drugs or
medicines within paragraph  (c) , or

161.2.a.e

a product which is a special medicinal product for the purposes of regulation
167 of the Human Medicines Regulations 2012 ( S.I. 2012/1916 )

;

161.2.b

in subsection (8D)—

161.2.b.i

for “special medicinal products are” substitute  “anything within subsection
(8A) (a)  to  (e)  is” ;

161.2.b.ii

in paragraph (b), for “special medicinal products” substitute  “that thing,” ;

161.2.c

in subsection (8E), omit the definition of “special medicinal product”;

161.2.d

after subsection (8E) insert—

161.2.d.8F

Where regulations include provision made in reliance on subsection (8A)(c) or
(d) and the Welsh Ministers consider that the disease to which it relates is
no longer a pandemic disease or at risk of becoming a pandemic disease, the
Welsh Ministers must revoke that provision within such period as the Welsh
Ministers consider reasonable (taking into account, in particular, the need
for any transitional arrangements).

#### International healthcare

##### International healthcare arrangements

162

162.1

The Healthcare (European Economic Area and Switzerland Arrangements) Act 2019
is renamed the Healthcare (International Arrangements) Act 2019.

162.2

That Act is amended as follows.

162.3

Omit section 1 (power to make healthcare payments).

162.4

For section 2 substitute—

########### Healthcare agreements and payments

162.4.2

162.4.2.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for the purpose of
giving effect to a healthcare agreement (including provision about payments).

162.4.2.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising the
Secretary of State to make a payment (otherwise than under a healthcare
agreement) in respect of healthcare provided in a relevant country or
territory, but only where the Secretary of State considers that exceptional
circumstances justify the payment.

162.4.2.3

In subsection  (2)  “ relevant country or territory ” means a country or
territory, outside the United Kingdom, in respect of which there is a
healthcare agreement.

162.4.2.4

Regulations under this section may include provision about administrative
arrangements (including provision about evidential requirements).

162.4.2.5

Regulations under this section may—

162.4.2.5.a

confer functions on a relevant public authority or a Scottish or Welsh health
board (including discretions);

162.4.2.5.b

provide for the delegation of functions to a relevant public authority or a
Scottish or Welsh health board.

162.4.2.6

The Secretary of State may give directions to a person about the exercise of
any functions exercisable by the person under regulations made by virtue of
subsection  (5)  (and may vary or revoke any such directions).

162.4.2.7

In this section “ relevant public authority ” means a person who exercises
functions of a public nature other than—

162.4.2.7.a

the Scottish Ministers,

162.4.2.7.b

a Scottish public authority with mixed functions or no reserved functions
(within the meaning of the Scotland Act 1998),

162.4.2.7.c

the Welsh Ministers,

162.4.2.7.d

a devolved Welsh authority as defined by section 157A of the Government of
Wales Act 2006,

162.4.2.7.e

a Northern Ireland department, or

162.4.2.7.f

any other person whose functions—

162.4.2.7.f.i

are exercisable only or mainly in or as regards Northern Ireland, and

162.4.2.7.f.ii

relate only or mainly to transferred matters within the meaning of the
Northern Ireland Act 1998.

162.4.2.8

In this section—

      “ Scottish health board ” means a Health Board established under section
2(1)(a) of the National Health Service (Scotland) Act 1978;           “ Welsh
health board ” means a Local Health Board established under section 11 of the
National Health Service (Wales) Act 2006.

########### Healthcare agreements and payments: powers of devolved authorities

162.4.2A

162.4.2A.1

A devolved authority may by regulations make provision for the purpose of
giving effect to a healthcare agreement (including provision about payments).

162.4.2A.2

No provision may be made by a devolved authority under subsection (1) unless
the provision is within the devolved competence of that devolved authority
(and any applicable consent requirement under section 2B has been complied
with).

162.4.2A.3

In this section “ devolved authority ” means the Scottish Ministers, the Welsh
Ministers or a Northern Ireland department.

162.4.2A.4

For the purposes of this section—

162.4.2A.4.a

provision is within the devolved competence of the Scottish Ministers if it
would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if it
were contained in an Act of that Parliament;

162.4.2A.4.b

provision is within the devolved competence of the Welsh Ministers if it would
be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if it were contained in
an Act of Senedd Cymru (including any provision that could only be made with
the consent of a Minister of the Crown);

162.4.2A.4.c

provision is within the devolved competence of a Northern Ireland department
if it would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland
Assembly if it were contained in an Act of that Assembly.

162.4.2A.5

Regulations under this section may include provision about administrative
arrangements (including provision about evidential requirements).

162.4.2A.6

Regulations under this section may—

162.4.2A.6.a

confer functions on a public authority (including discretions);

162.4.2A.6.b

provide for the delegation of functions to a public authority.

162.4.2A.7

A devolved authority may give directions to a person about the exercise of any
functions exercisable by the person under regulations made by that devolved
authority by virtue of subsection  (6)  (and may vary or revoke any such
directions).

162.4.2A.8

In this section “ public authority ” means a person who exercises functions of
a public nature.

########### Regulations under section 2A: consent requirements

162.4.2B

162.4.2B.1

The consent of a Minister of the Crown is required before any provision is
made by the Welsh Ministers in regulations under section 2A(1) so far as that
provision, if contained in an Act of Senedd Cymru, would require the consent
of a Minister of the Crown.

162.4.2B.2

The consent of the Secretary of State is required before any provision is made
by a Northern Ireland department in regulations under section 2A(1) so far as
that provision, if contained in a Bill in the Northern Ireland Assembly, would
require the consent of the Secretary of State.

162.5

In section 3 (meaning of “ healthcare ” and “ healthcare agreement ”), for the
definition of “healthcare agreement” substitute—

      “ healthcare agreement ” means an agreement or other commitment between
the United Kingdom and either a country or territory outside the United
Kingdom or an international organisation, concerning healthcare provided
anywhere in the world;

.

162.6

In section 7 (regulations and directions)—

162.a

in subsection (1), after “A power” insert  “of the Secretary of State or Welsh
Ministers” ;

162.b

after subsection (1) insert—

162.b.1A

A power of a Northern Ireland department to make regulations under section 2A
is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of the Statutory Rules
(Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12) ).

;

162.c

for subsection (4) substitute—

162.c.4

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Act may not be made
by the Secretary of State unless a draft of the instrument has been laid
before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

;

162.d

omit subsection (5);

162.e

after subsection (5) insert—

162.e.5A

Regulations made by the Scottish Ministers under section 2A are subject to the
affirmative procedure (see Part 2 of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform
(Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 10) ).

162.e.5B

A statutory instrument containing regulations under section 2A may not be made
by the Welsh Ministers unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before
and approved by a resolution of Senedd Cymru.

162.e.5C

Regulations may not be made by a Northern Ireland department under section 2A
unless a draft of the regulations has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of the Northern Ireland Assembly.

162.7

In section 8 (short title etc), in subsection (3), for “Healthcare (European
Economic Area and Switzerland Arrangements) Act 2019” substitute  “Healthcare
(International Arrangements) Act 2019” .

#### Social care

##### Regulation of local authority functions relating to adult social care

163

163.1

Chapter 3 of Part 1 of the Health and Social Care Act 2008 (quality of health
and social care) is amended as follows.

163.2

In section 46 (reviews and performance assessments by the Care Quality
Commission), in the heading, at the end insert  “: registered service
providers” .

163.3

After section 46 insert—

########### Reviews and performance assessments: local authorities

163.3.46A

163.3.46A.1

The Commission must, in accordance with this section—

163.3.46A.1.a

conduct reviews of the exercise of regulated care functions by English local
authorities,

163.3.46A.1.b

assess the performance of those authorities following each such review, and

163.3.46A.1.c

publish a report of its assessment.

163.3.46A.2

In this section “ regulated care functions ” means such functions under Part 1
of the Care Act 2014 (functions relating to adult social care in England) as
may be prescribed.

163.3.46A.3

Regulations under subsection  (2)  may prescribe—

163.3.46A.3.a

all functions of English local authorities under Part 1 of the Care Act 2014
or some of their functions under that Part;

163.3.46A.3.b

the whole of a function or a particular aspect of it.

163.3.46A.4

The Secretary of State—

163.3.46A.4.a

must set, and may from time to time revise, objectives and priorities for the
Commission in relation to the assessment under this section of the performance
of English local authorities, and

163.3.46A.4.b

must inform the Commission of the objectives and priorities.

163.3.46A.5

The Commission—

163.3.46A.5.a

must determine, and may from time to time revise, indicators of quality for
the purposes of the assessment under this section of the performance of
English local authorities, and

163.3.46A.5.b

must obtain the approval of the Secretary of State in relation to the
indicators.

163.3.46A.6

The Secretary of State may direct the Commission to revise the indicators
under subsection  (5) .

163.3.46A.7

Different objectives and priorities may be set, and different indicators of
quality may be determined, for different cases.

163.3.46A.8

The Commission—

163.3.46A.8.a

must prepare, and may from time to time revise, a statement—

163.3.46A.8.a.i

setting out the frequency with which reviews under this section are to be
conducted and the period to which they are to relate, and

163.3.46A.8.a.ii

describing the method that it proposes to use in assessing and evaluating the
performance of a English local authority under this section, and

163.3.46A.8.b

must obtain the approval of the Secretary of State in relation to the
statement.

163.3.46A.9

The Secretary of State may direct the Commission to revise the statement under
subsection  (8) .

163.3.46A.10

The statement may—

163.3.46A.10.a

make different provision about frequency and period of reviews for different
cases, and

163.3.46A.10.b

describe different methods for different cases.

163.3.46A.11
