164.3

After section 72 insert—

########### Default by local authority

############ Default power of Secretary of State

164.3.72A

164.3.72A.1

Where the Secretary of State is satisfied that a local authority is failing,
or has failed, to discharge any of its functions under or by virtue of this
Part to an acceptable standard, the Secretary of State may give to the local
authority any directions that the Secretary of State considers appropriate for
the purpose of addressing the failure.

164.3.72A.2

The directions may include provision requiring the local authority—

164.3.72A.2.a

to act in accordance with advice given by the Secretary of State or a person
nominated by the Secretary of State,

164.3.72A.2.b

to collaborate with the Secretary of State or a person nominated by the
Secretary of State in taking steps specified in the directions, or

164.3.72A.2.c

to provide the Secretary of State or a person nominated by the Secretary of
State with information of a description specified in the directions, on
request or otherwise.

164.3.72A.3

If the Secretary of State considers it necessary for the purpose of addressing
the failure, the directions may include provision—

164.3.72A.3.a

for specified functions of the local authority to be exercised by the
Secretary of State or a person nominated by the Secretary of State for a
period specified in the direction or for so long as the Secretary of State
considers appropriate, and

164.3.72A.3.b

requiring the local authority to comply with any instructions of the Secretary
of State or the nominee in relation to the exercise of the functions.

164.3.72A.4

So far as is appropriate in consequence of directions given by virtue of
subsection  (3) , a reference (however expressed) in an enactment, instrument
or other document to a local authority is to be read as a reference to the
person by whom the function is exercisable.

164.3.72A.5

If directions given by virtue of subsection  (3)  expire or are revoked
without being replaced then, so far as is appropriate in consequence of the
expiry or revocation, a reference (however expressed) in an instrument or
other document to the person by whom the function was exercisable is to be
read as a reference to the local authority to whom the directions were given.

164.3.72A.6

The Secretary of State may, for the purposes of cases in which directions are
given under subsection  (3)(a) , make regulations disapplying or modifying an
enactment which confers a function on the Secretary of State in respect of a
function of a local authority.

164.3.72A.7

Directions under this section may require the local authority to provide
financial assistance to the Secretary of State, or a person nominated by the
Secretary of State, for the purpose of meeting costs incurred by the Secretary
of State or the nominee as a result of the directions.

############ Default power of Secretary of State: supplementary

164.3.72B

164.3.72B.1

Before giving directions under section  72A  the Secretary of State must give
the local authority concerned an opportunity to make representations about the
proposed directions, except so far as the Secretary of State considers that it
is impractical to do so for reasons of urgency.

164.3.72B.2

The power to give directions under section  72A  includes a power to vary or
revoke the directions by subsequent directions.

164.3.72B.3

Subsection  (1)  does not apply in relation to proposed directions varying
previous directions if the Secretary of State does not consider the variations
to be significant.

164.3.72B.4

Directions under section  72A  must be in writing.

164.3.72B.5

The Secretary of State must publish—

164.3.72B.5.a

any directions given under section  72A , and

164.3.72B.5.b

the reasons for giving them.

164.3.72B.6

Directions under section  72A  are enforceable, on the Secretary of State’s
application, by a mandatory order.

164.4

In section 125(4) (regulations and orders subject to affirmative procedure),
after paragraph (k) insert—

164.4.ka

regulations under section  72A (6)  (modification of enactments where local
authority functions are exercised by the Secretary of State or a nominee);

.

##### Cap on care costs for charging purposes

166

166.1

The Care Act 2014 is amended as follows.

166.2

In section 15 (cap on care costs), for subsections (2) and (3) substitute—

166.2.2

The reference to costs accrued in meeting the adult’s eligible needs is a
reference—

166.2.2.a

in relation to eligible needs met by a local authority, to any amount the
local authority charged the adult under section 14(1)(a) or 48(5) for meeting
those needs;

166.2.2.b

in relation to eligible needs met by a person other than a local authority, to
what the cost of meeting those eligible needs would have been to the local
authority that was the responsible local authority when the needs were met.

166.2.3

A reference in subsection (2)(b) to eligible needs does not include any
eligible needs during a period when the adult had neither a personal budget
nor an independent personal budget, other than eligible needs at any time
after a local authority was required to carry out a needs assessment that
resulted in the preparation of a personal budget or an independent personal
budget for the adult.

166.2.3A

For the purposes of this Part an adult’s needs are “eligible needs” if—

166.2.3A.a

the needs meet the eligibility criteria,

166.2.3A.b

the needs are not being met by a carer, and

166.2.3A.c

the adult is ordinarily resident or present in the area of a local authority.

166.2.3B

In this Part, “ the responsible local authority ” means the local authority in
whose area the adult is ordinarily resident or in whose area the adult is
present (where the adult is of no settled residence).

166.3

In section 24 (the steps for the local authority to take), for subsection (3)
substitute—

166.3.3

Where, following a determination under section 13(1), no local authority is
going to meet any of an adult’s needs for care and support, the local
authority that is for the time being the responsible local authority must
prepare an independent personal budget for the adult (see section 28) if—

166.3.3.a

the adult has any eligible needs, and

166.3.3.b

the adult has at any time either—

166.3.3.b.i

asked a local authority that was, at that time, the responsible local
authority, to prepare an independent personal budget, or

166.3.3.b.ii

had needs met by a local authority as mentioned in section 24(1).

166.4

In section 26 (personal budget), for subsections (1) and (2) substitute—

166.4.1

A personal budget is a statement which specifies, in respect of the adult’s
needs which a local authority is required or decides to meet as mentioned in
section 24(1)—

166.4.1.a

the current cost to the local authority of meeting those needs,

166.4.1.b

how much of that cost the adult will be required to pay under section
14(1)(a), and

166.4.1.c

the balance, if any, of the cost referred to in paragraph (a).

166.4.2

If the needs referred to in section 26(1) include eligible needs, the personal
budget must also specify—

166.4.2.a

the current cost to the local authority of meeting those eligible needs,

166.4.2.b

how much of that cost the adult will be required to pay under section
14(1)(a), and

166.4.2.c

where the amount referred to in paragraph (a) includes daily living costs, the
amount attributable to those daily living costs.

166.4.2A

If the adult has needs which a local authority is required or decides to meet
as mentioned in section 24(1) and also has eligible needs which are not being
met by any local authority, the personal budget must specify—

166.4.2A.a

what the current cost would be to the responsible local authority of meeting
those eligible needs, and

166.4.2A.b

where the amount referred to in paragraph (a) includes daily living costs, the
amount attributable to those daily living costs.

166.5

In section 28 (independent personal budget)—

166.5.a

for subsection (1) substitute—

166.5.a.1

An independent personal budget is a statement which specifies what the current
cost would be to the responsible local authority of meeting the adult’s
eligible needs (but the independent personal budget need not specify the cost
of meeting those needs at any time when the local authority required to
prepare it has ceased to be the responsible local authority or at any time
when the adult has needs which a local authority is required or decides to
meet as mentioned in section 24(1)).

;

166.5.b

omit subsection (3).

166.6

In section 29 (care account), in subsection (1), in the words before paragraph
(a), for the words from “the local authority” to “present” substitute  “the
responsible local authority” .

166.7

In section 31 (adults with capacity to request direct payments), in subsection
(1), for paragraph (a) substitute—

166.7.a

a personal budget for an adult specifies an amount under section 26(1)(c) in
respect of any needs, and

.

166.8

In section 32 (adults without capacity to request direct payments), in
subsection (1), for paragraph (a) substitute—

166.8.a

a personal budget for an adult specifies an amount under section 26(1)(c) in
respect of any needs, and

.

166.9

In section 37 (notification, assessment etc.), in subsection (15), omit
paragraph (a).

#### Medical examiners

##### Medical examiners

169

169.1

After section 18 of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009 insert—

########### Medical examiners: England

169.1.18A

169.1.18A.1

An English NHS body may appoint persons as medical examiners to discharge in
England the functions conferred on medical examiners by or under this Chapter.

169.1.18A.2

The Secretary of State must take such steps as the Secretary of State
considers appropriate for the purpose of ensuring—

169.1.18A.2.a

that enough medical examiners are appointed under subsection  (1)  to enable
those functions to be discharged in England,

169.1.18A.2.b

that the funds and other resources that are made available to such medical
examiners are enough to enable those functions to be discharged in England,
and

169.1.18A.2.c

that the performance of such medical examiners is monitored by reference to
any standards or levels of performance that they are expected to attain.

169.1.18A.3

For the purposes of discharging the duty in subsection  (2) , the Secretary of
State may give a direction to an English NHS body—

169.1.18A.3.a

requiring the body to appoint or arrange for the appointment of one or more
medical examiners,

169.1.18A.3.b

about the funds or other resources to be made available to a medical examiner
employed by an English NHS body,

169.1.18A.3.c

about the steps to be taken by the body to monitor the performance of such a
medical examiner, or

169.1.18A.3.d

about the steps to be taken by the body to monitor the performance of
functions by an English NHS body in relation to such a medical examiner.

169.1.18A.4

169.1.18A.4.d

#### Organ trafficking

##### Commercial dealings in organs for transplantation: extra-territorial offences

170

170.1

After section 32 of the Human Tissue Act 2004 insert—

########### Offences under section 32 committed outside UK

170.1.32A

170.1.32A.1

If—

170.1.32A.1.a

a person who is habitually resident in England and Wales, or who is a UK
national and not habitually resident in Northern Ireland, does an act outside
the United Kingdom,

170.1.32A.1.b

the act, if done in England and Wales, would constitute an offence under
section 32(1), and

170.1.32A.1.c

the controlled material to which the act relates is controlled material
consisting of or including a human organ,

the person is guilty in England and Wales of that offence.

170.1.32A.2

In this section “ United Kingdom national ” means an individual who is—

170.1.32A.2.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

170.1.32A.2.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

170.1.32A.2.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

170.2

After section 20 of the Human Tissue (Scotland) Act 2006 insert—

########### Offences under section 20 committed outside UK

170.2.20A

170.2.20A.1

If—

170.2.20A.1.a

a person who is habitually resident in Scotland, or who is a UK national and
not habitually resident in Northern Ireland, does an act outside the United
Kingdom, and

170.2.20A.1.b

the act, if done in Scotland, would constitute an offence under section 20(1),
and

170.2.20A.1.c

the part of the human body to which the act relates consists of or includes a
human organ,

the person is guilty in Scotland of that offence.

170.2.20A.2

In this section “ United Kingdom national ” means an individual who is—

170.2.20A.2.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

170.2.20A.2.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

170.2.20A.2.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

170.2.20A.3

Where a person outside the United Kingdom commits an offence under section
20(1) the person may be prosecuted, tried and punished for the offence—

170.2.20A.3.a

in a sheriff court district in which the person is apprehended or in custody,
or

170.2.20A.3.b

in a sheriff court district determined by the Lord Advocate,

as if the offence had been committed in that district.

170.2.20A.4

Where subsection  (3)  applies, the offence is, for all purposes incidental to
or consequential on the trial and punishment, deemed to have been committed in
that district.

170.2.20A.5

In this section “ sheriff court district ” is to be construed in accordance
with section 307(1) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995
(interpretation).

##### Fluoridation of water supplies: transitional provision

176

176.1

The Water Industry Act 1991 is amended in accordance with subsections  (2)
and  (3) .

176.2

After section 90A insert—

########### Old English fluoridation arrangements: transitional provision

176.2.90B

176.2.90B.1

With effect from the day on which section 176 of the Health and Care Act 2022
comes into force, old English fluoridation arrangements are to be treated for
the purposes of this Chapter as if they were arrangements entered into by the
water undertaker with the Secretary of State under section 87(1).

176.2.90B.2

The Secretary of State may request such modifications to the arrangements as
the Secretary of State considers necessary in order to give effect to
subsection (1) (for example to insert the terms mentioned in section 87(6)).

176.2.90B.3

If the Secretary of State and the water undertaker fail to agree the
modifications requested by the Secretary of State—

176.2.90B.3.a

subsection (2) or, as the case may be, (4) of section 87B is to apply as if
the parties had failed to agree the terms of the arrangements under section
87(1), and

176.2.90B.3.b

following determination of the modifications—

176.2.90B.3.b.i

the Secretary of State is to give notice of the determination to the water
undertaker, and

176.2.90B.3.b.ii

the arrangements are deemed to have been modified as so determined with effect
from the day after the date of notice.

176.2.90B.4

Sections 87(11) and 89(1) (which relate to consultation) do not apply to the
deemed entry into, and modification of, arrangements by virtue of this
section.

176.2.90B.5

References in this Chapter to arrangements entered into under section 87(1)
include arrangements entered into by a water undertaker by virtue of
subsection (1).

176.2.90B.6

In this section “ old English fluoridation arrangements ” means—

176.2.90B.6.a

any arrangements entered into by a water undertaker with a Strategic Health
Authority under section 87(1) of the Water Industry Act 1991 (before section
87(3) was amended by section 35(2) of the Health and Social Care Act 2012 in
relation to England), and

176.2.90B.6.b

any arrangements which were treated as arrangements falling within paragraph
(a) by virtue of section 91 (as that section had effect immediately before the
commencement of section 37(4) of the Health and Social Care Act 2012).

176.3

In section 91—

176.3.a

for the heading substitute  “Old Welsh fluoridation arrangements: transitional
provision” ;

176.3.b

in subsection (1)—

176.3.b.i

arrangements” ;

176.3.b.ii

for “relevant authority” substitute  “Welsh Ministers” ;

176.3.c

in subsection (2), for “relevant authority” substitute  “Welsh Ministers” ;

176.3.d

in subsection (3)—

176.3.d.i

for “relevant authority”, in both places it occurs, substitute  “Welsh
Ministers” ;

176.3.d.ii

in the words before paragraph (a), for “the authority” substitute  “the Welsh
Ministers” ;

176.3.d.iii

in paragraph (a), omit “(2),”;

#### Disputes about treatment of critically ill children

##### Review into disputes relating to treatment of critically ill children

177

177.1

The Secretary of State must arrange for the carrying out of a review into the
causes of disputes between (on the one hand) persons with parental
responsibility for a critically ill child and (on the other) persons
responsible for the provision of care or medical treatment for the child as
part of the health service in England.

177.2

The Secretary of State must publish and lay before Parliament a report on the
outcome of the review, within one year beginning with the date on which this
section comes into force.

177.3

In this section—

      “ child ” means a person aged under 18;           “ health service in
England ” means the health service continued under section 1(1) of the
National health Service Act 2006;           “ parental responsibility ” has
the meaning given by section 3 of the Children Act 1989.

#### Termination of pregnancy

##### Early medical termination of pregnancy

178

178.1

Section 1 of the Abortion Act 1967 is amended as follows.

178.2

In subsection (3), for “subsection” substitute  “subsections  (3B)  to” .

178.3

In subsection (3A)—

178.3.a

the words from “includes” to the end become paragraph (a);

178.3.b

after that paragraph insert—

178.3.b.b

is not limited by subsections  (3C)  and  (3D) .

178.4

After subsection (3A) insert—

178.4.3B

Subsections  (3C)  and  (3D)  apply where—

178.4.3B.a

the treatment referred to in subsection (3) consists of the prescription and
administration of medicine, and

178.4.3B.b

the registered medical practitioner terminating the pregnancy is of the
opinion, formed in good faith, that, if the medicine is administered in
accordance with their instructions, the pregnancy will not exceed ten weeks at
the time when the medicine is administered (or in the case of a course of
medicine, when the first medicine in the course is administered).

178.4.3C

If the usual place of residence of the registered medical practitioner
terminating the pregnancy is in England or Wales, the medicine may be
prescribed from that place by the registered medical practitioner.

178.4.3D

If the pregnant woman’s usual place of residence is in England or Wales and
she has had a consultation (in person, by telephone or by electronic means)
with a registered medical practitioner, registered nurse or registered midwife
about the termination of the pregnancy, the medicine may be self-administered
by the pregnant woman at that place.

#### Child safeguarding: information sharing

##### Child safeguarding etc in health and care: policy about information sharing

179

179.1

The Secretary of State must publish and lay before Parliament a report
describing the government’s policy in relation to the sharing of information
by or with public authorities in the exercise of relevant functions of those
authorities, for purposes relating to—

179.1.a

children’s health or social care, or

179.1.b

the safeguarding or promotion of the welfare of children.

179.2

In this section, “ relevant functions ” means functions relating to children’s
health or social care, so far as exercisable in relation to England.

179.3

The report must include an explanation of whether or to what extent it is the
government’s policy that a consistent identifier should be used for each
child, to facilitate the sharing of information.

179.4

The report must include a summary of the Secretary of State’s views about
implementation of the policy referred to in subsection  (1) , including any
views about steps that should be taken to overcome barriers to implementation.

179.5

The report must be published and laid before Parliament within one year
beginning with the date on which this section comes into force.

179.6

In this section “ child ” means a person aged under 18.

#### Cosmetic procedures

##### Licensing of cosmetic procedures

180

180.1

The Secretary of State may, for the purposes of reducing the risk of harm to
the health or safety of members of the public, make regulations—

180.1.a

prohibiting an individual in England from carrying out specified cosmetic
procedures in the course of business, unless the person has a personal
licence;

180.1.b

prohibiting a person from using or permitting the use of premises in England
for the carrying out of specified cosmetic procedures in the course of
business, unless the person has a premises licence.

180.2

In this section—

“ cosmetic procedure ” means a procedure, other than a surgical or dental
procedure, that is or may be carried out for cosmetic purposes; and the
reference to a procedure includes— the injection of a substance; the
application of a substance that is capable of penetrating into or through the
epidermis; the insertion of needles into the skin; the placing of threads
under the skin; the application of light, electricity, cold or heat; “
licensed premises ” means premises in respect of which a premises licence is
in force; “ local authority ” means— a county council in England; a district
council in England; a London borough council; a combined authority established
under section 103 of the Local Democracy, Economic Development and
Construction Act 2009;   a combined county authority established under section
9(1) of the Levelling-up and Regeneration Act 2023;   the Common Council of
the City of London (in its capacity as a local authority), the Sub-Treasurer
of the Inner Temple or the Under Treasurer of the Middle Temple; the Council
of the Isles of Scilly; “ personal licence ” means a licence, granted by a
specified local authority under the regulations, which authorises an
individual to carry out a cosmetic procedure of a description specified in the
licence; “ premises licence ” means a licence, granted by a specified local
authority under the regulations, which authorises premises to be used for the
carrying out of a cosmetic procedure of a description specified in the
licence; “ specified cosmetic procedure ” means a cosmetic procedure of a
description specified in the regulations; “ specified local authority ” means
a local authority of a description specified in the regulations.

180.3

The provision which may be made by regulations under this section by virtue of
section 183(1)(a) includes—

180.3.a

provision amending Schedule 5 to the Consumer Rights Act 2015 (investigatory
powers);

180.3.b

provision repealing, revoking or amending provision made by or under any local
Act.

180.4

Before making regulations under this section, the Secretary of State must
consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

180.5

Schedule 19 makes further provision about regulations under this section
(including provision for the imposition of fees, the creation of criminal
offences and financial penalties).

      “ learning disability ” has the meaning given by section 1(4) of the

activity.

########### Learning disability and autism training: code of practice

181.4.21A

181.4.21A.1

The Secretary of State must issue a code of practice about compliance with

training on learning disability and autism).

181.4.21A.2.a

draft of a code or revised code under section  21A , the Secretary of State
decides to proceed with the draft (in its original form or with
modifications), the Secretary of State must lay a copy of the draft before

181.5.e.5B

The Secretary of State may not issue the code or revised code if, within the
40-day period, either House of Parliament resolves not to approve it.

181.5.e.5C.a

### General

#### Power to make consequential provision

182

182.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential
on this Act.

182.2

Regulations under this section may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by
this Act or any provision made by or under primary legislation passed—

182.2.a

before this Act, or

182.2.b

later in the same session of Parliament as this Act.

182.3

In this section “ primary legislation ” means—

182.3.a

an Act,

182.3.b

an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru,

182.3.c

an Act of the Scottish Parliament, or

182.3.d

Northern Ireland legislation.

#### Regulations

183

183.1

A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to
make—

183.1.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

183.1.b

different provision for different purposes.

183.2

A power to make regulations under section 92, 103 or 104 includes power to
make different provision for England, Wales, Scotland or Northern Ireland.

183.3

Regulations under this Act are to be made by statutory instrument.

183.4

A statutory instrument containing any of the following (whether alone or with
other provision) may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been
laid before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament—

183.4.a

regulations under section 20 (4) ;

183.4.b

regulations under section 92;

183.4.c

regulations under section 103 or 104;

183.4.d

regulations under section 123;

183.4.e

regulations under section 180;

183.4.f

regulations under section 182 that amend or repeal provision made by primary
legislation (as defined by section 182 (3) ).

183.5

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations under section 182 is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

183.6

This section does not apply to regulations under section 186.

#### Financial provision

184

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament—

184.a

any expenditure incurred by the Secretary of State under or by virtue of this
Act, and

184.b

any increase attributable to this Act in the sums payable under any other Act
out of money so provided.

#### Extent

185

185.1

This Act extends to England and Wales only, subject to subsections  (2)  to
(5) .

185.2

The following extend to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland—

185.2.a

in Part 1, paragraph  1(3)  and  (4)  of Schedule 1 (renaming of NHS
Commissioning Board);

185.2.b

in Part 2, sections 92 to 94 (information about payments etc to persons in the
health care sector);

185.2.c

Part 3 (Secretary of State’s powers to transfer or delegate functions);

185.2.d

in Part 4, section 125 (restriction of statutory powers requiring disclosure);

185.2.e

in Part 6, section 171 and Part 2 of Schedule 17 (storage of gametes and
embryos);

185.2.f

this Part.

185.3

The following extend to Scotland only—

185.3.a

sections 140 to 143 (offences relating to virginity testing);

185.3.b

sections 152 to 155 (offences relating to hymenoplasty).

185.4

The following extend to Northern Ireland only—

185.4.a

sections 144 to 147 (offences relating to virginity testing);

185.4.b

sections 156 to 159 (offences relating to hymenoplasty).

185.5

An amendment, repeal or revocation made by this Act has the same extent as the
provision amended, repealed or revoked.

#### Commencement

186

186.1

This Part comes into force on the day on which this Act is passed.

186.2

Section 161(2) comes into force on such day as the Welsh Ministers may by
regulations appoint.

186.3

Section 171 and Schedule 17 (storage of gametes and embryos) come into force
on 1 July 2022.

186.4

Section 172 and Schedule 18 (advertising of less healthy food and drink) come
into force at the end of the period of two months beginning with the day on
which this Act is passed.

186.5

Section 179 comes into force at the end of the period of three months
beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.

186.6

Except as mentioned in subsections  (1)  to  (5) , this Act comes into force
on such day as the Secretary of State may by regulations appoint.

186.7

Different days may be appointed under subsection  (2)  or  (6)  for different
purposes.

186.8

In relation to section 166, different days may be appointed under subsection
(6)  for different areas.

186.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with the coming into force of any provision of this
Act.

186.10

The Welsh Ministers may by regulations make transitional or saving provision
in connection with the coming into force of section 161(2).

186.11

The power to make regulations under subsection  (9)  or  (10)  includes power
to make different provision for different purposes.

186.12

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

#### Short title

187

This Act may be cited as the Health and Care Act 2022.

section 42(4A); the Health and Social Care Act 2008, sections 20A, 30, 39,
45A, 48, 54, 59, 64, 80, 81 and 97; the Autism Act 2009, section 4; the Health
Act 2009, sections 2, 8 and 36; the Charities Act 2011, section 149; the
Health and Social Care Act 2012, sections 83, 84, 102, 130, 197, 234, 236,
237, 239, 241, 249, 250(4) and (7), 253, 254, 255, 260, 263, 265, 268, 274,
295, 296, 298 and Schedule 12; the Care Act 2014, sections 6, 22 and 101 and
Schedule 1; the Children and Families Act 2014, sections 26, 28, 31, 53, 56,
57 and 77; the Immigration Act 2014, Schedule 3; the Local Audit and
Accountability Act 2014, section 13 and Schedules 7 and 11; the Cities and
Local Government Devolution Act 2016, section 18; the Data Protection Act
2018, Schedule 3; the Mental Health Units (Use of Force) Act 2018, section 9.

1.3

In any other enactment (apart from this Act) passed before the day on which
section 1 comes into force, and in any instrument or other document made
before that day, any reference to the National Health Service Commissioning
Board is to be read, in relation to any time on or after that day, as a
reference to NHS England.

1.4

In this paragraph “ enactment ” includes an enactment comprised in, or in an
instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish Parliament.

.

  Integrated care boards: constitution etc

Section 19

1

Before Schedule 4 to the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—

  Integrated care boards

########## Constitution of integrated care boards

########### Introduction

1.1

An integrated care board must have a constitution.

########### Name and area

1.2

The constitution must specify—

1.2.a

the name of the integrated care board, and

1.2.b

the area for which it is established.

########### Membership: general

1.3

1.3.1

The constitution must provide for the integrated care board to consist of—

1.3.1.a

a chair (see paragraphs  5  and  6 ),

1.3.1.b

a chief executive (see paragraph  7 ), and

1.3.1.c

at least three other members (see paragraph  8 ).

1.3.2

In this Part of this Schedule a reference to an “ordinary member” is to a
member other than the chair or chief executive.

1.4

The constitution must prohibit a person from appointing someone as a member
(“the candidate”) if they consider that the appointment could reasonably be
regarded as undermining the independence of the health service because of the
candidate’s involvement with the private healthcare sector or otherwise.

########### Chair

1.5

The constitution must provide for the chair to be appointed by NHS England,
with the approval of the Secretary of State.

1.6

The constitution may not confer power to remove the chair from office on any
person other than NHS England, and any such power must be expressed to be
subject to the approval of the Secretary of State.

########### Chief executive

1.7

1.7.1

The constitution must provide for the chief executive to be appointed by the
chair, with the approval of NHS England.

1.7.2

The constitution must provide that a person is eligible to become or remain
the chief executive only if the person is an employee of the integrated care
board.

########### Ordinary members

1.8

1.8.1

The constitution must—

1.8.1.a

specify who is to appoint the ordinary members, and

1.8.1.b

provide that the appointment of an ordinary member is subject to the approval
of the chair.

1.8.2

The constitution must provide for the ordinary members to include—

1.8.2.a

at least one member nominated jointly by the NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts that—

1.8.2.a.i

provide services for the purposes of the health service within the integrated
care board’s area, and

1.8.2.a.ii

are of a prescribed description,

1.8.2.b

at least one member nominated jointly by persons who—

1.8.2.b.i

provide primary medical services for the purposes of the health service within
the integrated care board’s area, and

1.8.2.b.ii

are of a prescribed description,

1.8.2.c

at least one member nominated jointly by the local authorities whose areas
coincide with, or include the whole or any part of, the integrated care
board’s area.

1.8.3

The constitution must set out the process for nominating the ordinary members
mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2) .

1.8.4

A person participating in the process for nominating the ordinary members
mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2)  must have regard to any guidance published by
NHS England in relation to the selection of candidates.

1.8.5

The descriptions of trusts or other persons that may be prescribed for the
purposes of sub-paragraph  (2)(a)  or  (b)  may, in particular, be framed by
reference to the nature of the services that they provide or the proportion of
their services that are provided within the integrated care board’s area.

1.8.6

The chair must exercise the approval function mentioned in sub-paragraph
(1)(b) with a view to ensuring that at least one of the ordinary members has
knowledge and experience in connection with services relating to the
prevention, diagnosis and treatment of mental illness.

1.8.7

In this paragraph “ local authority ” has the meaning given by section 2B(5).

########### Further provision in connection with membership

1.9

The constitution may make further provision in connection with the membership
of the integrated care board, including provision about—

1.9.a

how members are to be appointed;

1.9.b

qualification and disqualification for membership;

1.9.c

the tenure of members (including the circumstances in which a member ceases to
hold office or may be removed or suspended from office);

1.9.d

eligibility for re-appointment;

1.9.e

terms of appointment (including provision about the remuneration or allowances
of the chair and ordinary members);

1.9.f

the validation of proceedings in the event of a vacancy or defect in an
appointment.

1.10

1.10.1

The constitution of an integrated care board must comply with any requirements
in connection with membership that are imposed by regulations.

1.10.2

The regulations may impose requirements in connection with any provision that
may be included in an integrated care board’s constitution by virtue of
paragraphs  3  to  9 .

########### Arrangements for discharging functions

1.11

1.11.1

The constitution must specify arrangements for the exercise of the integrated
care board’s functions (including its functions in determining the terms and
conditions of its employees).

1.11.2

The arrangements may include provision—

1.11.2.a

for the appointment of committees or sub-committees of the integrated care
board, and

1.11.2.b

for any such committees to consist of or include persons other than members or
employees of the integrated care board.

1.11.3

The arrangements may include provision for any functions of the integrated
care board to be exercised on its behalf by—

1.11.3.a

any of its members or employees;

1.11.3.b

a committee or sub-committee of the board.

1.11.4

If the constitution includes provision under this paragraph allowing
committees or sub-committees to exercise commissioning functions, the
constitution must—

1.11.4.a

provide for the members of any such committee or sub-committee to be approved
or appointed by the chair of the integrated care board, and

1.11.4.b

prohibit the chair from approving or appointing someone as a member of any
such committee or sub-committee (“the candidate”) if the chair considers that
the appointment could reasonably be regarded as undermining the independence
of the health service because of the candidate’s involvement with the private
healthcare sector or otherwise.

1.11.5

In sub-paragraph (4) “ commissioning functions ” means the functions of an
integrated care board in arranging for the provision of services as part of
the health service.

1.12

1.12.1

The constitution must specify the procedure to be followed by the integrated
care board in making decisions.

1.12.2

The constitution must also specify the arrangements to be made by the
integrated care board for securing that there is transparency about the
decisions of the board and the manner in which they are made.

########### Arrangements for conflicts of interests

1.13

The constitution must include—

1.13.a

provision about the arrangements to be made by the integrated care board for
discharging its functions under section  14Z30 (1)  to (4), and

1.13.b

a statement of the principles to be followed by the board in implementing
those arrangements.

########### Arrangements for public involvement

1.14

The constitution must include—

1.14.a

provision about the arrangements to be made by the integrated care board for
discharging its functions under section  14Z45 (2) , and

1.14.b

a statement of the principles to be followed by the board in implementing
those arrangements.

########### Variation of constitution

1.15

1.15.1

The constitution must include a power to vary the constitution in accordance
with a procedure set out there.

1.15.2

The provision made by the constitution in accordance with sub-paragraph (1)
must—

1.15.2.a

include power for NHS England to vary the constitution on its own initiative,
and

1.15.2.b

require NHS England’s approval to be obtained before any other variation is
made.

########### Further provision

1.16

In addition to the provision authorised or required to be included under this
Part of this Schedule, the constitution may make further provision.

########## Further provision about integrated care boards

########### Status

1.17

1.17.1

An integrated care board is a body corporate.

1.17.2

An integrated care board is not to be regarded—

1.17.2.a

as a servant or agent of the Crown, or

1.17.2.b

as enjoying any status, privilege or immunity of the Crown.

1.17.3

An integrated care board’s property is not to be regarded as property of, or
property held on behalf of, the Crown.

########### Staff

1.18

1.18.1

An integrated care board may appoint employees.

1.18.2

Employees of an integrated care board are to be paid such remuneration and
allowances as the board may determine.

1.18.3

Employees of an integrated care board are to be appointed on such other terms
and conditions as the board may determine.

1.18.4

An integrated care board may pay or make provision for the payment of such
pensions, allowances or gratuities as it may determine to or in respect of any
person who is or has been an employee of the board.

1.19

1.19.1

An integrated care board may make arrangements for a person to be seconded to
the board to serve as a member of the board’s staff.

1.19.2

A period of secondment to an integrated care board does not affect the
continuity of a person’s employment with the employer from whose service the
person is seconded.

1.19.3

In paragraphs  11  and  18  a reference to an employee of an integrated care
board includes a person seconded to the board.

1.19.4

In paragraph  7(2)  the reference to an employee of an integrated care board
includes any of the following seconded to the board—

1.19.4.a

a person employed in the civil service of the State, or

1.19.4.b

a person employed by—

1.19.4.b.i

NHS England,

1.19.4.b.ii

an NHS trust established under section 25,

1.19.4.b.iii

an NHS foundation trust,

1.19.4.b.iv

a Special Health Authority performing functions only or mainly in respect of
England,

1.19.4.b.v

the Care Quality Commission,

1.19.4.b.vi

the Health and Social Care Information Centre,

1.19.4.b.vii

the Health Services Safety Investigations Body,

1.19.4.b.viii

the Human Tissue Authority,

1.19.4.b.ix

the Human Fertilisation and Embryology Authority, or

1.19.4.b.x

NICE.

1.19.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this paragraph so as to
provide that other references in this Act to an employee of an integrated care
board include persons, or persons of a prescribed description, seconded to the
board.

########### Additional powers in respect of payment of allowances

1.20

An integrated care board may pay such allowances as it considers appropriate
to a member of a committee or sub-committee of the integrated care board who
is not a member of the board.

########### Externally financed development agreements

1.21

1.21.1

The powers of an integrated care board include power to enter into externally
financed development agreements.

1.21.2

For the purposes of this paragraph, an agreement is an externally financed
development agreement if it is certified as such in writing by the Secretary
of State.

1.21.3

The Secretary of State may give a certificate under this paragraph if—

1.21.3.a

in the Secretary of State’s opinion the purpose or main purpose of the
agreement is the provision of services or facilities in connection with the
exercise by an integrated care board of any of its functions, and

1.21.3.b

a person proposes to make a loan to, or provide any other form of finance for,
another party in connection with the agreement.

1.21.4

If an integrated care board enters into an externally financed development
agreement it may also, in connection with that agreement, enter into an
agreement with a person who falls within sub-paragraph (3)(b) in relation to
the externally financed development agreement.

1.21.5

In sub-paragraph (3)(b) “ another party ” means any party to the agreement
other than the integrated care board.

1.21.6

The fact that an agreement made by an integrated care board has not been
certified under this paragraph does not affect its validity.

########### Accounts and audits

1.22

1.22.1

An integrated care board must keep proper accounts and proper records in
relation to the accounts.

1.22.2

An integrated care board must prepare annual accounts in respect of each
financial year.

1.22.3

NHS England may, with the approval of the Secretary of State, direct an
integrated care board to prepare accounts in respect of such period or periods
as may be specified in the direction.

1.22.4

NHS England may, with the approval of the Secretary of State, give directions
to an integrated care board as to—

1.22.4.a

the methods and principles according to which any accounts under this
paragraph must be prepared, and

1.22.4.b

the form and content of any accounts prepared under this paragraph.

1.22.5

For the audit of the annual accounts, see the Local Audit and Accountability
Act 2014 (and, in particular, section 4 of that Act).

1.22.6

Accounts prepared under sub-paragraph  (3)  are also to be audited under that
Act if NHS England so directs.

1.22.7

The Comptroller and Auditor General may examine—

1.22.7.a

the annual accounts and any records relating to them, and

1.22.7.b

any report on them by the auditor or auditors.

1.22.8

An integrated care board must send any audited accounts prepared under this
paragraph to NHS England by the date specified in a direction by NHS England.

1.22.9

NHS England may direct an integrated care board to send it any unaudited
accounts prepared under this paragraph by the date specified in a direction by
NHS England.

########### Incidental powers

1.23

The power conferred on an integrated care board by section 2 includes, in
particular, power to—

1.23.a

enter into agreements,

1.23.b

acquire and dispose of property, and

1.23.c

accept gifts (including property to be held on trust for the purposes of the
integrated care board).

########### Seal and evidence

1.24

1.24.1

The application of an integrated care board’s seal must be authenticated by
the signature of any person who has been authorised (generally or specially)
for that purpose.

1.24.2

A document purporting to be duly executed under an integrated care board’s
seal or to be signed on its behalf must be received in evidence and, unless
the contrary is proven, taken to be so executed or signed.

2

In section 272 of that Act (orders, regulations, rules and directions), in
subsection (6), after paragraph  (d)  (inserted by section 17 of this Act),
insert—

2.e

regulations under paragraph  19(5)  of Schedule 1B.

Conferral of primary care functions on integrated care boards etc

Section 22

##### Conferral of functions etc

###### Preliminary

1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

###### Power to require NHS England to continue to exercise certain primary care functions

2

In section 3B (Secretary of State’s power to require NHS England to commission
services), in subsection (1)—

2.a

before paragraph (a) insert—

2.a.za

primary medical services of a prescribed description;

;

2.b

after paragraph (a), insert—

2.b.aa

primary ophthalmic services of a prescribed description;

.

###### Medical services

3

For section 83 and the italic heading before it substitute—

########## Meaning of primary medical services

########### Primary medical services for purposes of this Act

3.82A

3.82A.1

Regulations may provide that services of a prescribed description must, or
must not, be regarded as primary medical services for the purposes of this
Act.

3.82A.2

Regulations under this section may, in particular, describe services by
reference to the manner or circumstances in which they are provided.

########## Duty of integrated care boards to arrange primary medical services

########### Duty of integrated care boards to arrange primary medical services

3.82B

3.82B.1

Each integrated care board must exercise its powers so as to secure the
provision of primary medical services to such extent as it considers necessary
to meet the reasonable requirements of the persons for whom it has
responsibility.

3.82B.2

For the purposes of this section an integrated care board has responsibility
for—

3.82B.2.a

the group of people for whom it has core responsibility (see section  14Z31 ),
and

3.82B.2.b

such other people as may be prescribed (whether generally or in relation to a
prescribed service).

########## General functions

########### General power to make arrangements

3.83

3.83.1

An integrated care board may make such arrangements for the provision of
primary medical services as it considers appropriate for the purpose of
discharging its functions under section 82B (and may, in particular, make
contractual arrangements with any person).

3.83.2

NHS England may make such arrangements for the provision of primary medical
services as it considers appropriate for the purpose of discharging any
functions under section 3B(1) (and may, in particular, make contractual
arrangements with any person).

3.83.3

The arrangements that may be made under this section include—

3.83.3.a

in the case of an integrated care board, arrangements for the performance of a
service outside its area (whether or not in England);

3.83.3.b

in the case of NHS England, arrangements for the performance of a service
outside England.

3.83.4

Arrangements under this section may confer discretions on a person with whom
they are made in relation to anything to be provided under the arrangements.

3.83.5

The powers under this section are in addition to the powers conferred by
sections 84 and 92.

########### Publication of information

3.83A

Each integrated care board and NHS England must publish information about such
matters as may be prescribed in relation to the primary medical services
provided under this Act.

4

4.1

Section 84 (general medical services contracts: introductory) is amended as
follows.

4.2

In subsection (1), for “The Board” substitute  “An integrated care board or
NHS England” .

4.3

In subsection (3) for “the Board” substitute  “the integrated care board or
NHS England (as the case may be)” .

4.4

For subsection (4) substitute—

4.4.4

The services to be provided under a general medical services contract may
include services which are not primary medical services.

4.4.4A

The services to be provided under a general medical services contract may
include—

4.4.4A.a

in the case of a contract entered into by an integrated care board, services
to be performed outside its area (whether or not in England);

4.4.4A.b

in the case of a contract entered into by NHS England, services to be
performed outside England.

4.4.4B

A general medical services contract may confer discretions on a person with
whom it is made in relation to anything to be provided under the contract.

4.5

In subsection (5), for “the Board” substitute  “the integrated care board or
NHS England” .

###### Dental services

15

For section 99 and the italic heading before it substitute—

########## Meaning of primary dental services

########### Primary dental services for purposes of this Act

15.98C

15.98C.1

Regulations may provide that services of a prescribed description must, or
must not, be regarded as primary dental services for the purposes of this Act.

15.98C.2

Regulations under this section may, in particular, describe services by
reference to the manner or circumstances in which they are provided.

########## Duty of integrated care boards to arrange primary dental services

########### Duty of integrated care boards to arrange primary dental services

15.99

15.99.1

Each integrated care board must exercise its powers so as to secure the
provision of primary dental services to such extent as it considers necessary
to meet the reasonable requirements of the people for whom it has
responsibility.

15.99.2

For the purposes of this section an integrated care board has responsibility
for—

15.99.2.a

the group of people for whom it has core responsibility (see section  14Z31 ),
and

15.99.2.b

such other people as may be prescribed (whether generally or in relation to a
prescribed service).

########## General functions

########### General power to make arrangements

15.99A

15.99A.1

An integrated care board may make such arrangements for the provision of
primary dental services as it considers appropriate for the purpose of
discharging its functions under section  99  (and may, in particular, make
contractual arrangements with any person).

15.99A.2

NHS England may make such arrangements for the provision of primary dental
services as it considers appropriate for the purpose of discharging any
functions under section 3B(1) (and may, in particular, make contractual
arrangements with any person).

15.99A.3

The arrangements that may be made under this section include—

15.99A.3.a

in the case of an integrated care board, arrangements for the performance of a
service outside its area (whether or not in England);

15.99A.3.b

in the case of NHS England, arrangements for the performance of a service
outside England.

15.99A.4

The powers in this section are in addition to the powers conferred by sections
100 and 107.

########### Publication of information

15.99B

Each integrated care board and NHS England must publish information about such
matters as may be prescribed in relation to the primary dental services
provided under this Act.

######### Application of section 223 to integrated care boards

115.223A

115.223A.1

Section 223 applies in relation to an integrated care board as it applies in
relation to NHS England.

115.223A.2

But the powers conferred by that section are exercisable by an integrated care
board only for the purpose of securing improvement—

115.223A.2.a

in the physical and mental health of the group of people for whom it has core
responsibility (see section  14Z31 ), or

115.223A.2.b

in the prevention, diagnosis and treatment of illness in such people.

Abolition of Monitor and transfer of its functions

Section 33

##### General

1

Any reference to Monitor in an instrument or other document made before the
day on which section 33(2) comes into force is to be read, in relation to any
time after that provision comes into force, as a reference to NHS England.

##### Public Bodies (Admission to Meetings) Act 1960

  Intervention powers over the reconfiguration of NHS services

Section 46

  In the National Health Service Act 2006, after Schedule 10 insert—
SCHEDULE 10A   Intervention powers in relation to the reconfiguration of NHS
services   Section 68A   Definitions   1     In this Schedule—         “ NHS
commissioning body ” means NHS England or an integrated care board;
“ NHS services ” means services provided as part of the health service in
England;           “ NHS trust ” means an NHS trust established under section
25;           “ reconfiguration of NHS services ” means a change in the
arrangements made by an NHS commissioning body for the provision of NHS
services where that change has an impact on—         the manner in which a
service is delivered to individuals (at the point when the service is received
by users), or           the range of health services available to individuals.
Duty to notify Secretary of State of reconfiguration proposals   2       1
If an NHS commissioning body proposes a notifiable reconfiguration of NHS
services it must notify the Secretary of State.         2     For the purposes
of this paragraph a reconfiguration of NHS services is “notifiable” if it is
of a description specified in regulations.           Power to call-in proposal
for reconfiguration   3       1     The Secretary of State may give an NHS
commissioning body a direction calling in any proposal by the body for the
reconfiguration of NHS services.         2     Where a direction is given
under sub-paragraph  (1) , the Secretary of State—     a     may, within the
period of 6 months beginning with the date of the direction, take any decision
in relation to the proposal that could have been taken by the NHS
commissioning body, and         b     must notify the NHS commissioning body
once the Secretary of State has finished considering the proposal.
3     The power of the Secretary of State to take decisions under sub-
paragraph  (2)(a)  includes—     a     power to decide whether a proposal
should, or should not, proceed, or should proceed in a modified form;
b     power to decide particular results to be achieved by the NHS
commissioning body in taking decisions in relation to the proposal;         c
power to decide procedural or other steps that should, or should not, be taken
in relation to the proposal;         d     power to retake any decision
previously taken by the NHS commissioning body.             4     The
Secretary of State must, before acting under sub-paragraph (2), give each of
the following an opportunity to make representations to the Secretary of State
in relation to the proposal—     a     the NHS commissioning body,         b
if the NHS commissioning body is an integrated care board, NHS England,
c     each local authority (within the meaning of section 2B) to whose area
the proposed reconfiguration of NHS services relates, and         d     any
other person that the Secretary of State considers appropriate.             5
The Secretary of State must—     a     publish any decision under sub-
paragraph  (2)(a)  together with an explanation of the reasons for taking it,
and         b     notify the NHS commissioning body of the decision and the
reasons.             6     The Secretary of State must publish a summary of
any representations made under sub-paragraph (4).           4       1     This
paragraph applies where the Secretary of State gives a direction under
paragraph  3(1)  calling in a proposal for the reconfiguration of NHS
services.         2     Until notified that the Secretary of State has
finished considering the proposal, the NHS commissioning body must not take
further steps in relation to a proposal except to such extent (if any) as may
be permitted by the direction.         3     Once notified that the Secretary
of State has finished considering the proposal, the NHS commissioning body
must give effect to any decision of the Secretary of State under paragraph
3(2)(a)  in relation to the proposal.           Power to require consideration
of proposals for reconfiguration   5       1     The Secretary of State may
direct an NHS commissioning body to consider a reconfiguration of NHS
services.         2     The Secretary of State must publish any direction
under this paragraph, together with an explanation of the reasons for giving
it.           Duties to provide information and other assistance   6     An
NHS commissioning body, NHS trust or NHS foundation trust must give the
Secretary of State any information or other assistance that the Secretary of
State requires it to give for the purposes of carrying out any functions under
this Schedule.       Guidance   7       1     The Secretary of State must
publish guidance for NHS commissioning bodies, NHS trusts and NHS foundation
trusts about—     a     the exercise of their functions under this Schedule,
and         b     how the Secretary of State proposes to exercise the
Secretary of State’s functions under this Schedule.             2     NHS
commissioning bodies, NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts must have regard to
any guidance published under sub- paragraph (1).

Trust special administrators: NHS trusts and NHS foundation trusts

Section 70

##### Amendments about trust special administrators

1

The National Health Service Act 2006 is amended as follows.

2

For section 65B substitute—

######### NHS trusts: appointment of trust special administrator

2.65B

2.65B.1

NHS England may make an order in accordance with this section authorising the
appointment of a trust special administrator to exercise the functions of the
chair and directors of an NHS trust to which this Chapter applies.

2.65B.2

NHS England—

2.65B.2.a

must make an order under subsection  (1)  if required to do so by the Care
Quality Commission, and

2.65B.2.b

may otherwise make an order under subsection  (1)  only if—

2.65B.2.b.i

NHS England considers it appropriate to do so in the interests of the health
service, and

2.65B.2.b.ii

the Secretary of State has approved the making of the order.

2.65B.3

The Care Quality Commission may require NHS England to make an order under
subsection  (1)  only if it is satisfied that there is a serious failure by
the NHS trust to provide services that are of sufficient quality to be
provided under this Act.

2.65B.4

Before requiring NHS England to make an order under subsection  (1)  the Care
Quality Commission must—

2.65B.4.a

consult the Secretary of State and NHS England, and

2.65B.4.b

having done that, consult—

2.65B.4.b.i

the trust,

2.65B.4.b.ii

any integrated care board in whose area the trust has hospitals,
establishments or facilities, and

2.65B.4.b.iii

any person to which the trust provides goods or services under this Act and
which the Commission considers it appropriate to consult.

2.65B.5

Before making an order under subsection  (1)  in a case where it is not
required to do so by the Care Quality Commission, NHS England must consult—

2.65B.5.a

the trust,

2.65B.5.b

any integrated care board in whose area the trust has hospitals,
establishments or facilities,

2.65B.5.c

any other person to which the trust provides goods or services under this Act
and which NHS England considers it appropriate to consult, and

2.65B.5.d

the Care Quality Commission.

2.65B.6

An order under subsection  (1)  must specify the date when the appointment is
to take effect, which must be within the period of 5 working days beginning
with the day on which the order is made.

2.65B.7

NHS England must lay before Parliament (with the statutory instrument
containing the order) a report stating the reasons for making the order.

2.65B.8

If an order is made under subsection  (1) , NHS England must—

2.65B.8.a

appoint a person as the trust special administrator with effect from the day
specified in the order, and

2.65B.8.b

publish the name of the person appointed.

2.65B.9

A person appointed as a trust special administrator holds and vacates office
in accordance with the terms of the appointment.

2.65B.10

NHS England may pay remuneration and expenses to a trust special administrator
appointed under this section.

######### Care Quality Commission report on safety and quality of services

2.65BA

2.65BA.1

This section applies where the Care Quality Commission require NHS England to
make an order under section  65B (1)  in relation to an NHS trust.

2.65BA.2

The Care Quality Commission must, as soon as reasonably practicable after the
making of the order, provide to NHS England and the Secretary of State a
report on the safety and quality of the services that the trust provides under
this Act.

5.2.1

A trust special administrator appointed in relation to an NHS trust must,

provide NHS England and the Secretary of State with a draft report

publish a copy of that draft report,

unless unable to obtain the statements required by subsections  (1B)  and
(1C) .

5.2.1B

A trust special administrator may not provide a draft report under subsection
(1A) —

5.2.1B.a

without having obtained a statement from each commissioner that the
commissioner considers that the recommendation in the draft report—

5.2.1B.a.i

would achieve the objective set out in section 65DA(1)(a), and

5.2.1B.a.ii

would do so without harming essential services provided for the purposes of
the NHS by any other NHS foundation trust or NHS trust that provides services
under this Act to the commissioner, or

5.2.1B.b

where the administrator is unable to obtain a statement to that effect from
one or more of the commissioners (other than NHS England), without having
obtained a statement to that effect from NHS England.

5.2.1C

A trust special administrator may not provide a draft report under subsection
(1A)  without having obtained a statement from the Care Quality Commission
that it considers that the recommendation in the draft report would achieve
that part of the objective set out in section 65DA(1)(aa).

5.2.2

When preparing a draft report under subsection  (1)  or  (1A) , the
administrator must consult—

5.2.2.a

any person to which the trust provides goods or services under this Act and
which NHS England directs the administrator to consult, and

5.2.2.b

the Care Quality Commission.

5.2.3

After receiving a draft report under subsection  (1)  or  (1A) , NHS England
must lay it before Parliament.

5.3

Omit subsections (4), (5) and (5A).

5.4

5.4.6

Where NHS England decides not to provide to the administrator a statement to
the effect mentioned in subsection  (1B)(b) , NHS England must—

5.4.6.a

5.4.6.b

publish the notice, and

5.4.6.c

5.4.6A.b

5.4.6A.c

######### Decision of NHS England or Secretary of State in case of NHS trust

  The NHS payment scheme

Section 77

1

The Health and Social Care Act 2012 is amended as follows.

2

In section 97 (conditions of licences for health care service providers), in
subsection (1)(g), for “the national tariff (see section 116)” substitute
“the NHS payment scheme (see section  114A )” .

3

In Part 3, for Chapter 4 substitute—

######## The NHS payment scheme

######### The NHS payment scheme

3.114A

3.114A.1

NHS England must publish a document, to be known as “ the NHS payment scheme
”, containing rules for determining the price that is to be payable by a
commissioner—

3.114A.1.a

for the provision of health care services for the purposes of the NHS;

3.114A.1.b

for the provision of services in pursuance of arrangements made by NHS England
or an integrated care board in the exercise of any public health functions of
the Secretary of State, within the meaning of the National Health Service Act
2006, by virtue of any provision of that Act.

3.114A.2

The commissioner and the provider of services mentioned in subsection  (1)
must comply with rules under that subsection.

3.114A.3

Rules under subsection  (1)  may, in particular—

3.114A.3.a

specify prices;

3.114A.3.b

specify amounts, formulae or other matters on the basis of which prices are to
be determined;

3.114A.3.c

provide for prices to be determined for, or by reference to, components of
services or groups of services;

3.114A.3.d

make different provision for different services or provision for some services
but not others;

3.114A.3.e

make different provision for the same service by reference to different
circumstances or areas, different descriptions of provider, or other factors
relevant to the provision of the service or the arrangements for its
provision;

3.114A.3.f

confer a discretion on the commissioner of a service or on NHS England.

3.114A.4

Rules under subsection  (1)  may allow or require a price to be agreed between
the commissioner and the provider of a service.

3.114A.5

Rules made by virtue of subsection  (4)  may—

3.114A.5.a

make provision about how the price is to be agreed;

3.114A.5.b

allow the agreement to make any provision that could be made by rules by
virtue of subsection  (3) ;

3.114A.5.c

provide for the publication by the commissioner, the provider or NHS England
of information relevant to the agreement.

3.114A.6

For the purpose of securing that the prices payable for the provision of
services mentioned in subsection  (1) (a)  or  (b)  result in a fair level of
pay for providers of those services, NHS England must, in exercising functions
under subsection  (1) , have regard to—

3.114A.6.a

differences in the costs incurred in providing those services to persons of
different descriptions, and

3.114A.6.b

differences between providers with respect to the range of those services that
they provide.

3.114A.7

The NHS payment scheme may contain rules relating to the making of payments to
the provider of a service for the provision of that service.

3.114A.8

The NHS payment scheme may contain guidance as to the application of rules
under subsection  (1) .

3.114A.9

A commissioner of a service mentioned in subsection  (1)  must have regard to
any such guidance.

3.114A.10

The NHS payment scheme has effect for the period specified in the NHS payment
scheme or, where a new edition of the NHS payment scheme takes effect before
the end of that period, until that new edition takes effect.

######### The NHS payment scheme: enforcement

3.114B

Where the commissioner of a service fails to comply with rules contained in
the NHS payment scheme, NHS England may direct the commissioner to take steps
specified in the direction, within a period specified in the direction—

3.114B.a

to secure that the failure does not continue or recur, or

3.114B.b

to secure that the position is (so far as practicable) restored to what it
would have been if the failure was not occurring or had not occurred.

######### The NHS payment scheme: impact assessment and consultation

3.114C

3.114C.1

Before publishing the NHS payment scheme, NHS England must—

3.114C.1.a

carry out an assessment of the likely impact of the proposed scheme, or

3.114C.1.b

publish a statement setting out its reasons for concluding that such
assessment is not needed.

3.114C.2

Before publishing the NHS payment scheme, NHS England must consult the
following—

3.114C.2.a

each integrated care board;

3.114C.2.b

each relevant provider;

3.114C.2.c

such other persons as NHS England considers appropriate.

3.114C.3

NHS England must give those persons a notice—

3.114C.3.a

describing the proposed NHS payment scheme,

3.114C.3.b

setting out any impact assessment carried out under subsection  (1)(a) , and

3.114C.3.c

specifying when the period within which representations may be made about the
proposed NHS payment scheme (“the consultation period”) will come to an end.

3.114C.4

The consultation period is the period of 28 days beginning with the day after
that on which the notice is published.

3.114C.5

NHS England must publish the notice given under subsection  (2) .

3.114C.6

If, having consulted under this section—

3.114C.6.a

NHS England decides to make amendments of the proposed NHS payment scheme that
are, in its opinion, significant, and

3.114C.6.b

it would, in NHS England’s opinion, be unfair to make the amendments without
further consultation,

NHS England must consult again under this section.

3.114C.7

Subsection  (6)  does not apply where section  114D  applies.

3.114C.8

In this section “ relevant provider ” means—

3.114C.8.a

a licence holder, or

3.114C.8.b

another person, of a prescribed description, that provides—

3.114C.8.b.i

health care services for the purposes of the NHS, or

3.114C.8.b.ii

services in pursuance of arrangements made by NHS England or an integrated
care board by virtue of section 7A or 7B of the National Health Service Act
2006 (Secretary of State’s public health functions).

######### Objections to proposed NHS payment scheme

3.114D

3.114D.1

This section applies where—

3.114D.1.a

within the consultation period under section  114C , NHS England receives
objections to the proposed NHS payment scheme from one or more integrated care
boards or relevant providers, and

3.114D.1.b

either or both of the following apply—

3.114D.1.b.i

the objection percentage for integrated care boards exceeds the prescribed
percentage;

3.114D.1.b.ii

the objection percentage for relevant providers exceeds the prescribed
percentage.

3.114D.2

In subsection  (1)(b)  the “objection percentage” is the proportion (expressed
as a percentage) of integrated care boards or (as the case may be) relevant
providers that objected.

3.114D.3

NHS England must consult such persons as appear to NHS England to be
representative of the integrated care boards or relevant providers from whom
objections were received.

3.114D.4

If, having complied with subsection  (3) —

3.114D.4.a

NHS England decides to make amendments of the proposed NHS payment scheme that
are, in its opinion, significant, and

3.114D.4.b

it would, in NHS England’s opinion, be unfair to make the amendments without
further consultation,

NHS England must consult again under section  114C .

3.114D.5

If, having complied with subsection  (3) , NHS England decides not to amend
the proposed NHS payment scheme, it may publish the scheme but, before doing
so, must—

3.114D.5.a

publish a notice stating that decision and setting out the reasons for it, and

3.114D.5.b

send a copy of the notice to—

3.114D.5.b.i

the persons consulted under subsection  (3) , and

3.114D.5.b.ii

the integrated care boards or relevant providers from whom objections were
received.

######### Amendments of the NHS payment scheme

3.114E

3.114E.1

NHS England may amend the NHS payment scheme during the period for which it
has effect, provided that, in the opinion of NHS England, the amendments are
not so significant as to require publication of a new edition of the NHS
payment scheme.

3.114E.2

In deciding whether the amendments are so significant as to require the
publication of a new edition of the NHS payment scheme, NHS England must have
regard to—

3.114E.2.a

the proportion of integrated care boards that would be affected by the
proposed amendments;

3.114E.2.b

the proportion of relevant providers that would be affected by the proposed
amendments;

3.114E.2.c

the impact that the proposed amendments would have on integrated care boards
and relevant providers that would be affected by them;

3.114E.2.d

whether any integrated care boards or relevant providers would be
disproportionately affected by the proposed amendments;

3.114E.2.e

the amount of any increase or decrease in prices that would result from the
proposed amendments.

3.114E.3

If NHS England amends the NHS payment scheme, it must publish the NHS payment
scheme as amended.

3.114E.4

Before amending the NHS payment scheme, NHS England must, in accordance with
subsections  (5)  to  (7) , consult the following about the proposed
amendments—

3.114E.4.a

any integrated care boards that would be affected by the proposed amendments;

3.114E.4.b

any relevant providers that would be affected by the proposed amendments;

3.114E.4.c

such other persons as NHS England considers appropriate.

3.114E.5

NHS England must publish a notice specifying—

3.114E.5.a

the proposed amendments, and

3.114E.5.b

when the period within which representations may be made about the proposed
amendments (“the consultation period”) will come to an end.

3.114E.6

The consultation period is the period of 28 days beginning with the day after
that on which the notice is published.

3.114E.7

NHS England must send a copy of the notice to each of the persons to be
consulted under subsection  (4) .

######### Interpretation

3.114F

In this Chapter—

      “ commissioner ”, in relation to a service, means the person who
arranges for the provision of the service;           “ the NHS payment scheme
” means the document published under section  114A (1) ;           “ relevant
provider ” has the meaning given by section  114C (8) .

4

In section 304 (regulations, orders and directions), in subsection (5), for
paragraph (g) substitute—

4.g

regulations under section  114D (1)(b)(i)  or  (ii)  (percentage to be
prescribed in cases of objections to proposals for NHS payment scheme);

.

  Patient choice: undertakings by integrated care boards

Section 78

  After Schedule 1 to the National Health Service Act 2006 insert—
SCHEDULE 1ZA   Patient choice: undertakings by integrated care boards
Section 6F   Introductory   1     This Schedule makes further provision about
undertakings under section 6F.       Procedure   2       1     NHS England
must publish a procedure for entering into undertakings.         2     NHS
England may revise the procedure and, if it does so, NHS England must publish
the procedure as revised.         3     NHS England must consult such persons
as it considers appropriate before publishing or revising the procedure.
3       1     Where NHS England accepts an undertaking, NHS England must
publish the undertaking.         2     But NHS England must not under sub-
paragraph  (1)  publish any part of an undertaking which contains information
which it is satisfied is—     a     commercial information the disclosure of
which would, or might, significantly harm the legitimate business interests of
the person to whom it relates;         b     information relating to the
private affairs of an individual the disclosure of which would, or might,
significantly harm that person’s interests.               Variation of terms
4     The terms of an undertaking (including, in particular, the action
specified under it and the period so specified within which the action must be
taken) may be varied if both the integrated care board giving the undertaking
and NHS England agree.       Compliance certificates   5       1     Where NHS
England is satisfied that an undertaking has been complied with, NHS England
must issue a certificate to that effect (referred to in this Schedule as a “
compliance certificate ”).         2     An integrated care board which has
given an undertaking may at any time make an application to NHS England for a
compliance certificate.         3     The application must be made in such
form, and accompanied by such information, as NHS England requires.         4
NHS England must decide whether or not to issue a compliance certificate, and
give notice to the applicant of its decision, before the end of the period of
14 days beginning with the day after that on which the application is
received.           6       1     An appeal lies to the First-tier Tribunal
against a decision of NHS England to refuse an application for a compliance
certificate.         2     The grounds for an appeal under this paragraph are
that the decision was—     a     based on an error of fact,         b
wrong in law, or         c     unfair or unreasonable.             3     On an
appeal under this paragraph, the Tribunal may confirm NHS England’s decision
or direct that it is not to have effect.           Inaccurate, incomplete or
misleading information   7     Where NHS England is satisfied that an
integrated care board which has given an undertaking has supplied NHS England
with inaccurate, misleading or incorrect information in relation to the
undertaking—     a     NHS England may treat the integrated care board as
having failed to comply with the undertaking, and         b     if NHS England
decides so to treat the integrated care board, NHS England must by notice
revoke any certificate of compliance given to that integrated care board.
