The Health Services Safety Investigations Body

Section 109

##### Constitution

###### Status

1

1.1

The HSSIB is not to be regarded—

1.1.a

as the servant or agent of the Crown, or

1.1.b

as enjoying any status, immunity or privilege of the Crown.

1.2

The HSSIB’s property is not to be regarded—

1.2.a

as the property of the Crown, or

1.2.b

as property held on behalf of the Crown.

###### Membership

2

2.1

The HSSIB is to consist of—

2.1.a

a Chief Investigator appointed in accordance with paragraph  3 ,

2.1.b

other members appointed in accordance with paragraph  4 , and

2.1.c

a chair and at least four other members appointed by the Secretary of State.

2.2

The Chief Investigator is to be the chief executive of the HSSIB.

2.3

The HSSIB must have more non-executive than executive members.

2.4

In this Schedule—

2.4.a

references to executive members of the HSSIB are references to the members
mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) (a)  and  (b) , and

2.4.b

references to non-executive members of the HSSIB are references to the members
mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) (c) .

###### The Chief Investigator: appointment and status

3

3.1

The Chief Investigator is to be appointed by the non-executive members with
the consent of the Secretary of State.

3.2

The Chief Investigator is to be an employee of the HSSIB.

###### Other executive members: appointment and status

4

4.1

The other executive members of the HSSIB are to be appointed by the non-
executive members.

4.2

The non-executive members may not appoint more than five other executive
members without the consent of the Secretary of State.

4.3

The other executive members are to be employees of the HSSIB.

###### Non-executive members: tenure

5

5.1

A person holds and vacates office as a non-executive member of the HSSIB in
accordance with that person’s terms of appointment (subject to the following
provisions of this paragraph).

5.2

A person may at any time resign from office as a non-executive member by
giving notice to the Secretary of State.

5.3

The Secretary of State may at any time remove a person from office as a non-
executive member on any of the following grounds—

5.3.a

incapacity,

5.3.b

misbehaviour, or

5.3.c

failure to carry out the person’s duties as a non-executive member.

5.4

The Secretary of State may suspend a person from office as a non-executive
member if it appears to the Secretary of State that there are or may be
grounds to remove the person from office under sub-paragraph  (3) .

5.5

A person may be appointed as a non-executive member for an initial term of up
to three years.

5.6

A person who has been appointed as a non-executive member for an initial term
may be re-appointed, but only for one further term of up to three years.

5.7

The further term must begin at the end of the initial term.

###### Non-executive members: suspension from office

6

6.1

This paragraph applies where a person is suspended under paragraph  5 (4) .

6.2

The Secretary of State must give notice of the decision to suspend to the
person.

6.3

The suspension takes effect on receipt by the person of the notice.

6.4

The notice may be—

6.4.a

delivered in person (in which case the person is taken to receive it when it
is delivered), or

6.4.b

sent by first class post to the person’s last known address (in which case the
person is taken to receive it on the third day after the day on which it is
posted).

6.5

The initial period of suspension must not exceed six months.

6.6

The Secretary of State may review the suspension at any time.

6.7

The Secretary of State—

6.7.a

must review the suspension if requested in writing by the person to do so, but

6.7.b

is not required to review the suspension before the end of the period of three
months beginning with the start of the initial period of suspension.

6.8

Following a review during a period of suspension, the Secretary of State may—

6.8.a

confirm the suspension,

6.8.b

revoke the suspension, or

6.8.c

suspend the person for another period of not more than six months beginning
with the expiry of the current period.

6.9

The Secretary of State must revoke the suspension if the Secretary of State—

6.9.a

decides that there are no grounds to remove the person from office under
paragraph  5 (3) , or

6.9.b

decides that there are grounds to do so but does not remove the person from
office under that provision.

7

7.1

Where a person is suspended from office as the chair under paragraph  5 (4) ,
the Secretary of State may appoint a non-executive member as interim chair to
exercise the chair’s functions.

7.2

Appointment as interim chair is for a term not exceeding the shorter of—

7.2.a

the period ending with either—

7.2.a.i

the appointment of a new chair, or

7.2.a.ii

the revocation or expiry of the existing chair’s suspension, and

7.2.b

the remainder of the interim chair’s term as a non-executive member.

7.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies if—

7.3.a

a person’s initial term as interim chair is to cease as a result of the expiry
of the person’s initial term as a non-executive member, and

7.3.b

that person is to be re-appointed as a non-executive member.

7.4

The person may be re-appointed as interim chair for a further term determined
in accordance with sub-paragraph  (2) .

7.5

That further term must begin at the end of the person’s initial term as
interim chair.

###### Non-executive members: payment

8

8.1

The HSSIB must pay to the non-executive members such remuneration as the
Secretary of State may determine.

8.2

The HSSIB must pay or make provision for the payment of such pensions,
allowances or gratuities as the Secretary of State may determine to or in
respect of any person who is or has been a non-executive member.

8.3

If a person ceases to be a non-executive member and the Secretary of State
decides that there are exceptional circumstances which mean that the person
should be compensated, the HSSIB must pay compensation to the person of such
amount as the Secretary of State may determine.

###### Staff

9

9.1

The HSSIB may appoint such persons to be employees of the HSSIB as it
considers appropriate.

9.2

Employees of the HSSIB are to be paid such remuneration as the HSSIB may
determine.

9.3

Employees of the HSSIB are to be appointed on such other terms and conditions
as the HSSIB may determine.

9.4

The HSSIB may pay or make provision for the payment of such pensions,
allowances or gratuities as it may determine to or in respect of any person
who is or has been an employee of the HSSIB.

9.5

Before making a determination as to remuneration, pensions, allowances or
gratuities for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2)  or  (4) , the HSSIB must
obtain the approval of the Secretary of State to its policy on that matter.

###### Procedure

10

10.1

The HSSIB may regulate its own procedure.

10.2

The validity of any act of the HSSIB is not affected by any vacancy among the
members or by any defect in the appointment of any member.

###### Committees

11

11.1

The HSSIB may appoint such committees and sub-committees as it considers
appropriate.

11.2

A committee or sub-committee may consist of or include persons who are not
members or employees of the HSSIB.

11.3

The HSSIB may pay such remuneration and allowances as it may determine to any
person who—

11.3.a

is a member of a committee or a sub-committee, but

11.3.b

is not an employee of the HSSIB,

whether or not that person is a non-executive member of the HSSIB.

11.4

Before making a determination as to remuneration or allowances for the
purposes of sub-paragraph  (3) , the HSSIB must consult the Secretary of
State.

###### Exercise of functions

12

12.1

The HSSIB must exercise the functions conferred on it by this Part
effectively, efficiently and economically.

12.2

The HSSIB may arrange for the exercise of any of its functions on its behalf
by—

12.2.a

any non-executive member,

12.2.b

any employee (including any executive member), or

12.2.c

a committee or sub-committee.

###### Assistance in exercise of functions

13

13.1

The HSSIB may arrange for persons to assist it in the exercise of its
functions in relation to—

13.1.a

a particular case, or

13.1.b

cases of a particular description.

13.2

Such arrangements may include provision with respect to the payment of
remuneration and allowances to, or amounts in respect of, such persons.

###### Funding

14

14.1

The Secretary of State may make payments to the HSSIB out of money provided by
Parliament of such amounts as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

14.2

Payments made under sub-paragraph  (1)  may be made at such times and on such
conditions (if any) as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

###### Supplementary powers

15

15.1

The HSSIB may do anything which is calculated to facilitate, or is conducive
or incidental to, the discharge of any function conferred on it by this Part.

15.2

The power under sub-paragraph (1) includes power for the HSSIB to do the
following—

15.2.a

enter into agreements;

15.2.b

acquire and dispose of property;

15.2.c

supply materials, facilities and services to any person;

15.2.d

develop and exploit ideas and exploit intellectual property.

15.3

But the HSSIB requires the consent of the Secretary of State to borrow money
temporarily by way of overdraft.

###### Use of income from charges

16

Where the HSSIB receives income from imposing charges under section 127 (8)
or 128 (4) , it must ensure that the income is used for exercising its
functions.

###### Losses and liabilities etc

17

17.1

Section 265 of the Public Health Act 1875 (which relates to the protection of
members and officers of certain authorities from personal liability) has
effect as if the HSSIB were an authority of the kind referred to in that
section.

17.2

In its application to the HSSIB as a result of sub-paragraph  (1) , section
265 of that Act has effect as if the references in that section to that Act
were references to this Part of this Act.

###### Accounts

18

18.1

The HSSIB must keep proper accounts and proper records in relation to the
accounts.

18.2

The Secretary of State may give directions to the HSSIB as to—

18.2.a

the content and form of its accounts, and

18.2.b

the methods and principles to be applied in the preparation of its accounts.

19

19.1

The HSSIB must prepare annual accounts in respect of each financial year.

19.2

The HSSIB must send copies of the annual accounts to the Secretary of State
and the Comptroller and Auditor General within such period after the end of
the financial year to which the accounts relate as the Secretary of State may
direct.

19.3

The Comptroller and Auditor General must—

19.3.a

examine, certify and report on the annual accounts, and

19.3.b

lay copies of them and the report before Parliament.

19.4

In this paragraph and paragraph  20 , “ financial year ” means a period of 12
months ending with 31 March.

###### Reports and other information

20

20.1

As soon as practicable after the end of each financial year, the HSSIB must
prepare an annual report on how it has exercised its functions during the
financial year to which the report relates.

20.2

The report must, among other things, set out the measures that the HSSIB has
taken to ensure that its functions are exercised effectively, efficiently and
economically.

20.3

The HSSIB must send a copy of the report to the Secretary of State.

20.4

The Secretary of State must lay a copy of the report before Parliament.

20.5

The HSSIB must publish the report once it has been laid before Parliament.

20.6

Subject to sub-paragraph  (7) , the Secretary of State may require the HSSIB
to provide to the Secretary of State such other reports and information
relating to the exercise of its functions as the Secretary of State may
request.

20.7

The Secretary of State may not require the HSSIB to provide any reports or
information that relate to an investigation that the HSSIB is carrying out or
has carried out.

###### Seal and signature

21

21.1

The application of the HSSIB’s seal must be authenticated by the signature of
any member of the HSSIB or any other person who has been authorised (generally
or specially) for that purpose.

21.2

A document purporting to be duly executed under the HSSIB’s seal or to be
signed on its behalf must be received in evidence and, unless the contrary is
proved, taken to be so executed or signed.

##### Transfer schemes

22

22.1

The Secretary of State may, in connection with the establishment of the HSSIB
by this Act, make one or more transfer schemes.

22.2

A “transfer scheme” is a scheme for the transfer to the HSSIB of any property,
rights or liabilities of NHS England relating to the discharge of NHS
England’s functions pursuant to any directions made by the Secretary of State
under the power conferred by section 44 which are in force at the time the
scheme is made.

22.3

The things that may be transferred under a transfer scheme include—

22.3.a

property, rights and liabilities that could not otherwise be transferred;

22.3.b

property acquired, and rights and liabilities arising, after the making of the
scheme;

22.3.c

criminal liabilities.

22.4

A transfer scheme may—

22.4.a

create rights, or impose liabilities, in relation to property or rights
transferred;

22.4.b

make provision about the continuing effect of things done by, on behalf of or
in relation to NHS England in respect of anything transferred;

22.4.c

make provision about the continuation of things (including legal proceedings)
in the process of being done by, on behalf of or in relation to NHS England in
respect of anything transferred;

22.4.d

make provision for references to NHS England in an instrument or other
document in respect of anything transferred to be treated as references to the
HSSIB;

22.4.e

make provision for the shared ownership or use of property;

22.4.f

make provision which is the same as or similar to the TUPE regulations;

22.4.g

make other consequential, supplementary, incidental or transitional provision.

22.5

A transfer scheme may provide—

22.5.a

for modifications by agreement;

22.5.b

for modifications to have effect from the date when the original scheme came
into effect.

22.6

In sub-paragraph  (4) (f) , “ the TUPE regulations ” means the Transfer of
Undertakings (Protection of Employment) Regulations 2006 ( S.I. 2006/246 ).

22.7

For the purposes of this paragraph—

22.7.a

references to rights and liabilities include rights and liabilities relating
to a contract of employment;

22.7.b

references to the transfer of property include the grant of a lease.

22.8

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (7) (a) —

22.8.a

an individual who holds employment in the civil service is to be treated as
employed by virtue of a contract of employment, and

22.8.b

the terms of the individual’s employment in the civil service of the State are
to be regarded as constituting the terms of the contract of employment.

23

23.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision varying the way in which a
relevant tax has effect in relation to—

23.1.a

anything transferred under a scheme under paragraph  22 , or

23.1.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, a transfer under such a
scheme.

23.2

The provision which may be made under sub-paragraph  (1) (a)  includes in
particular provision for—

23.2.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything transferred;

23.2.b

anything transferred to be treated in a specified way for the purposes of a
tax provision;

23.2.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything transferred.

23.3

The provision which may be made under sub-paragraph (1)(b) includes in
particular provision for—

23.3.a

a tax provision not to apply, or to apply with modifications, in relation to
anything done for the purposes of or in relation to the transfer;

23.3.b

anything done for the purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer to have or
not have a specified consequence or be treated in a specified way;

23.3.c

the Secretary of State to be required or permitted to determine, or specify
the method for determining, anything which needs to be determined for the
purposes of any tax provision so far as relating to anything done for the
purposes of, or in relation to, the transfer.

23.4

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of the House of Commons.

23.5

In this paragraph references to the transfer of property include the grant of
a lease.

23.6

In this paragraph—

“ relevant tax ” means income tax, corporation tax, capital gains tax, value
added tax, stamp duty or stamp duty reserve tax; “ tax provision ” means a
provision of an enactment about a relevant tax.

Prohibition on disclosure of HSSIB material: exceptions

Section 123

##### Disclosures for purposes of investigations

1

1.1

The HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSB, may disclose protected
material to an individual connected with the HSSIB if—

1.1.a

the person making the disclosure, or

1.1.b

an authorised person,

reasonably believes that the disclosure is necessary for the purposes of the
carrying out of the HSSIB’s investigation function.

1.2

In this paragraph “ authorised person ” means an individual connected with the
HSSIB who is authorised by the HSSIB for the purposes of this paragraph.

2

The HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSIB, may disclose protected
material to a person not connected with the HSSIB if the Chief Investigator
reasonably believes that the disclosure is necessary for the purposes of the
carrying out of the HSSIB’s investigation function.

##### Disclosures relating to prosecution or investigation of offences

3

The HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSIB, may disclose protected
material to a person if the Chief Investigator reasonably believes that the
disclosure is necessary for the purposes of the prosecution or investigation
of an offence under section 121 (offences relating to investigations) or 124
(unlawful disclosure).

##### Disclosures relating to safety risks

4

The HSSIB, or an individual connected with the HSSIB, may disclose protected
material to a person where—

4.a

the Chief Investigator reasonably believes that the disclosure of the material
is necessary to address a serious and continuing risk to the safety of any
patient or to the public,

4.b

the Chief Investigator reasonably believes that the person is in a position to
address the risk, and

4.c

the disclosure is only to the extent necessary to enable the person to take
steps to address the risk.

##### Disclosure by order of the High Court

5

5.1

A person may apply to the High Court for an order that any protected material
be disclosed by the HSSIB to the person for the purposes specified in the
application.

5.2

Those purposes may include onward disclosure by the person making the
application to a person specified in the application.

5.3

The HSSIB may make representations to the High Court about any application
under this paragraph.

5.4

The High Court may make an order on an application under this paragraph only
if it determines that the interests of justice served by the disclosure
outweigh—

5.4.a

any adverse impact on current and future investigations by deterring persons
from providing information for the purposes of investigations, and

5.4.b

any adverse impact on securing the improvement of the safety of health care
services provided to patients in England.

##### Exercise of Chief Investigator’s functions

6

6.1

The Chief Investigator may arrange for the Chief Investigator’s functions
under any provision of this Schedule to be exercised by an investigator.

6.2

An arrangement under this paragraph may relate to a particular case, a
particular class of case or all cases.

##### Guidance

7

7.1

The HSSIB must publish guidance as to—

7.1.a

when it might be appropriate for protected material to be disclosed under
paragraph  2 ,  3 , or  4 ,

7.1.b

the types of protected material which it might be appropriate to disclose
under any such provision, and

7.1.c

the processes which should be used when disclosing protected material under
any such provision.

7.2

If the HSSIB revises the guidance, the HSSIB must publish it as revised.

  Consequential amendments relating to Part 4

Section 134

##### Public Records Act 

1

In Schedule 1 to the Public Records Act 1958 (definition of public records) in
Part 2 of the table in paragraph 3, at the appropriate place insert—

      Health Services Safety Investigations Body (except for any record that
is prohibited from being disclosed by section 122 of the Health and Care Act
2022).

##### Public Bodies (Admission to Meetings) Act 

2

In the Schedule to the Public Bodies (Admission to Meetings) Act 1960 (public
authorities to which that Act applies) in paragraph 1, after paragraph  (p)
(inserted by Schedule 4 to this Act) insert—

2.q

the Health Services Safety Investigations Body.

##### Parliamentary Commissioner Act 

3

In Schedule 2 to the Parliamentary Commissioner Act 1967 (departments etc
subject to investigation) at the appropriate place insert—

      The Health Services Safety Investigations Body.

##### House of Commons Disqualification Act 

4

In Part 3 of Schedule 1 to the House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975
(other disqualifying offices) at the appropriate place insert —

      Chief Investigator, chair or other member of the Health Services Safety
Investigations Body.

##### Copyright, Designs and Patents Act 

5

In section 48(6) of the Copyright, Designs and Patents Act 1988 (material
communicated to the Crown in the course of public business) after “the Care
Quality Commission,” insert  “the Health Services Safety Investigations Body,”
.

##### Employment Rights Act 

6

6.1

The Employment Rights Act 1996 is amended as follows.

6.2

In section 49B(7) (regulations prohibiting discrimination because of protected
disclosure) after paragraph (g) insert—

6.2.ga

the Health Services Safety Investigations Body;

.

6.3

In section 50(8) (right to time off for public duties) after paragraph (ad)
insert—

Storage of gametes and embryos

Section 171

##### Amendments to Human Fertilisation and Embryology Act 1990

###### Introductory

1

The Human Fertilisation and Embryology Act 1990 is amended as follows.

###### Maximum storage periods

2

2.1

Section 14 (conditions of storage licences) is amended as follows.

2.2

In subsection (1), for paragraph (c) substitute—

2.2.c

that the requirements of subsection (3) (maximum storage periods) are met,

.

2.3

For subsections (3) to (5) substitute—

2.3.3

The requirements referred to in subsection (1)(c) are as follows—

2.3.3.a

gametes must not be kept in storage for longer than such period not exceeding
55 years beginning with the day on which they are first placed in storage as
the licence may specify;

2.3.3.b

an embryo must not be kept in storage for treatment purposes for longer than
such period not exceeding 55 years beginning with the day on which it is first
so kept as the licence may specify;

2.3.3.c

an embryo that is kept in storage for the research or training purpose but not
for treatment purposes must not be so kept for longer than such period not
exceeding 10 years beginning with the day on which consent was given under
Schedule 3 to the storage of the embryo for that purpose as the licence may
specify;

2.3.3.d

a human admixed embryo must not be kept in storage for longer than such period
not exceeding 10 years beginning with the day on which it is first placed in
storage as the licence may specify.

2.3.4

Where under Schedule 3 consent is given to the storage of an embryo for the
training or research purpose by different persons on different days, the
reference in subsection (3)(c) to the day on which consent was given is to be
taken as a reference to the last of those days.

2.3.5

For the purposes of this section—

2.3.5.a

“treatment purposes” are purposes referred to in paragraph 2(1)(a) or (b) of
Schedule 3;

2.3.5.b

the “training purpose” is the purpose referred to in paragraph 2(1)(ba) of
that Schedule;

2.3.5.c

the “research purpose” is the purpose referred to in paragraph 2(1)(c) of that
Schedule.

3

In section 47 (index), omit the entry for the “Statutory storage period”.

4

In Schedule 3 (consents), in paragraph 2(2)(a), for “statutory storage period”
substitute  “period for which, by virtue of section 14(3), the gametes, embryo
or human admixed embryo may be stored under the licence” .

###### Disposal of material

5

In section 14 (conditions of storage licences), in subsection (1), after
paragraph (c) insert—

5.ca

that any gametes, embryos or human admixed embryos that have been kept in
storage pursuant to the licence must, once they may no longer lawfully be so
kept, be removed from storage and disposed of, and

.

6

In section 17 (the person responsible), in subsection (1)(c), for “allowed to
perish” substitute  “removed from storage” .

###### Consent to storage

7

7.1

Schedule 3 (consents) is amended as follows.

7.2

In paragraph 1—

7.2.a

in sub-paragraph (1), before the first “and” insert  “any renewal of consent,”
;

7.2.b

in sub-paragraph (2), before the first “and” insert  “any renewal of consent
by a person unable to sign,” ;

7.2.c

in sub-paragraph (3)—

7.2.c.i

the words from ““effective consent” to the end become paragraph (a);

7.2.c.ii

after that paragraph insert—

7.2.c.ii.b

references to renewal of consent are to renewal of consent to the storage of
any gametes or embryo under paragraph 11A or 11C.

7.3

In paragraph 3, in sub-paragraph (1), after “gives” insert  “or renews” .

7.4

After paragraph 11 insert—

############ Renewal of consent to storage of gametes

7.4.11A

7.4.11A.1

This paragraph applies where—

7.4.11A.1.a

the gametes of a person (“ P ”) are in storage,

7.4.11A.1.b

P’s consent to the storage of the gametes is required under paragraph 8(1),

7.4.11A.1.c

there is effective consent from P to the storage of the gametes, and

7.4.11A.1.d

the gametes are being kept for use for the purposes of providing treatment
services to—

7.4.11A.1.d.i

P, or

7.4.11A.1.d.ii

P and another person together.

7.4.11A.2

The person keeping the gametes in storage (“ K ”) must, in each consent
period, request P to renew consent to storage of the gametes within the
renewal period.

For the meaning of “consent period” and “renewal period”, see paragraph 11B.

7.4.11A.3

A request under sub-paragraph  (2)  must be given in writing before the start
of the renewal period.

7.4.11A.4

The duty in sub-paragraph  (2)  ceases to apply if K is notified that P has
died.

7.4.11A.5

The duty in sub-paragraph  (2)  does not apply in relation to any consent
period if—

7.4.11A.5.a

K has at any time been informed in writing that P has been certified as
lacking capacity to renew consent to storage of the gametes, and

7.4.11A.5.b

K has not subsequently been informed in writing, before the start of the
renewal period which relates to that consent period, that P has been certified
as having capacity to renew consent to storage of the gametes.

7.4.11A.6

P renews consent by informing K in writing that P consents to the storage of
the gametes.

7.4.11A.7

If P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph  (6)  before the end of the
consent period, K must, as soon as possible after the end of that period, give
a notice to P stating that if P does not renew consent before the end of the
renewal period, the gametes will be removed from storage and disposed of.

7.4.11A.8

P’s consent to the storage of the gametes is to be taken as having been
withdrawn at the end of a renewal period that relates to a consent period if—

7.4.11A.8.a

K has complied with the requirements of sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (7)  in
relation to that consent period, and

7.4.11A.8.b

P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph  (6)  before the end of the
renewal period.

But this is subject to sub-paragraphs  (9)  and  (10) .

7.4.11A.9

If, in a case referred to in sub-paragraph  (8)(a)  and  (b) , P dies before
the end of the renewal period—

7.4.11A.9.a

P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (8) , but

7.4.11A.9.b

if at the end of the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P died
there is still effective consent from P to the storage, P’s consent is to be
taken as withdrawn at that time.

7.4.11A.10

If, in a case referred to in sub-paragraph  (8)(a)  and  (b) , before the end
of the renewal period P is certified as lacking capacity to renew consent—

7.4.11A.10.a

P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (8) , but

7.4.11A.10.b

if at the end of the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P was
so certified there is still effective consent from P to the storage, P’s
consent is to be taken as withdrawn at that time.

7.4.11A.11

But P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (10)(b)
if, before the time it would be taken to be withdrawn under that sub-
paragraph—

7.4.11A.11.a

P is certified as having capacity to renew consent to storage of the gametes,
and

7.4.11A.11.b

P renews consent to storage of the gametes by informing K in writing that P
consents to their storage.

7.4.11A.12

In a case where P renews consent under sub-paragraph  (11)(b) , this paragraph
applies subsequently as if references to a consent period were to—

7.4.11A.12.a

the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P so renewed consent,
and

7.4.11A.12.b

each successive period of 10 years.

7.4.11B

7.4.11B.1

For the purposes of paragraph 11A, each of the following is a “consent
period”—

7.4.11B.1.a

the period of 10 years beginning with the relevant day, and

7.4.11B.1.b

each successive period of 10 years.

7.4.11B.2

In sub-paragraph  (1)(a)  “ relevant day ” means—

7.4.11B.2.a

the day on which the gametes are first placed in storage, or

7.4.11B.2.b

in a case where sub-paragraph  (3)  or  (5)  applies, the day on which P gives
consent to the storage of the gametes.

7.4.11B.3

This sub-paragraph applies where the gametes are taken from or provided by P
before P attains the age of 18 years and, at the time the gametes are first
stored—

7.4.11B.3.a

P has not attained the age of 16 years and is not competent to deal with the
issue of consent to storage of the gametes, or

7.4.11B.3.b

P has attained that age but, although not lacking capacity to consent to the
storage of the gametes, is not competent to deal with the issue of consent to
their storage.

7.4.11B.4

In relation to Scotland, sub-paragraph  (3)  is to be read as if, for
paragraphs (a) and (b), there were substituted  “P does not have capacity
(within the meaning of section 2(4) of the Age of Legal Capacity (Scotland)
Act 1991) to consent to storage of the gametes” .

7.4.11B.5

This sub-paragraph applies where the gametes are taken from or provided by P
after P attains the age of 16 years and, at the time the gametes are first
stored, P lacks capacity to consent to their storage.

7.4.11B.6

In paragraph  11A  “ the renewal period ”, in relation to a consent period,
means the period which—

7.4.11B.6.a

begins 12 months before the end of the consent period, and

7.4.11B.6.b

ends 6 months after the end of the consent period.

7.4.11B.7

In paragraph  11A  “ certified ” means certified in writing by a registered
medical practitioner.

7.4.11B.8

In paragraph  11A  and this paragraph, in relation to Scotland, references to
a person lacking or having capacity to consent or renew consent are to be read
as references to the person being or not being incapable (within the meaning
of section 1(6) of the Adults with Incapacity (Scotland) Act 2000) of
consenting or renewing consent.

############ Renewal of consent to storage of embryos

7.4.11C

7.4.11C.1

This paragraph applies where—

7.4.11C.1.a

an embryo, the creation of which was brought about  in vitro , is in storage,

7.4.11C.1.b

the embryo is being kept for use for the purposes of providing treatment
services to—

7.4.11C.1.b.i

a person (“ P ”) whose gametes or human cells were used to bring about the
creation of the embryo, or

7.4.11C.1.b.ii

P and another person together,

7.4.11C.1.c

P’s consent to the storage of the embryo is required under paragraph 8(2), and

7.4.11C.1.d

there is effective consent from P to the storage of the embryo.

7.4.11C.2

The person keeping the embryo in storage (“ K ”) must, in each consent period,
request P to renew consent to storage of the embryo within the renewal period.

For the meaning of “consent period” and “renewal period”, see paragraph 11D.

7.4.11C.3

A request under sub-paragraph  (2)  must be given in writing before the start
of the renewal period.

7.4.11C.4

The duty in sub-paragraph  (2)  ceases to apply if—

7.4.11C.4.a

K is notified that P has died, or

7.4.11C.4.b

K is notified under paragraph 4A(1)(c) of the withdrawal of a person’s consent
to storage of the embryo.

7.4.11C.5

The duty in sub-paragraph  (2)  does not apply in relation to any consent
period if—

7.4.11C.5.a

K has at any time been informed in writing that P has been certified as
lacking capacity to renew consent to storage of the embryo, and

7.4.11C.5.b

K has not subsequently been informed in writing, before the start of the
renewal period which relates to that consent period, that P has been certified
as having capacity to renew consent to storage of the embryo.

7.4.11C.6

P renews consent by informing K in writing that P consents to the storage of
the embryo.

7.4.11C.7

If P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph  (6)  before the end of the
consent period, K must, as soon as possible after the end of that period, give
a notice to P stating that if P does not renew consent before the end of the
renewal period, the embryo will be removed from storage and disposed of.

7.4.11C.8

P’s consent to the storage of the embryo is to be taken as having been
withdrawn at the end of a renewal period that relates to a consent period if—

7.4.11C.8.a

K has complied with the requirements of sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (7)  in
relation to that consent period, and

7.4.11C.8.b

P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph  (6)  before the end of the
renewal period.

But this is subject to sub-paragraphs  (9)  and  (10) .

7.4.11C.9

If, in a case referred to in sub-paragraph  (8)(a)  and  (b) , P dies before
the end of the renewal period—

7.4.11C.9.a

P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (8) , but

7.4.11C.9.b

if at the end of the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P died
there is still effective consent from P to the storage, P’s consent is to be
taken as withdrawn at that time.

7.4.11C.10

If, in a case referred to in sub-paragraph  (8)(a)  and  (b) , before the end
of the renewal period P is certified as lacking capacity to renew consent—

7.4.11C.10.a

P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (8) , but

7.4.11C.10.b

if at the end of the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P was
so certified there is still effective consent from P to the storage, P’s
consent is to be taken as withdrawn at that time.

7.4.11C.11

But P’s consent is not to be taken as withdrawn under sub-paragraph  (10)(b)
if, before the time it would be taken to be withdrawn under that sub-
paragraph—

7.4.11C.11.a

P is certified as having capacity to renew consent to storage of the embryo,
and

7.4.11C.11.b

P renews consent to storage of the embryo by informing K in writing that P
consents to its storage.

7.4.11C.12

In a case where P has renewed consent under sub-paragraph  (11)(b) , this
paragraph applies subsequently as if references to the consent period were to—

7.4.11C.12.a

the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which P so renewed consent,
and

7.4.11C.12.b

each successive period of 10 years.

7.4.11C.13

Where P’s consent is taken as withdrawn under this paragraph, K must, as soon
as possible, take all reasonable steps to give notice of the withdrawal to
each person whose gametes or human cells were used to bring about its
creation.

7.4.11C.14

Storage of the embryo remains lawful until—

7.4.11C.14.a

the end of the period of 6 months beginning with the day on which P’s consent
is taken as withdrawn under this paragraph, or

7.4.11C.14.b

if, before the end of that period, K receives a notice from each person
notified under sub-paragraph  (13)  stating that the person consents to the
disposal of the embryo, the time at which the last of those notices was
received.

7.4.11D

7.4.11D.1

For the purposes of paragraph  11C , each of the following is a “consent
period”—

7.4.11D.1.a

the period of 10 years beginning with the day on which the embryo is first
placed in storage, and

7.4.11D.1.b

each successive period of 10 years.

7.4.11D.2

In paragraph  11C  “ the renewal period ”, in relation to a consent period,
means the period which—

7.4.11D.2.a

begins 12 months before the end of the consent period, and

7.4.11D.2.b

ends 6 months after the end of the consent period.

7.4.11D.3

In paragraph  11C  “ certified ” means certified in writing by a registered
medical practitioner.

7.4.11D.4

In paragraph  11C , in relation to Scotland, references to a person lacking or
having capacity to renew consent are to be read as references to the person
being or not being incapable (within the meaning of section 1(6) of the Adults
with Incapacity (Scotland) Act 2000) of renewing consent.

##### Transitional provision

###### Interpretation

8

8.1

In this Part of this Schedule—

“ the commencement day ” means 1 July 2022; “ the transitional period ” means
the period beginning with the commencement day and ending with 30 June 2024.

8.2

In this Part of this Schedule—

“ the 1990 Act ” means the Human Fertilisation and Embryology Act 1990; “ the
2009 Regulations ” means the Human Fertilisation and Embryology (Statutory
Storage Period for Embryos and Gametes) Regulations 2009 ( S.I. 2009/1582 ); “
the 2020 Regulations ” means the Human Fertilisation and Embryology (Statutory
Storage Period for Embryos and Gametes) (Coronavirus) Regulations 2020 ( S.I.
2020/566 ).

8.3

In this Part of this Schedule—

“ gamete storage licence ” means a licence under Schedule 2 to the 1990 Act
that authorises the storage of gametes; “ embryo storage licence ” means a
licence under Schedule 2 to the 1990 Act that authorises the storage of
embryos; “ storage licence ” means a licence under Schedule 2 to the 1990 Act
that authorises the storage of gametes, embryos or human admixed embryos; “
pre-commencement ”, in relation to a storage licence, or a storage licence of
any description, means granted before the commencement day and “ post-
commencement ” means granted on or after that day.

8.4

In this Part of this Schedule—

“ statutory storage period ” has the same meaning as in the 1990 Act
immediately before the commencement day; references to gametes, embryos and
human admixed embryos have the same meaning as in that Act; “ the training
purpose ”, “ the research purpose ” and “ treatment purposes ” have the same
meanings as in section 14(3)(c) of that Act.

###### Application of Part 1 to material already in storage

9

9.1

The amendments in paragraphs  2  to  6  of this Schedule have effect in
relation to pre-commencement storage licences under which gametes, embryos or
human admixed embryos are kept in storage on or after the commencement day (as
well as having effect in relation to post-commencement storage licences).

This is subject to sub-paragraphs (2) and (3).

9.2

In the case of a pre-commencement embryo storage licence, the condition
imposed by section 14(3)(c) of the 1990 Act (as substituted by paragraph  2
of this Schedule) does not apply in relation to an embryo which, on the
commencement day, is kept in storage for the training or research purpose but
not for treatment purposes.

9.3

In the case of any pre-commencement storage licence, the condition imposed by
section 14(1)(ca) of the 1990 Act (as substituted by paragraph  5  of this
Schedule) applies only in relation to times on or after the commencement day.

10

The amendments made by paragraph  7  of this Schedule have effect in relation
to the storage of gametes and embryos under a pre-commencement gamete or
embryo storage licence, where the gametes or embryos are kept in storage on or
after the commencement day (as well as having effect in relation to the
storage of gametes and embryos under a post-commencement gamete or embryo
storage licence).

###### Date of first storage

11

11.1

This paragraph applies if the person storing gametes or an embyro under a pre-
commencement gamete or embryo storage licence—

11.1.a

has, before the end of the transitional period, taken all reasonable steps to
establish the date on which the gametes were or embryo was first placed in
storage, but

11.1.b

is unable to establish that date.

11.2

The person may give a notice to each person whose consent to the storage is
required under Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act specifying a date on which the
gametes are or embryo is to be regarded as having been first placed in
storage.

11.3

Where notice is given under sub-paragraph (2), the gametes are or embryo is to
be regarded, for all purposes of the 1990 Act and this Part of this Schedule,
as having been first placed in storage on the date specified in the notice.

###### Storage periods specified in pre-commencement storage licences

12

12.1

For the purposes of section 14(3)(a) of the 1990 Act (as substituted by
paragraph  2  of this Schedule), a pre-commencement gamete storage licence
under which, on and after the commencement day, gametes are kept in storage is
to be regarded as specifying the period of 55 years beginning with the day on
which the gametes were first placed in storage.

12.2

For the purposes of section 14(3)(b) of the 1990 Act (as substituted by
paragraph  2  of this Schedule), a pre-commencement embryo storage licence
under which, on and after the commencement day, an embryo is kept in storage
for treatment purposes is to be regarded as specifying for those purposes the
period of 55 years beginning with the day on which the embryo was first so
kept.

###### Storage after expiry of pre-commencement consent

13

13.1

If a pre-commencement consent to the storage of gametes or an embryo expires
at any time in the transitional period, the storage of the gametes or embryo
for the remainder of that period is not unlawful merely because of that fact.

13.2

In sub-paragraph (1)—

13.2.a

“ pre-commencement consent ” means consent given under Schedule 3 to the 1990
Act before the commencement day;

13.2.b

the reference to expiry of consent does not include withdrawal.

###### Storage with no effective consent prior to commencement

14

14.1

This paragraph applies in relation to the storage of gametes or an embryo
under a pre-commencement gamete or embryo storage licence where, immediately
before the commencement day, there is no effective consent to the storage by a
relevant person.

14.2

The person keeping the gametes or embryo in storage must request the relevant
person to give consent to the storage under Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act.

14.3

A request under sub-paragraph  (2)  must be given before 1 July 2023 in
writing.

14.4

The storage of the gametes or embryo at any time before the end of the
transitional period is not unlawful merely because there is no effective
consent to the storage by the relevant person.

14.5

In this paragraph—

“ effective consent ” means consent under Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act which has
not been withdrawn; “ relevant person ” means a person whose consent is
required under Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act to storage of the gametes or embryo.

###### Time for first renewal of consent

15

15.1

This paragraph applies in relation to the storage of gametes under a pre-
commencement gamete storage licence where the statutory storage period
applicable immediately before the commencement day was provided for by—

15.1.a

regulation 4, 4A, 7 or 8 of the 2009 Regulations, or

15.1.b

regulation 4 of the 2020 Regulations.

15.2

For the purposes of paragraph  11A  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act (as inserted
by paragraph  7  of this Schedule), paragraph  11B(1)(a)  of that Schedule has
effect as if the reference to the period of 10 years beginning with the
relevant day were a reference to the period which—

15.2.a

begins with the relevant day, and

15.2.b

ends at the end of the statutory storage period referred to in sub-paragraph
(1) .

16

16.1

This paragraph applies in relation to the storage of an embryo under a pre-
commencement embryo storage licence where the statutory storage period
applicable immediately before the commencement day was provided for by—

16.1.a

regulation 3, 3A, 5 or 6 of the 2009 Regulations, or

16.1.b

regulation 3 of the 2020 Regulations.

16.2

For the purposes of paragraph  11C  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act (as inserted
by paragraph 7 of this Schedule), paragraph  11D(1)(a)  of that Schedule has
effect as if the reference to the period of 10 years beginning with the day on
which the embryo was first placed in storage were a reference to the period
which—

16.2.a

begins with the day on which the embryo was first so placed, and

16.2.b

ends at the end of the statutory storage period referred to in sub-paragraph
(1) .

###### Renewals falling due in the transitional period

17

17.1

This paragraph applies in relation to the storage of gametes under a pre-
commencement gamete storage licence in a case where—

17.1.a

paragraph  11A  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act applies in relation to the
storage, and

17.1.b

for the purposes of that paragraph, the first consent period (see paragraph
11B(1)(a)  of that Schedule) ends in the transitional period.

17.2

Where this paragraph applies, paragraph  11A  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act
has effect in relation to that first consent period as if—

17.2.a

for sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  there were substituted—

17.2.a.2

The person keeping the gametes in storage (“ K ”) must request P to renew
consent to storage of the gametes before 1 July 2024.

17.2.a.3

A request under sub-paragraph (2) must—

17.2.a.3.a

be given in writing before 1 July 2023;

17.2.a.3.b

state that if P does not renew consent before 1 July 2024, the gametes will be
removed from storage and disposed of.

;

17.2.b

in sub-paragraph  (5)(b) , for “the start of the renewal period which relates
to that consent period” there were substituted  “1 July 2023” ;

17.2.c

sub-paragraph  (7)  were omitted;

17.2.d

for sub-paragraph  (8)  there were substituted—

17.2.d.8

P’s consent to the storage of the gametes is to be taken as having been
withdrawn at the beginning of 1 July 2024 if—

17.2.d.8.a

K has complied with sub-paragraph (2), and

17.2.d.8.b

P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph (6) before 1 July 2024.

But this is subject to sub-paragraphs (9) and (10).

;

17.2.e

in sub-paragraphs  (9)  and  (10) , references to the end of the renewal
period were to 1 July 2024.

18

18.1

This paragraph applies in relation to the storage of an embryo under a pre-
commencement embryo storage licence in a case where—

18.1.a

paragraph  11C  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act applies in relation to the
storage, and

18.1.b

for the purposes of that paragraph, the first consent period (see paragraph
11D(1)(a)  of that Schedule) ends in the transitional period.

18.2

Where this paragraph applies, paragraph  11C  of Schedule 3 to the 1990 Act
has effect in relation to that first consent period as if—

18.2.a

for sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  there were substituted—

18.2.a.2

The person keeping the embryo in storage (“ K ”) must request P to renew
consent to storage of the embryo before 1 July 2024.

18.2.a.3

A request under sub-paragraph (2) must—

18.2.a.3.a

be given in writing before 1 July 2023;

18.2.a.3.b

state that if P does not renew consent before 1 July 2024, the embryo will be
removed from storage and disposed of.

;

18.2.b

in sub-paragraph  (5)(b) , for “the start of the renewal period which relates
to that consent period” there were substituted  “1 July 2023” ;

18.2.c

sub-paragraph  (7)  were omitted;

18.2.d

for sub-paragraph  (8)  there were substituted—

18.2.d.8

P’s consent to the storage of the embryo is to be taken as having been
withdrawn at the beginning of 1 July 2024 if—

18.2.d.8.a

K has complied with sub-paragraph (2), and

18.2.d.8.b

P’s consent is not renewed under sub-paragraph (6) before 1 July 2024.

But this is subject to sub-paragraphs (9) and (10).

;

18.2.e

in sub-paragraphs  (9)  and  (10) , references to the end of the renewal
period were to 1 July 2024.

  Advertising of less healthy food and drink

Section 172

##### Programme services: watershed

###### Television programme services

1

After section 321 of the Communications Act 2003 insert—

########## Objectives for advertisements: less healthy food and drink

1.321A

1.321A.1

OFCOM must set standards by virtue of section 321(1)(b) prohibiting television
programme services provided between 5.30 am and 9.00 pm from including
advertisements for an identifiable less healthy food or drink product, except
as provided for by subsection  (3) .

1.321A.2

OFCOM must ensure that the prohibition provided for by the first standards set
by virtue of subsection  (1)  takes effect from the beginning of 1 January
2023.

1.321A.3

Standards set by virtue of subsection  (1)  must exempt from the prohibition
imposed by them—

1.321A.3.a

advertisements included in television programme services as a result of
arrangements made by or on behalf of a person who is, at the time when the
arrangements are made, a food or drink SME;

1.321A.3.b

advertisements prescribed in any regulations made by the Secretary of State
under this paragraph.

1.321A.4

For the purposes of this section—

1.321A.4.a

“ advertisements ” includes advertisements under a sponsorship agreement and
anything else which, under a sponsorship agreement, is included in a
television programme service, other than in a television programme;

1.321A.4.b

a product is “ identifiable ”, in relation to advertisements, if persons in
the United Kingdom (or any part of the United Kingdom) could reasonably be
expected to be able to identify the advertisements as being for that product;

1.321A.4.c

a food or drink product is “less healthy” if—

1.321A.4.c.i

it falls within a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary
of State, and

1.321A.4.c.ii

it is “less healthy” in accordance with the relevant guidance;

1.321A.4.d

“the relevant guidance” is the guidance entitled “Nutrient Profiling Technical
Guidance” published by the Department of Health on 1 January 2011;

1.321A.4.e

“ food or drink SME ” means a small or medium enterprise, within the meaning
given by regulations made by the Secretary of State, of a description
specified in the regulations.

1.321A.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)(e)  that make provision by reference to the
number of members of staff of a person may make provision about who is to
count as a member of staff (including members of staff of another person).

1.321A.6

The Secretary of State may, before the date specified in subsection  (2) ,
amend that subsection so as to substitute a later date for the date that is
for the time being specified there.

1.321A.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section to change the
meaning of “the relevant guidance”.

1.321A.8

Before making regulations under subsection (3)(b) or  (7) , the Secretary of
State must consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

1.321A.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (7)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

###### On-demand programme services

2

After section 368F of the Communications Act 2003 insert—

########## Advertising: less healthy food and drink

2.368FA

2.368FA.1

From the beginning of 1 January 2023, on-demand programme services must not,
between 5.30 am and 9.00 pm, include advertisements for an identifiable less
healthy food or drink product.

2.368FA.2

The prohibition imposed by subsection  (1)  does not apply in relation to
advertisements included in on-demand programme services as a result of
arrangements made by or on behalf of a person who is, at the time when the
arrangements are made, a food or drink SME.

2.368FA.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for further exemptions from
the prohibition imposed by subsection  (1) .

2.368FA.4

For the purposes of this section—

2.368FA.4.a

“ advertisements ” includes advertisements and sponsorship announcements
(within the meaning given by section 368G(17)) under a sponsorship agreement;

2.368FA.4.b

a product is “ identifiable ”, in relation to advertisements, if persons in
the United Kingdom (or any part of the United Kingdom) could reasonably be
expected to be able to identify the advertisements as being for that product;

2.368FA.4.c

a food or drink product is “less healthy” if—

2.368FA.4.c.i

it falls within a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary
of State, and

2.368FA.4.c.ii

it is “less healthy” in accordance with the relevant guidance;

2.368FA.4.d

“ the relevant guidance ” means the guidance entitled “Nutrient Profiling
Technical Guidance” published by the Department of Health on 1 January 2011;

2.368FA.4.e

“ food or drink SME ” means a small or medium enterprise, within the meaning
given by regulations made by the Secretary of State, of a description
specified in the regulations.

2.368FA.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)(e)  that make provision by reference to the
number of members of staff of a person may make provision about who is to
count as a member of staff (including members of staff of another person).

2.368FA.6

The Secretary of State may, before the date specified in subsection  (1) ,
amend that subsection so as to substitute a later date for the date that is
for the time being specified there.

2.368FA.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section to change the
meaning of “the relevant guidance”.

2.368FA.8

Before making regulations under subsection  (3)  or  (7) , the Secretary of
State must consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

2.368FA.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (7)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

##### Online services: prohibition

3

In the Communications Act 2003, after Part 4B insert—

######### Online advertising of less healthy food and drink

########## Advertising of less healthy food and drink

########### Prohibition of paid-for advertising of less healthy food and drink

3.368Z14

3.368Z14.1

From the beginning of 1 January 2023, a person must not pay for advertisements
for an identifiable less healthy food or drink product to be placed on the
internet.

3.368Z14.2

Subsection  (1)  does not apply where the person paying is, at the time when
the payment is made, a food or drink SME.

3.368Z14.3

Subsection  (1)  does not apply—

3.368Z14.3.a

in relation to advertisements which are directed solely at persons who are
engaged in, or employed by, a business which involves or is associated with
the manufacture or sale of food or drink,

3.368Z14.3.b

in relation to advertisements included in on-demand programme services (as to
which, see section  368FA ),

3.368Z14.3.c

in relation to advertisements included in services connected to regulated
radio services, or

3.368Z14.3.d

in relation to advertisements which are not intended to be accessed
principally by persons in any part of the United Kingdom.

3.368Z14.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for further exemptions from
the prohibition imposed by subsection  (1) .

3.368Z14.5

For the purposes of this section—

3.368Z14.5.a

paying includes providing any consideration (monetary or non-monetary);

3.368Z14.5.b

“ placed ” includes continues to be placed;

3.368Z14.5.c

paying for advertisements to be placed on the internet includes paying under a
sponsorship agreement as result of which advertisements are placed on the
internet;

3.368Z14.5.d

a product is “ identifiable ”, in relation to advertisements, if persons in
the United Kingdom (or any part of the United Kingdom) could reasonably be
expected to be able to identify the advertisements as being for that product;

3.368Z14.5.e

a food or drink product is “less healthy” if—

3.368Z14.5.e.i

it falls within a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary
of State, and

3.368Z14.5.e.ii

it is “less healthy” in accordance with the relevant guidance;

3.368Z14.5.f

“the relevant guidance” is the guidance entitled “Nutrient Profiling Technical
Guidance” published by the Department of Health on 1 January 2011;

3.368Z14.5.g

“ food or drink SME ” means a small or medium enterprise, within the meaning
given by regulations made by the Secretary of State, of a description
specified in the regulations;

3.368Z14.5.h

“ services connected to regulated radio services ” has the meaning given by
regulations made by the Secretary of State.

3.368Z14.6

Regulations under subsection  (5)(g)  that make provision by reference to the
number of members of staff of a person may make provision about who is to
count as a member of staff (including members of staff of another person).

3.368Z14.7

The Secretary of State may, before the date specified in subsection (1)—

3.368Z14.7.a

amend that subsection so as to substitute a later date for the date that is
for the time being specified there, and

3.368Z14.7.b

make corresponding amendments to the references to that date in subsections
(11)  and  (12) .

3.368Z14.8

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section to change the
meaning of “the relevant guidance”.

3.368Z14.9

Before making regulations under subsection  (4)  or  (8) , the Secretary of
State must consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

3.368Z14.10

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (8)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

3.368Z14.11

A person is to be treated as having contravened subsection  (1)  if—

3.368Z14.11.a

at any time on or after 1 August 2021 but before 1 January 2023, the person
made a payment for advertisements to be placed on the internet on or after 1
January 2023, and

3.368Z14.11.b

if the payment had been made on 1 January 2023, the person would have
contravened subsection  (1) .

3.368Z14.12

Subsection  (11)  does not apply if the person—

3.368Z14.12.a

has put in place arrangements to ensure that they are entitled to require that
the advertisements are not placed on the internet on or after 1 January 2023,
and

3.368Z14.12.b

uses all reasonable endeavours to ensure that the advertisements are not so
placed.

########### Enforcement

3.368Z15

3.368Z15.1

Where the appropriate regulatory authority determine that a person is
contravening or has contravened section  368Z14  they may do one or both of
the following—

3.368Z15.1.a

give the person an enforcement notification;

3.368Z15.1.b

impose a financial penalty on the person in accordance with section  368Z16 .

3.368Z15.2

The appropriate regulatory authority must not make a determination as
mentioned in subsection  (1)  unless—

3.368Z15.2.a

there are reasonable grounds for believing that a contravention of section
368Z14  is occurring or has occurred, and

3.368Z15.2.b

they have allowed the person an opportunity to make representations about that
apparent contravention.

3.368Z15.3

An enforcement notification is a notification which—

3.368Z15.3.a

specifies the determination made as mentioned in subsection (1),

3.368Z15.3.b

imposes requirements on the person to take such steps for complying with
section  368Z14  and for remedying the consequences of the contravention as
may be specified in the notification,

3.368Z15.3.c

fixes a reasonable period for the taking of those steps, and

3.368Z15.3.d

sets out the reasons for the appropriate regulatory authority’s decision to
give the enforcement notification.

3.368Z15.4

The requirements specified in an enforcement notification may include
requirements to do one or more of the following—

3.368Z15.4.a

instruct or request specified persons to remove specified advertisements from
the internet;

3.368Z15.4.b

arrange for specified advertisements to be modified in specified ways.

3.368Z15.5

A person to whom an enforcement notification is given must comply with it.

3.368Z15.6

The duty under subsection  (5)  is enforceable in civil proceedings by the
appropriate regulatory authority—

3.368Z15.6.a

for an injunction,

3.368Z15.6.b

for specific performance of a statutory duty under section 45 of the Court of
Session Act 1988, or

3.368Z15.6.c

for any other appropriate remedy or relief.

3.368Z15.7

If a person to whom an enforcement notification has been given does not comply
with it, the appropriate regulatory authority may impose a financial penalty
on that person in accordance with section  368Z16 .

########### Financial penalties

3.368Z16

3.368Z16.1

The amount of a penalty imposed on a person under section  368Z15  is to be
such amount not exceeding the maximum penalty as the appropriate regulatory
authority determine to be—

3.368Z16.1.a

appropriate, and

3.368Z16.1.b

proportionate to the contravention in respect of which it is imposed.

3.368Z16.2

The maximum penalty is—

3.368Z16.2.a

in a case in which the person carries on a relevant business, an amount not
exceeding the greater of—

3.368Z16.2.a.i

5% of the turnover of the person’s relevant business for the relevant period,
and

3.368Z16.2.a.ii

£250,000;

3.368Z16.2.b

in any other case, £250,000.

3.368Z16.3

For the purposes of this section—

3.368Z16.3.a

a person’s “relevant business” is so much of any business carried on by the
person as involves or is associated with the manufacture or sale of less
healthy food or drink products;

3.368Z16.3.b

“ relevant period ”, in relation to a person’s relevant business, means—

3.368Z16.3.b.i

except in a case falling within sub-paragraph  (ii)  or  (iii) , the period of
one year ending with the 31 March before the time at which the penalty is
imposed;

3.368Z16.3.b.ii

in the case of a person who at the time at which the penalty is imposed has
been carrying on that business for a period of less than a year, the period,
ending with that time, during which the person has been carrying it on;

3.368Z16.3.b.iii

in the case of a person who at the time at which the penalty is imposed has
ceased to carry on that business, the period of one year ending with the time
when the person ceased to carry it on;

3.368Z16.3.c

the amount of the turnover of a person’s relevant business for the relevant
period is to be calculated by the appropriate regulatory authority in
accordance with the following sub-paragraphs—

3.368Z16.3.c.i

the amount is to be calculated in conformity with accounting practices and
principles which are generally accepted in the United Kingdom;

3.368Z16.3.c.ii

the amount is limited to the amounts derived by the person from the relevant
business after deduction of sales rebates, value added tax and other taxes
directly related to turnover;

3.368Z16.3.c.iii

where the person’s relevant business consists of two or more undertakings that
each prepare accounts, the amount is to be calculated by adding together the
turnover of each, save that no account is to be taken of any turnover
resulting from the supply of goods or the provision of services between them.

3.368Z16.4

In determining the amount of a penalty under subsection  (1)  the appropriate
regulatory authority must have regard to any statement published by OFCOM
under section 392 (guidelines to be followed in determining amount of
penalties).

3.368Z16.5

A financial penalty imposed under this section, if not paid within the period
fixed by the appropriate regulatory authority, is to be recoverable by the
appropriate regulatory authority as a debt due to them from the person obliged
to pay it.

3.368Z16.6

Where a financial penalty is imposed under this section in respect of matters
appearing to OFCOM to have a connection with Northern Ireland and no
connection with the rest of the United Kingdom, the penalty must be paid into
the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland.

3.368Z16.7

In any other case, a financial penalty imposed under this section is to be
paid into the Consolidated Fund of the United Kingdom.

########### Power to demand information

3.368Z17

3.368Z17.1

The appropriate regulatory authority may give a person a notice demanding
information that the authority require for the purpose of carrying out their
functions under this Part.

3.368Z17.2

The notice may relate to any information that the person appears to have or be
able to generate.

3.368Z17.3

A notice under this section must—

3.368Z17.3.a

describe the required information,

3.368Z17.3.b

fix a reasonable period within which the information is to be provided, and

3.368Z17.3.c

set out the appropriate regulatory authority’s reasons for requiring it.

3.368Z17.4

A notice under this section may specify the manner in which the information is
to be provided.

3.368Z17.5

The appropriate regulatory authority may not require the provision of
information under this section unless they have given the person from whom it
is required an opportunity of making representations to them about the matters
appearing to them to provide grounds for making the request.

3.368Z17.6

Section  368Z15  applies in relation to a failure to comply with a demand for
information imposed under this section as if that failure were a contravention
of section  368Z14 .

3.368Z17.7

In this section “ information ” includes copies of advertisements.

########### Guidance

3.368Z18

3.368Z18.1

The appropriate regulatory authority must draw up and, from time to time,
review and revise, guidance setting out their intentions concerning the
exercise of their functions under this Part.

3.368Z18.2

The appropriate regulatory authority must consult the Secretary of State
before drawing up or revising the guidance.

3.368Z18.3

The appropriate regulatory authority must publish the guidance and any revised
guidance in such manner as they consider appropriate for bringing it to the
attention of the persons who, in their opinion, are likely to be affected by
it.

########### The appropriate regulatory authority

3.368Z19

3.368Z19.1

OFCOM may designate any body corporate to be, to the extent provided by the
designation, the appropriate regulatory authority for the purposes of any
provision of this Part, subject to subsection  (9) .

3.368Z19.2

To the extent that no body is designated for a purpose, OFCOM is the
appropriate regulatory authority for that purpose.

3.368Z19.3

Where a body is designated for a purpose, OFCOM may act as the appropriate
regulatory authority for that purpose concurrently with or in place of that
body.

3.368Z19.4

OFCOM may provide a designated body with assistance (including financial
assistance) in connection with any of the functions of the body under this
Part.

3.368Z19.5

A designation may in particular—

3.368Z19.5.a

provide for a body to be the appropriate regulatory authority in relation to
advertisements of a specified description;

3.368Z19.5.b

provide that a function of the appropriate regulatory authority is exercisable
by the designated body—

3.368Z19.5.b.i

to such extent as may be specified;

3.368Z19.5.b.ii

either generally or in such circumstances as may be specified;

3.368Z19.5.b.iii

either unconditionally or subject to such conditions as may be specified.

3.368Z19.6

The conditions that may be specified pursuant to subsection  (5)(b)(iii)
include a condition to the effect that a function may, generally or in
specified circumstances, be exercised by the body only with the agreement of
OFCOM.

3.368Z19.7

A designation has effect for such period as may be specified and may be
revoked by OFCOM at any time.

3.368Z19.8

OFCOM must publish any designation in such manner as they consider appropriate
for bringing it to the attention of persons who, in their opinion, are likely
to be affected by it.

3.368Z19.9

OFCOM may not designate a body unless, as respects that designation, they are
satisfied that the body—

3.368Z19.9.a

is a fit and proper body to be designated,

3.368Z19.9.b

has consented to being designated,

3.368Z19.9.c

has access to financial resources that are adequate to ensure the effective
performance of its functions as the appropriate regulatory authority (taking
into account any financial assistance that OFCOM intends to provide under
subsection  (4) ),

3.368Z19.9.d

is sufficiently independent of persons who carry on business that involves or
is associated with the manufacture or sale of less healthy food or drink
products, and

3.368Z19.9.e

will, in performing any function to which the designation relates, have regard
in all cases—

3.368Z19.9.e.i

to the principles under which regulatory activities should be transparent,
accountable, proportionate, consistent and targeted only at cases in which
action is needed, and

3.368Z19.9.e.ii

to such of the matters mentioned in section 3(4) as appear to the body to be
relevant in the circumstances.

3.368Z19.10

Subject to any enactment or rule of law restricting the disclosure or use of
information by OFCOM or by a designated body—

3.368Z19.10.a

a designated body may provide information to another designated body for use
by that other body in connection with any of its functions as the appropriate
regulatory authority;

3.368Z19.10.b

a designated body may provide information to OFCOM for use by OFCOM in
connection with any of their functions under this Part;

3.368Z19.10.c

OFCOM may provide information to a designated body for use by that body in
connection with any of its functions as the appropriate regulatory authority.

3.368Z19.11

In carrying out their functions as the appropriate regulatory authority, a
designated body may carry out, commission or support (financially or
otherwise) research.

3.368Z19.12

In this section—

      “ designation ” means a designation under this section and cognate
expressions are to be construed accordingly;           “ specified ” means
specified in a designation.

########### Power to amend this Part to extend prohibition

3.368Z20

3.368Z20.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this Part for the purpose of
prohibiting persons from doing either or both of the following (so far as not
already prohibited)—

3.368Z20.1.a

placing on the internet advertisements for an identifiable less healthy food
or drink product;

3.368Z20.1.b

making arrangements for advertisements for an identifiable less healthy food
or drink product to be placed on the internet.

3.368Z20.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1) —

3.368Z20.2.a

“ placing ” includes leaving in place;

3.368Z20.2.b

“ placed ” includes continues to be placed.

3.368Z20.3

The provision which may be made by regulations under subsection  (1)  by
virtue of section 402(3)(c) includes provision repealing, revoking or amending
provision made by or under any of the following whenever passed or made—

3.368Z20.3.a

an Act;

3.368Z20.3.b

an Act of the Scottish Parliament;

3.368Z20.3.c

a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru;

3.368Z20.3.d

Northern Ireland legislation.

3.368Z20.4

Before making regulations under subsection  (1) , the Secretary of State must
consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

3.368Z20.5

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (1)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

########### Interpretation

3.368Z21

In this Part—

      “ appropriate regulatory authority ” is to be construed in accordance
with section  368Z19 ;           “ less healthy ”, in relation to a food or
drink product, has the meaning given by section  368Z14 (5)(e) .

Licensing of cosmetic procedures

Section 180

##### Introduction

1

This Schedule is about the provision that may be made by regulations under
section 180.

##### Grant of licence

2

The regulations may—

2.a

require a local authority not to grant a licence unless satisfied as to a
matter specified in the regulations;

2.b

require a local authority to have regard, in deciding whether to grant a
licence, to a matter specified in the regulations.

3

The regulations may make provision requiring a local authority not to grant a
premises licence unless the premises have been inspected in accordance with
the regulations.

##### Licence conditions

4

4.1

The regulations may make provision for the grant of a licence subject to
conditions.

4.2

Provision of the kind mentioned in sub-paragraph (1) may—

4.2.a

enable a local authority to attach conditions to a licence;

4.2.b

require a local authority to attach to a licence a condition specified in the
regulations.

##### Duration of licence etc

5

5.1

The regulations may make provision about the duration, renewal, variation,
suspension or revocation of licences.

5.2

The provision that may be made under sub-paragraph  (1)  includes provision
conferring power on a court by which a person is convicted of an offence under
the regulations to vary, suspend or revoke a licence.

##### Reviews and appeals

6

The regulations may make provision for—

6.a

the review of decisions under the regulations;

6.b

appeals against decisions under the regulations.

##### Offences

7

7.1

The regulations may create offences in relation to—

7.1.a

the breach of a prohibition imposed by virtue of section 180 (1) ;

7.1.b

the breach of a condition attached to a licence;

7.1.c

the provision of false or misleading information to a local authority in
connection with anything done under the regulations.

7.2

The regulations must provide for any such offence to be punishable on summary
conviction with a fine or a fine not exceeding an amount specified, or
determined in accordance with, the regulations.

##### Financial penalties

8

8.1

The regulations may confer power on a local authority to impose a financial
penalty in relation to—

8.1.a

the breach of a prohibition imposed by virtue of section 180(1);

8.1.b

the breach of a condition attached to a licence.

8.2

The amount of the financial penalty is to be specified in, or determined in
accordance with, the regulations.

8.3

If the regulations confer power to impose a financial penalty in respect of
conduct for which a criminal offence is created under the regulations, they
must provide that a person is not liable to such a penalty in respect of
conduct for which the person has been convicted of the offence.

8.4

If the regulations confer power to impose a financial penalty they must
include provision—

8.4.a

requiring the local authority, before imposing a financial penalty on a
person, to give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the
proposed financial penalty;

8.4.b

ensuring that the person is given an opportunity to make representations about
the proposed financial penalty;

8.4.c

requiring the local authority, after the period for making representations, to
decide whether to impose the financial penalty;

8.4.d

requiring the local authority, if it decides to impose the financial penalty,
to give the person notice in writing (a “final notice”) imposing the penalty;

8.4.e

enabling a person on whom a financial penalty is imposed to appeal to a court
or tribunal in accordance with the regulations;

8.4.f

as to the powers of the court or tribunal on such an appeal.

8.5

The provision that may be made by the regulations by virtue of sub-paragraph
(1)  includes provision—

8.5.a

enabling a notice of intent or final notice to be withdrawn or amended;

8.5.b

requiring the local authority to withdraw a final notice in circumstances
specified in the regulations;

8.5.c

for a financial penalty to be increased by an amount specified in or
determined in accordance with the regulations in the event of late payment;

8.5.d

as to how financial penalties are recoverable.

##### Enforcement

9

The regulations may confer on a local authority the function of enforcing the
regulations in its area.

##### Fees

10

The regulations may include provision for fees in relation to the carrying out
of functions of a local authority under or in connection with the regulations
(including the cost of its enforcement functions under the regulations).

##### Guidance

11

The regulations may require a local authority, in carrying out functions under
the regulations, to have regard to guidance published by the Secretary of
State.

##### Interpretation

12

12.1

In this Schedule—

“ grant ”, in relation to a licence, includes vary or renew; “ licence ” means
a personal licence or premises licence; “ personal licence ” has the meaning
given by section 180 (2) ; “ premises licence ” has the meaning given by
section 180 (2) .

12.2

Nothing in this Schedule is to be read as limiting the scope of the power to
make regulations under section 180.
